Invitation Rights and Walima Rulings
Rulings on accepting invitations and walima timing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which accepting an invitation becomes wajib and identify the time of walima according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Accepting an invitation is wajib only when it follows Sunnah; walima is after consummation.

The Hanafi school provides detailed guidelines on social obligations like accepting invitations. This lesson focuses on the first three notifications: when accepting an invitation becomes binding, the timing of the walima (wedding feast), and the difference of opinion on whether acceptance is sunnah or wajib.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditions for wajib acceptance
From notification 1, the right of invitation (haqq al-da'wah) is binding only when the invitation is according to the Sunnah. If it is not, acceptance is not obligat.
The source cites al-Ayni: ignorance excuses sin.
2
Note the dispute on the ruling
Notification 3 mentions that some scholars consider acceptance sunnah, while Fatawa Tatarkhaniyya states it is wajib. The Hanafi relied-upon position (mufta bihi) for walima is wajib when there is no hindrance.
The footnote references al-Basit and al-Shami.
3
State the time of walima
Notification 2 quotes Hafiz ibn Hajar: walima is at the time of consummation or after it.
This is the preferred view.

Source Text

تنبية - ا لم يلزمه حق الدعوة اس كو حق دعوت لازم نہیں ہے یعنی دعوت قبول کرنالازم نہیں کیونکہ دعوت کا قبول کرنا اسی وقت لازم ہوتا ہے جبکہ دعوت سنت کے طریقہ پر ہو اور بعد لحضور حضوری کی وجہ سے حق دعوت لازم ہو گیا تو اس کو عدم علم کی وجہ سے معذور شمار کیا جائے گا كذا قال العيني في البناية - تنبیہ - ولیمہ کا وقت کیا ہے؟ حافظ ابن حجر نے فتح الباری ص ۲۳۰ ج ۱ پر اقوال مختلفہ پیش کرنے کے بعد فرمایا ہے فدل على انها عند الدخول او بعده - تنبیه - ولیمہ کی دعوت ہو یا اور اگر کوئی مانع نہ ہو تو دعوت قبول کرے بعض نے قبول کرنے کو سنت اور فتاوی تا تارخانیہ میں واجب کہا ہے۔ والبسط فی الشامی ص ۲۱۱ ج ۵ - تنبیہ - اگر دستر خوان پر غیبت ہورہی ہو تو اس کا حکم بھی ملائی جیسا ہے۔ شامی ص ۲۲۱ ج ۵ - تنبیہ - جولوگ منکر فعل میں مبتلا ہیں ان پر نکیر کرنے کے لئے اجازت کے بغیر دخول جائز ہے، شامی ص ۲۲۲ ج ۵ ۔ تنبیه - ۶ اپنے نفس کی ہلاکت کو دور کرنے کے لئے کھانا فرض ہے اور ایسے ہی ستر عورت اور بدن کو گرمی اور سردی سے بچانا اور پیٹ بھر کھانا مباح ہے اور اگر اس سے بھی زیادہ کھائے جس میں فساد معدہ کا ظن ہو تو یہ حرام ہے مگر مہمان کی رعایت میں یا زندہ پر قوت کے لئے اتنا کھانا حلال ہے۔ تنبیہ کے ننگے سر کھانے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے ، شامی ص ۲۱۶ ج ۵ ۔ تنبیہ - ۸ کھانے سے پہلے جوانوں کے ہاتھ ڈھلانے سے ابتداء کی جائے گی اور کھانے سے فراغت کے بعد بوڑھوں سے ہاتھ ڈھلانے کی ابتداء کی جائے گی۔ شامی ص ۲۱۶ ج ۵ ۔ تنبیه 9 جس نے مخمصہ کی حالت میں مردار سے احتراز کیا یا روزہ رکھا اور مر گیا تو وہ گنہگار ہوگا البتہ اگر بیماری میں دوا نہیں ں اور مکی تو گندگا نہ ہوگا کیوں کہ دوا سے صحت کا یقین نہیں ہے بلکہ بغیر علاج کے بھی صحیح ہوسکتا ہے۔ مجمع الانہر ص ۵۰۵ ج ۲۔ تنبیه ۱۰ اپنے نفس کو اتنا بھوکا رکھنا کہ عبادات کی ادائیگی میں خلل واقع نہ ہو حلال ہے، حوالہ بالا۔ تنبیه بهترین پیشہ جہاد پھر تجارت، پھر زراعت پھر ضباعت ، مجمع الا نبرص ۵۰۸ ج ۲ پیشہ - تنبیہ - ۱۲ اپنی اور اپنے اہل و عیال کی ضرورت کے مطابق کمانا فرض ہے اور مقدار کفایت سے زیادہ کمانا مستحب ہے تا کہ فقرا ء کی عظیم خواری کر سکے، اور تقبل کے لئے اس سے زیادہ کمانا مباح ہے اور تفاخر اور اترانے کی غرض سے مال جمع کرنا حرام ہے، مجمع الانہرص ۵۰۸ ج ۲ - تنبیہ - ۱۳ جو شخص کمائی سے عاجز ہو تو اس پر اپنی ضرورت پوری کرنے کے لئے سوال کرنالازم ہے اور اگر اس نے قدرت کے باوجود سوال نہیں کیا اور مرگیا تو گنہگار ہوگا۔ اور اگر وہ سوال کرنے سے بھی عاجز ہو جائے تو جو اس کے حال سے واقف ہو تو اس پر فرض ہوگا کہ اس کو کھلائے ورنہ ایسے آدمی کی رہنمائی کر دے جو اس کو کھلا دے۔ مجمع الا نہ ص ۵۸ ج ۲ ۔
Notification: The right of invitation is not binding on him, meaning accepting the invitation is not obligatory, because accepting invitation is obligatory only when the invitation is in the manner of Sunnah. And after attending, due to attendance, the right of invitation became binding, so he will be considered excused due to ignorance. Thus said al-Ayni in al-Binaya. Notification: What is the time of walima? Hafiz ibn Hajar said in Fath al-Bari vol.1 p.230 after presenting various opinions: 'It indicates that it is at the time of consummation or after it.' Notification: Whether it is an invitation to walima or other, if there is no hindrance, one should accept; some said it is sunnah, and in Fatawa Tatarkhaniyya it is said wajib. And al-Basit in al-Shami vol.5 p.211. Notification: If backbiting is taking place on the dining cloth, its ruling is similar to that of [the previous]. Al-Shami vol.5 p.221. Notification: For those who are engaged in sinful acts, entering without permission to forbid evil is permissible. Al-Shami vol.5 p.222. Notification 6: To remove destruction from oneself, eating is fard, and similarly covering the private parts and protecting the body from heat and cold are fard, and eating to fill the stomach is mubah. And if one eats more than that such that there is suspicion of stomach problems, then it is haram, except in consideration of a guest or for strength to earn livelihood, in which case eating that much is halal. Notification: There is no harm in eating with uncovered head. Al-Shami vol.5 p.216. Notification 8: Before eating, one should start washing hands with the young, and after finishing eating, one should start washing hands with the elders. Al-Shami vol.5 p.216. Notification 9: Whoever avoids carrion in a state of extreme hunger, or keeps a fast, and dies, he will be sinful. However, if in illness he does not take medicine and dies, he will not be sinful because medicine does not bring certainty of health; rather, one may become healthy without treatment. Majma' al-Anhur vol.2 p.505. Notification 10: Keeping oneself so hungry that it does not impair performance of worship is halal. Same reference. Notification: The best profession is jihad, then trade, then agriculture, then craftsmanship. Majma' al-Anhur vol.2 p.508. Notification 12: Earning according to one's own and one's family's needs is fard, and earning more than the sufficiency amount is mustahabb in order to help the poor, and earning more for taraffuh (luxury) is mubah, and accumulating wealth for boasting and pride is haram. Majma' al-Anhur vol.2 p.508. Notification 13: The person who is unable to earn is obligated to ask for his needs, and if he does not ask despite being able and dies, he will be sinful. And if he is also unable to ask, then whoever knows his condition is obligated to feed him, or else to guide him to someone who will feed him. Majma' al-Anhur vol.2 p.58.
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage consists of multiple notifications (tanbeeh) covering various rulings. The first notification clarifies that the right of invitation (haqq al-da'wah) becomes binding only when the invitation follows the Sunnah; if it does not, acceptance is not obligatory. However, if one attends without knowing the nature of the gathering and later discovers sin, they are excused. The second notification discusses the time of walima (wedding feast) – according to Ibn Hajar, it is at the time of consummation or after. The third notification states that accepting an invitation is either sunnah or wajib per Fatawa Tatarkhaniyya, provided no hindrance. The fourth equates sitting where backbiting occurs to the previous ruling on sin. The fifth permits entering without permission to forbid evil. Notification 6 details the hierarchy of eating: eating to prevent harm (e.g., starvation) is fard, eating to fill the stomach is mubah, overeating that harms is haram except for hosting guests or gaining strength for livelihood. Notification 7 says eating with uncovered head is permissible. Notification 8 provides etiquette for hand washing: start with the young before eating, and with the elders after. Notification 9 warns that avoiding carrion in severe hunger or fasting to the point of death is sinful, but not taking medicine in illness is not sinful because cure is not guaranteed. Notification 10 permits moderate hunger that does not affect worship. Notification 11 lists the best professions in order: jihad, trade, agriculture, craftsmanship. Notifications 12 and 13 detail the rulings on earning: earning for basic needs is fard, extra for helping others is mustahabb, for luxury is mubah, for boasting is haram; the unable person must ask, and if unable, others must feed him.

Key Terms
حَقُّ الدَّعْوَةِ (haqq al-da'wah): The right or obligation to accept an invitation; here it becomes binding only if the invitation is according to Sunnah.
وَلِيمَة (walima): The wedding feast; its timing is after consummation according to the preferred view.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to notification 2, when is the walima held?
A) Before the wedding contract
B) At the time of consummation or after
C) One week before the wedding
D) It is not specified

Key Takeaway
Accepting a Sunnah-compliant invitation without valid excuse is wajib; walima timing is after consummation.

Eating: Obligations, Permissibility, and Prohibitions
Rulings on eating: degrees of obligation, permissibility, and prohibition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify eating into fard, mubah, and haram based on necessity and quantity, and identify the ruling on carrion in extreme hunger.

Core Idea
Eating to prevent death is fard; overeating with probable harm is haram; moderate hunger for worship is halal.

This lesson covers notifications 4-10, which address various rulings on eating: from the obligation to eat when starving to the prohibition of overeating that harms the stomach. It also includes etiquette for hand washing and the ruling on covering the head.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the three levels of eating
From notification 6: eating to prevent destruction of oneself is fard; eating to fill the stomach is mubah; eating more with probable harm is haram except for guests or for strength to earn.
The exception: extra eating is halal for a guest or for livelihood strength.
2
Explain the ruling on carrion in extreme hunger
Notification 9: If one avoids carrion in severe hunger and dies, he is sinful because preserving life is fard; but not taking medicine in illness is not sinful as cure is uncertain.
The source is Majma' al-Anhur.
3
List the etiquette of hand washing
Notification 8: Before eating, start hand washing with the young; after eating, start with the elders.
This is from al-Shami.

Commentary
This passage consists of multiple notifications (tanbeeh) covering various rulings. The first notification clarifies that the right of invitation (haqq al-da'wah) becomes binding only when the invitation follows the Sunnah; if it does not, acceptance is not obligatory. However, if one attends without knowing the nature of the gathering and later discovers sin, they are excused. The second notification discusses the time of walima (wedding feast) – according to Ibn Hajar, it is at the time of consummation or after. The third notification states that accepting an invitation is either sunnah or wajib per Fatawa Tatarkhaniyya, provided no hindrance. The fourth equates sitting where backbiting occurs to the previous ruling on sin. The fifth permits entering without permission to forbid evil. Notification 6 details the hierarchy of eating: eating to prevent harm (e.g., starvation) is fard, eating to fill the stomach is mubah, overeating that harms is haram except for hosting guests or gaining strength for livelihood. Notification 7 says eating with uncovered head is permissible. Notification 8 provides etiquette for hand washing: start with the young before eating, and with the elders after. Notification 9 warns that avoiding carrion in severe hunger or fasting to the point of death is sinful, but not taking medicine in illness is not sinful because cure is not guaranteed. Notification 10 permits moderate hunger that does not affect worship. Notification 11 lists the best professions in order: jihad, trade, agriculture, craftsmanship. Notifications 12 and 13 detail the rulings on earning: earning for basic needs is fard, extra for helping others is mustahabb, for luxury is mubah, for boasting is haram; the unable person must ask, and if unable, others must feed him.

Key Terms
مُخْمَصَة (mukhmashah): Extreme hunger where one fears death; in such a state, eating carrion becomes permissible to save life.
فَسَادُ الْمَعِدَةِ (fasad al-ma'idah): Corruption/damage of the stomach; the text uses it to define the threshold for haram overeating.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to notification 9, what is the ruling on a person who avoids carrion in extreme hunger and dies?
A) He is not sinful because carrion is haram.
B) He is sinful because preserving life is fard.
C) He is rewarded for his patience.
D) He is considered a martyr.

Key Takeaway
Eating to preserve life is fard; overeating with probable harm is haram except for guests or livelihood; carrion becomes wajib in extreme hunger.

Earning and Livelihood: Obligations and Best Professions
Rulings on earning, professions, and seeking help.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify earning into fard, mustahabb, mubah, and haram based on intention and quantity, and identify the hierarchy of best professions.

Core Idea
Earning for basic needs is fard; extra for helping others is mustahabb; for boasting is haram.

The final set of notifications (11-13) covers rulings on earning and professions. The best profession is jihad, followed by trade, agriculture, and craftsmanship. Earning for one's needs is fard; earning more to help the poor is mustahabb; and accumulating wealth for pride is haram. The lesson also addresses the obligation of the unable person to seek help.

Guided Path
1
List the best professions in order
From notification 11: the best is jihad, then trade, then agriculture, then craftsmanship.
Source: Majma' al-Anhur.
2
Classify earning by intention and amount
Notification 12: earning for basic needs is fard; earning more than sufficiency for helping others is mustahabb; earning for luxury (taraffuh) is mubah; earning for boasting and pride is haram.
The ruling varies based on intention.
3
Explain the duty to ask and the duty of others
Notification 13: if one cannot earn, it is wajib to ask for needs. If unable to ask, those aware are obligated to feed or guide.
Source: Majma' al-Anhur.

Notification: The right of invitation is not binding on him, meaning accepting the invitation is not obligatory, because accepting invitation is obligatory only when the invitation is in the manner of Sunnah. And after attending, due to attendance, the right of invitation became binding, so he will be considered excused due to ignorance. Thus said al-Ayni in al-Binaya. Notification: What is the time of walima? Hafiz ibn Hajar said in Fath al-Bari vol.1 p.230 after presenting various opinions: 'It indicates that it is at the time of consummation or after it.' Notification: Whether it is an invitation to walima or other, if there is no hindrance, one should accept; some said it is sunnah, and in Fatawa Tatarkhaniyya it is said wajib. And al-Basit in al-Shami vol.5 p.211. Notification: If backbiting is taking place on the dining cloth, its ruling is similar to that of [the previous]. Al-Shami vol.5 p.221. Notification: For those who are engaged in sinful acts, entering without permission to forbid evil is permissible. Al-Shami vol.5 p.222. Notification 6: To remove destruction from oneself, eating is fard, and similarly covering the private parts and protecting the body from heat and cold are fard, and eating to fill the stomach is mubah. And if one eats more than that such that there is suspicion of stomach problems, then it is haram, except in consideration of a guest or for strength to earn livelihood, in which case eating that much is halal. Notification: There is no harm in eating with uncovered head. Al-Shami vol.5 p.216. Notification 8: Before eating, one should start washing hands with the young, and after finishing eating, one should start washing hands with the elders. Al-Shami vol.5 p.216. Notification 9: Whoever avoids carrion in a state of extreme hunger, or keeps a fast, and dies, he will be sinful. However, if in illness he does not take medicine and dies, he will not be sinful because medicine does not bring certainty of health; rather, one may become healthy without treatment. Majma' al-Anhur vol.2 p.505. Notification 10: Keeping oneself so hungry that it does not impair performance of worship is halal. Same reference. Notification: The best profession is jihad, then trade, then agriculture, then craftsmanship. Majma' al-Anhur vol.2 p.508. Notification 12: Earning according to one's own and one's family's needs is fard, and earning more than the sufficiency amount is mustahabb in order to help the poor, and earning more for taraffuh (luxury) is mubah, and accumulating wealth for boasting and pride is haram. Majma' al-Anhur vol.2 p.508. Notification 13: The person who is unable to earn is obligated to ask for his needs, and if he does not ask despite being able and dies, he will be sinful. And if he is also unable to ask, then whoever knows his condition is obligated to feed him, or else to guide him to someone who will feed him. Majma' al-Anhur vol.2 p.58.
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage consists of multiple notifications (tanbeeh) covering various rulings. The first notification clarifies that the right of invitation (haqq al-da'wah) becomes binding only when the invitation follows the Sunnah; if it does not, acceptance is not obligatory. However, if one attends without knowing the nature of the gathering and later discovers sin, they are excused. The second notification discusses the time of walima (wedding feast) – according to Ibn Hajar, it is at the time of consummation or after. The third notification states that accepting an invitation is either sunnah or wajib per Fatawa Tatarkhaniyya, provided no hindrance. The fourth equates sitting where backbiting occurs to the previous ruling on sin. The fifth permits entering without permission to forbid evil. Notification 6 details the hierarchy of eating: eating to prevent harm (e.g., starvation) is fard, eating to fill the stomach is mubah, overeating that harms is haram except for hosting guests or gaining strength for livelihood. Notification 7 says eating with uncovered head is permissible. Notification 8 provides etiquette for hand washing: start with the young before eating, and with the elders after. Notification 9 warns that avoiding carrion in severe hunger or fasting to the point of death is sinful, but not taking medicine in illness is not sinful because cure is not guaranteed. Notification 10 permits moderate hunger that does not affect worship. Notification 11 lists the best professions in order: jihad, trade, agriculture, craftsmanship. Notifications 12 and 13 detail the rulings on earning: earning for basic needs is fard, extra for helping others is mustahabb, for luxury is mubah, for boasting is haram; the unable person must ask, and if unable, others must feed him.

Key Terms
تَجَارَة (tijarah): Trade; considered the second best profession after jihad.
مُسْتَحَب (mustahabb): Recommended; earning extra to help the poor is mustahabb.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Fard (obligatory)
B) Mustahabb (recommended)
C) Mubah (permissible)
D) Haram (forbidden)

Key Takeaway
Earning is classified by intention and amount; the best profession is jihad; helping the needy is rewarded.

The Prohibition of Silk for Men and Permissibility for Women
States the basic ruling on silk with two hadith proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wearing silk for men (haram) and women (halal) and identify the two primary hadith proofs.

Core Idea
Silk is haram for men, halal for women, as established by explicit prophetic hadith.

This lesson begins with the foundational ruling from al-Quduri's matn. The author presents a clear legal distinction: silk is forbidden for men and permitted for women. Two hadiths are cited, one general prohibition and one specific declaration from the Prophet ﷺ that silk and gold are haram for the males of his ummah and halal for its females. We will examine these proofs and their application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling from the matn
Read the opening statement: 'لا يحل للرجل لبس الحرير ويحل للنساء'. Note that the ruling is explicitly stated for men (not halal = haram) and for women (halal).
The matn does not use the word 'haram' directly but 'la yahillu', which is equivalent in this context.
2
Locate the first proof (general hadith)
The author cites a hadith: the Prophet ﷺ forbade wearing silk and dibaj, and said that only he who has no share in the Hereafter wears it. This is a strong prohibition.
This hadith is narrated by Bukhari and others; it indicates the severity of wearing silk for men.
3
Locate the second proof (specific hadith from Ali)
The second hadith is more explicit: the Prophet ﷺ held silk and gold and said 'These two are haram for the males of my ummah, halal for their females.' This directly distinguishes by gender.
This hadith is a clear dalil for the ruling.
4
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit words 'haram' and 'halal' are used. In Hanafi usul, such explicit texts are qat'i al-dalalah. The ruling is derived directly from the text without need for further interpretation.
The hadith is ahad but its meaning is clear and thus binding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مردوں اور عورتوں کیلئے ریشم پہنے کا حکم فصل في اللبس قال لا يحل للرجل لبس الحرير ويحل للنساء لان النبي عليه السلام نهى عن لبس الحرير والديباج وقال انما يلبسه من الاخلاق له في الآخرة والماحل للنساء بحديث آخر وهو مارواه عدة من الصحابة منهم على رضى الله عنه ان النبي خرج و باحدى يديه جرير وبالأخرى ذهب وقال هذان ـخـر مـان على ذكورا متى حلال لاناثهم ويروى حل لاناتهم ترجمہ یہ فصل ہے پہننے کے بیان میں قدوری نے فرمایا کہ مردوں کے لئے ریشم پہننا حلال نہیں اور عورتوں کے لئے حلال ہے اس لئے کہ نبی علیہ السلام نے ریشم اور دیبا کے پہنے سے منع فرمایا ہے اور فرمایا کہ اس کو وہ پہنتا ہے جس کا آخرت میں کوئی حصہ نہ ہو اور دوسری حدیث کی وجہ سے عورتوں کے لئے حلال ہے اور وہ حدیث ہے جس کو بہت سے صحابہ نے روایت کیا ہے انہیں میں سے علی ہیں کہ نبی علیہ السلام باہر تشریف لائے اور آپ کے ایک ہاتھ میں ریشم اور دوسرے ہاتھ میں سونا تھا اور فرمایا کہ یہ دونوں امت کے مردوں پر حرام ہیں ان کی عورتوں کے لئے حلال ہیں اور ایک روایت میں (حلال کے بجائے ) حل لانا شہم ہے۔ تشریح اس فصل کے اندر مصنف لباس کے بارے میں گفتگو فرمائیں گے جس کا خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ مردوں کے لئے ریشم پہنا جائز نہیں ہے البتہ عورتوں کے لئے جائز ہے ان احادیث کی وجہ سے جو مذکور ہیں۔ معفو قلیل مقدار کی تعیین الا ان القليل عفو وهو مقدار ثلثة اصابع او اربع كالاعلام والمكفوف بالحرير لماروى انه عليه السلام نهى عن لبس الحرير الا موضع اصبعين اوثلث او اربع اراد الاعلام وعنه عليه السلام انه كان يلبس جبة مكفوفة بالحرير ترجمہ عمر قلیل معاف ہے اور یہ تین یا چار انگلیوں کی مقدار ہے جیسے بوٹے یا ریشم کا جھالر بوجہ اس کے کہ نبی علیہ السلام نے منع فرمایا ہے ریشم کے پہنے سے مگر دو یا تین یا چار انگلیوں کی مقدار نبی علیہ السلام نے بوٹوں کا ارادہ فرمایا اور آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے بارے میں منقول ہے کہ آپ ایسا جبہ پہنتے تھے جس کا سنجاف (جھالر ) ریشم کا ہوتا۔
Ruling on wearing silk for men and women. Section on clothing. He (al-Quduri) said: It is not permissible for a man to wear silk, and it is permissible for women, because the Prophet ﷺ forbade wearing silk and brocade (dibaj), and said: 'Only he wears it who has no share in the Hereafter.' And it is permissible for women due to another hadith, which is narrated by several Companions, among them Ali رضی الله عنه, that the Prophet ﷺ came out with silk in one hand and gold in the other and said: 'These two are forbidden for the males of my ummah and permissible for their females.' In one narration it is 'حلال لاناثهم' (permissible for their females). Translation: This is a section on clothing. Imam Quduri stated: Wearing silk is not halal for men and is halal for women, because the Prophet ﷺ forbade wearing silk and brocade, and said that the one who wears it has no share in the Hereafter, and due to another hadith it is halal for women—the hadith narrated by many Companions, among them Ali, that the Prophet ﷺ came out with silk in one hand and gold in the other and said: 'These two are forbidden for the males of my ummah and permissible for their females' and in one narration 'حلال لاناثهم' is reported. Explanation: In this section, the author will discuss clothing, the summary being that wearing silk is not permissible for men but is permissible for women, due to the mentioned hadiths. Determination of the small excusable amount: However, a small amount is excused, and it is the size of three or four fingers, such as patches (a'lam) or silk trimming (makfuf). Because it is narrated that the Prophet ﷺ forbade wearing silk except for the place of two, three, or four fingers—he intended the patches (a'lam). And it is narrated from him ﷺ that he wore a cloak with silk trimming. Translation: But a small amount is forgiven, and it is the quantity of three or four fingers, like patches or silk trimming, because the Prophet ﷺ forbade wearing silk except for the area of two or three or four fingers—he intended the patches. And it is narrated from him ﷺ that he wore a cloak whose trimming (sinjaf/hem) was silk.
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on wearing silk, a clear topic in Hanafi fiqh. The matn from al-Quduri states: Silk is not halal for men but is halal for women. Two hadiths are cited: first, a general prohibition that one who wears silk has no share in the Hereafter (implying it is a major sin); second, a specific hadith from Ali that silk and gold are forbidden for males and permissible for females. The commentary (tashreeh) summarizes that men are prohibited, women permitted. The second part addresses the exception for a small amount (qalil). According to the author, a small amount up to three or four fingers' width is excused (ma'fu), such as patches (a'lam) or silk trimming (makfuf/ sinjaf). The proof is a hadith that the Prophet ﷺ forbade wearing silk except for two, three, or four fingers (intended for decorative patches) and the practice of the Prophet ﷺ himself wearing a cloak with silk trimming. This shows that a small amount for decoration is permissible for men.

Key Terms
حَرِير (harir): Silk fabric, specifically the cloth woven from silkworm threads.
مَعْفُوّ (ma'fu): Excused or forgiven; the small amount of silk that is permissible for men despite the general prohibition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which hadith is cited as the primary evidence that silk is haram for men and halal for women?
A) 'Only he who has no share in the Hereafter wears silk'
B) 'These two are haram for the males of my ummah and halal for their females'
C) 'Gold and silk are permissible for my ummah'
D) 'Wear silk, but do not wear it in the mosque'

Key Takeaway
Wearing silk is haram for men and halal for women, based on explicit prophetic hadith, with an exception for a small decorative amount.

The Excusable Small Amount of Silk for Men
Specifies the excusable amount of silk for men and its evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the amount of silk that is excused for men (three or four fingers) and state the evidence from the Prophet's practice.

Core Idea
A small amount of silk (up to 3-4 fingers' width) is excused for men based on prophetic practice.

While the general rule prohibits silk for men, an exception exists for a small decorative amount. This lesson details that exception: patches (a'lam) and silk trimmings (makfuf) up to the width of three or four fingers are excused. The evidence comes from a hadith that the Prophet ﷺ forbade wearing silk except for two, three, or four fingers (intended for patches), and from his own practice of wearing a cloak with silk trimming.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule and the exception
Recall that silk is haram for men. The text then says 'الا ان القليل عفو' (but a small amount is excused). This is the exception.
The exception applies only to decorative elements, not to whole garments.
2
Determine the threshold quantity
The author specifies the amount as 'ثلثة اصابع او اربع' (three or four fingers). This is the width considered excused.
There is a slight variation between three and four fingers; both are mentioned in hadith.
3
Examine the proof from hadith
The proof is that the Prophet ﷺ forbade wearing silk except for the area of two, three, or four fingers, which he intended for patches (a'lam). Additionally, he himself wore a cloak with silk trimming.
The Prophet's own action (fi'l) is also a source of law.

مردوں اور عورتوں کیلئے ریشم پہنے کا حکم فصل في اللبس قال لا يحل للرجل لبس الحرير ويحل للنساء لان النبي عليه السلام نهى عن لبس الحرير والديباج وقال انما يلبسه من الاخلاق له في الآخرة والماحل للنساء بحديث آخر وهو مارواه عدة من الصحابة منهم على رضى الله عنه ان النبي خرج و باحدى يديه جرير وبالأخرى ذهب وقال هذان ـخـر مـان على ذكورا متى حلال لاناثهم ويروى حل لاناتهم ترجمہ یہ فصل ہے پہننے کے بیان میں قدوری نے فرمایا کہ مردوں کے لئے ریشم پہننا حلال نہیں اور عورتوں کے لئے حلال ہے اس لئے کہ نبی علیہ السلام نے ریشم اور دیبا کے پہنے سے منع فرمایا ہے اور فرمایا کہ اس کو وہ پہنتا ہے جس کا آخرت میں کوئی حصہ نہ ہو اور دوسری حدیث کی وجہ سے عورتوں کے لئے حلال ہے اور وہ حدیث ہے جس کو بہت سے صحابہ نے روایت کیا ہے انہیں میں سے علی ہیں کہ نبی علیہ السلام باہر تشریف لائے اور آپ کے ایک ہاتھ میں ریشم اور دوسرے ہاتھ میں سونا تھا اور فرمایا کہ یہ دونوں امت کے مردوں پر حرام ہیں ان کی عورتوں کے لئے حلال ہیں اور ایک روایت میں (حلال کے بجائے ) حل لانا شہم ہے۔ تشریح اس فصل کے اندر مصنف لباس کے بارے میں گفتگو فرمائیں گے جس کا خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ مردوں کے لئے ریشم پہنا جائز نہیں ہے البتہ عورتوں کے لئے جائز ہے ان احادیث کی وجہ سے جو مذکور ہیں۔ معفو قلیل مقدار کی تعیین الا ان القليل عفو وهو مقدار ثلثة اصابع او اربع كالاعلام والمكفوف بالحرير لماروى انه عليه السلام نهى عن لبس الحرير الا موضع اصبعين اوثلث او اربع اراد الاعلام وعنه عليه السلام انه كان يلبس جبة مكفوفة بالحرير ترجمہ عمر قلیل معاف ہے اور یہ تین یا چار انگلیوں کی مقدار ہے جیسے بوٹے یا ریشم کا جھالر بوجہ اس کے کہ نبی علیہ السلام نے منع فرمایا ہے ریشم کے پہنے سے مگر دو یا تین یا چار انگلیوں کی مقدار نبی علیہ السلام نے بوٹوں کا ارادہ فرمایا اور آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے بارے میں منقول ہے کہ آپ ایسا جبہ پہنتے تھے جس کا سنجاف (جھالر ) ریشم کا ہوتا۔
Ruling on wearing silk for men and women. Section on clothing. He (al-Quduri) said: It is not permissible for a man to wear silk, and it is permissible for women, because the Prophet ﷺ forbade wearing silk and brocade (dibaj), and said: 'Only he wears it who has no share in the Hereafter.' And it is permissible for women due to another hadith, which is narrated by several Companions, among them Ali رضی الله عنه, that the Prophet ﷺ came out with silk in one hand and gold in the other and said: 'These two are forbidden for the males of my ummah and permissible for their females.' In one narration it is 'حلال لاناثهم' (permissible for their females). Translation: This is a section on clothing. Imam Quduri stated: Wearing silk is not halal for men and is halal for women, because the Prophet ﷺ forbade wearing silk and brocade, and said that the one who wears it has no share in the Hereafter, and due to another hadith it is halal for women—the hadith narrated by many Companions, among them Ali, that the Prophet ﷺ came out with silk in one hand and gold in the other and said: 'These two are forbidden for the males of my ummah and permissible for their females' and in one narration 'حلال لاناثهم' is reported. Explanation: In this section, the author will discuss clothing, the summary being that wearing silk is not permissible for men but is permissible for women, due to the mentioned hadiths. Determination of the small excusable amount: However, a small amount is excused, and it is the size of three or four fingers, such as patches (a'lam) or silk trimming (makfuf). Because it is narrated that the Prophet ﷺ forbade wearing silk except for the place of two, three, or four fingers—he intended the patches (a'lam). And it is narrated from him ﷺ that he wore a cloak with silk trimming. Translation: But a small amount is forgiven, and it is the quantity of three or four fingers, like patches or silk trimming, because the Prophet ﷺ forbade wearing silk except for the area of two or three or four fingers—he intended the patches. And it is narrated from him ﷺ that he wore a cloak whose trimming (sinjaf/hem) was silk.
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on wearing silk, a clear topic in Hanafi fiqh. The matn from al-Quduri states: Silk is not halal for men but is halal for women. Two hadiths are cited: first, a general prohibition that one who wears silk has no share in the Hereafter (implying it is a major sin); second, a specific hadith from Ali that silk and gold are forbidden for males and permissible for females. The commentary (tashreeh) summarizes that men are prohibited, women permitted. The second part addresses the exception for a small amount (qalil). According to the author, a small amount up to three or four fingers' width is excused (ma'fu), such as patches (a'lam) or silk trimming (makfuf/ sinjaf). The proof is a hadith that the Prophet ﷺ forbade wearing silk except for two, three, or four fingers (intended for decorative patches) and the practice of the Prophet ﷺ himself wearing a cloak with silk trimming. This shows that a small amount for decoration is permissible for men.

Key Terms
حَرِير (harir): Silk fabric.
مَعْفُوّ (ma'fu): Excused; the small amount of silk that is permissible for men.
أَعْلَام (a'lam): Patches; decorative silk pieces sewn onto garment.
مَكْفُوف (makfuf): Silk trimming; a border of silk around the edges of a garment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the maximum amount of silk that is excused for a man to wear as decoration?
A) Two or three fingers
B) Three or four fingers
C) One hand span
D) Any amount is haram

Key Takeaway
A small silk trim or patch up to three or four fingers' width is excused for men, based on prophetic exception and practice.

The Graded Rulings of Earning Based on Intention
Ruling on the graded legal status of earning based on intention and need

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four levels of ruling for earning wealth according to the Hanafi school and identify the decisive factor (intention and need) that determines each level.

Core Idea
Earning for basic needs is fard; earning for charity is mustahabb; earning for accumulation is mubah; earning for pride is haram.

This passage from Majma' al-Anhur presents a concise ethical-legal framework for understanding the ruling on earning wealth. Unlike a simple binary of halal/haram, the Hanafi school recognizes a spectrum based on intention and need. This hierarchy illustrates how the same act—earning—can be obligatory, recommended, merely permitted, or forbidden depending on why and for whom one earns.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the four rulings
The act under consideration is earning wealth (kamaana). The text gives four rulings: fard, mustahabb, mubah, and haram. Each is tied to a specific intention or condition.
Memorize the four terms: fard, mustahabb, mubah, haram.
2
Map each ruling to its condition
Fard: earning basic sufficiency for self and family. Mustahabb: earning extra to help the poor. Mubah: earning even more for mere increase (without pride). Haram: accumulating wealth for pride and arrogance.
The condition is both the amount earned and the underlying intention.
3
Understand the underlying principle
The ruling of a permissible act (earning) changes based on niyyah (intention) and need. This is a key Hanafi moral-legal concept: intention transforms the hukm.
This is consistent with the hadith: 'Actions are by intentions.'
4
Memorize the hierarchy
Commit the four levels in order of obligation: fard (obligatory), mustahabb (recommended), mubah (permissible), haram (forbidden). Recognize that the same physical action can have different rulings.
Use the hierarchy to analyze real-world earning scenarios.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبیہ - ۱۲ اپنی اور اپنے اہل و عیال کی ضرورت کے مطابق کمانا فرض ہے اور مقدار کفایت سے زیادہ کمانا مستحب ہے تا کہ فقرا ء کی عظیم خواری کر سکے، اور تقبل کے لئے اس سے زیادہ کمانا مباح ہے اور تفاخر اور اترانے کی غرض سے مال جمع کرنا حرام ہے، مجمع الانہرص ۵۰۸ ج ۲
Admonition 12: Earning according to one's own and one's family's need is obligatory (fard). Earning more than the amount of sufficiency is recommended (mustahabb) so that one can greatly help the poor. Earning even more than that for the sake of acceptance [?] is permissible (mubah). Accumulating wealth for the purpose of pride and arrogance is forbidden (haram). (Majma' al-Anhur, vol. 2, p. 508)
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the late Hanafi work Majma' al-Anhur. It provides a graded hierarchy of rulings for earning wealth based on intention and need. The lowest level (fard) is earning to meet basic needs for oneself and dependents. The mid level (mustahabb) is earning extra to give charity, and (mubah) simply to increase wealth without pride. The highest level of aversion (haram) is earning for pride and showing off. This classification is typical of Hanafi ethical-legal gradations.

Key Terms
كتاب الكراهية (Kitab al-Karahiyah): Book of Disliked Acts; a section of positive law covering acts that are disliked or prohibited in a less severe sense.
تنبیہ (tanbih): An admonition or note of caution; used in legal texts to draw attention to an important ruling or principle.
فرض (fard): An obligatory act established by definitive evidence (qat'i); omission is sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following intentions makes earning wealth haram?
A) Earning to meet family needs
B) Earning extra to give charity
C) Earning for pride and arrogance
D) Earning for mere increase

Key Takeaway
The ruling on earning wealth is not fixed; it ranges from fard to haram depending on one's intention and need, as outlined in this Hanafi hierarchy.

Ruling on Begging When Unable to Earn
Ruling on the obligation to beg for one unable to earn and the duty of others to feed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on begging for a person unable to earn and identify the obligations of others aware of his condition.

Core Idea
When unable to earn, begging becomes obligatory; neglect leads to sin.

This passage from Majma' al-Anhur clarifies the Hanafi position on begging. While begging is generally prohibited, it transforms into a duty when one cannot earn a living. The text also addresses the responsibility of those who know of such a person.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and his inability
The ruling applies to a person who is 'ajiz' (unable to earn) due to disability or other reasons.
Inability is the key condition.
2
Determine the ruling on the unable person
Begging (suwal) becomes wajib for him to fulfill his need.
This overrides the general prohibition of begging.
3
Note the consequence if he does not ask despite ability
If he can ask but does not, and dies, he will be sinful.
Sin is incurred due to neglect of a wajib.
4
Identify the second case: unable to ask
If the person is also unable to ask (e.g., mute or physically disabled), then the duty shifts.
Inability to ask is a further condition.
5
Determine the obligation on others
The one aware of his condition is obligated (fard) to feed him, or if unable, to guide him to someone who can.
This is a communal obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبیہ - ۱۳ جو شخص کمائی سے عاجز ہو تو اس پر اپنی ضرورت پوری کرنے کے لئے سوال کرنالازم ہے اور اگر اس نے قدرت کے باوجود سوال نہیں کیا اور مرگیا تو گنہگار ہوگا۔ اور اگر وہ سوال کرنے سے بھی عاجز ہو جائے تو جو اس کے حال سے واقف ہو تو اس پر فرض ہوگا کہ اس کو کھلائے ورنہ ایسے آدمی کی رہنمائی کر دے جو اس کو کھلا دے۔ مجمع الا نہ ص ۵۸ ج ۲
Admonition 13: A person who is unable to earn, it is necessary for him to ask (beg) to fulfill his need. If he, despite being able [to ask], does not ask and dies, he will be sinful. And if he is also unable to ask [due to disability], then the one who is aware of his condition is obligated (fard) to feed him; otherwise, he should guide such a person to someone who will feed him. (Majma' al-Anhur, p. 58, vol. 2)
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from Majma' al-Anhur establishing the obligation to beg when one cannot earn, and the communal obligation to feed those unable to beg. The ruling highlights the Hanafi view that begging becomes a duty in cases of necessity, reversing the general prohibition of begging. The ruling also imposes a fard obligation on those aware of the needy person's condition to provide food or guide them to a source.

Key Terms
عاجز (ajiz): Incapable of earning; unable to provide for oneself through work.
سوال (suwal): Begging or asking for financial help from others.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person is able to ask (beg) but does not do so and dies of hunger, what is their status?
A) They are not sinful
B) They are sinful
C) It is permissible to not ask
D) It is recommended to ask

Key Takeaway
When unable to earn, begging becomes a necessary duty; neglecting it brings sin, and the community must support those unable to ask.

Ruling on Using a Silk Pillow and Sleeping on It
Intra-Hanafi dispute on silk pillow use and the tarjih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on using a silk pillow, identify the proofs from each side, and explain why the mufta bihi is makruh.

Core Idea
The Sahibayn's view (makruh) is the mufta bihi, not Abu Hanifa's permissibility.

This lesson examines a classical intra-Hanafi dispute over using silk pillows. While Imam Abu Hanifa considered it permissible based on prophetic practice and analogy to embroidery, his two foremost students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, held it to be makruh due to general prohibitions on silk and imitation of tyrants. Understanding this ikhtilaf and the eventual tarjih helps you appreciate the evolution of Hanafi fatwa and the weight given to the Sahibayn's opinions.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi positions
Identify the ruling from Abu Hanifa (la ba'sa/permissible) and from the Sahibayn (makruh/disliked). Note that Abu Yusuf's exact view has some transmission variations.
In al-Jami' al-Saghir, only Muhammad's view is recorded; al-Quduri includes Abu Yusuf with Muhammad.
2
Analyze the proofs for each side
The Sahibayn rely on general prohibitions against silk and the hadith of 'Umar warning against imitating non-Arabs. Abu Hanifa cites the Prophet sitting on a silk cushion and Ibn 'Abbas having a silk cushion, arguing that a small amount (qalil) is permissible by analogy to embroidery.
The commonality (jami') is that both are a 'sample' (namudhaj) of Paradise's silk.
3
Examine the qiyas reasoning
Abu Hanifa uses qiyas: clothing with small silk embroidery is permissible, so using a small silk pillow is also permissible. The illa is the small amount serving as a sample.
The commentary addresses a potential objection that wearing and using are different; the common sample nature resolves it.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
Most mashayikh (as per Majma' al-Anhur and Sikk al-Anhar) prefer the Sahibayn's view. Thus, the operative ruling for fatwa is makruh tanzihi.
The authority weight is zahir riwayah for both views, but later tarjih favors the Sahibayn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ولا باس بتوسده و النوم عليه عند ابي حنيفة وقالا يكره وفى الجامع الصغير ذكر قول محمد وحده ولم يذكر قول ابى يوسف وانما ذكره القدورى وغيره من المشايخ وكذا الاختلاف في ستر الحرير وتعليقه على الابواب لهما العمومات ولانه من زى الاكاسرة والجبابرة والتشبه بهم حرام وقال عمر
اياكم وزى الاعاجم
ترجمه قدوری نے فرمایا اور کوئی حرج نہیں ریشم کے تکیہ لگانے میں اور اس پر سونے میں ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ مکروہ ہے اور جامع صغیر میں تنہا محمد کا قول مذکور ہے اور ابو یوسف کا قول مذکور نہیں ہے اور اس کو قدوری اور مشائخ میں سے ان کے غیر نے ذکر کیا ہے اور ایسے ہی اختلاف ہے ریشم کے پردے میں اور اس کو دروازے پر لٹکانے میں، صاحبین کی دلیل عمومات ہیں اور اس لئے کہ یہ شاہان نجم اور متکبرین کا طریقہ ہے اور ان کے ساتھ تشبہ حرام ہے اور فرمایا عمر نے اپنے کو بچاؤ عجمیوں کے حلیہ سے۔ تشریح امام صاحب کے نزدیک ریشم کا تکیہ لگانے میں اورایسے تکیہ پر سونے میں کوئی حرج نہیں اور اسی طرح اس کو دیوار پر ڈالنے میں کوئی حرج نہیں اور اسی طرح دروازہ پر ڈالنے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔
امام محمد نے اس کو مکر وہ کہا ہے۔ امام ابو یوسف کیا فرماتے ہیں تو امام قدوری وغیرہ نے ان کو امام محمد کے ساتھ بیان کیا ہے۔ اور جامع صغیر میں امام ابو یوسف کا قول مذکور نہیں ہے۔ بہر حال بقول قدوری صاحبین کی دلیل مذکورہ احادیث کا عموم ہے ( کما ہو ظاہر وفیہ بحث في الثائج) اور اس لئے بھی کہ یہ شاہان محجم اور متکبرین کا طریقہ ہے اور اس کے ساتھ تشبہ حرام ہے اور حضرت عمر فاروق کا فرمان ہے کہ عجمیوں کا حلیہ اختیار کرنے سے اپنے کو بچاؤ۔ تنبیہ کا سرہ، کسری کی جمع ہے جو عجم کے ملک فارس کے بادشاہ کو کہا جاتا ہے اور جبابرہ، جبار کی جمع ہے بمعنی متکبر ۔
امام صاحب کی دلیل
وله ماروى انه عليه السلام جلس على مرافقة حرير وقد كان على بساط عبد الله بن عباس مرفقة حرير وكان القليل من الملبوس مباح كالا علام فكذا القليل من اللبس والاستعمال والجامع كونه نموذجا
على ما عرف
ترجمہ اور ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل وہ ہے جو مروی ہے کہ نبی علیہ السلام ریشم کے تکیہ پر بیٹھے اور اس لئے کہ ملبوس میں سے قلیل مباح ہے جیسے بوٹے پس ایسے ہی قلیل پہننا اور استعمال اور جامع اس کا نمونہ ہونا ہے اس تفصیل کے مطابق جو جانی پہچانی ہے۔ تشریح امام صاحب کی جانب سے دو حدیث پیش کی گئی ہیں پہلی حدیث نہیں ملتی، بہر حال قلیل کا استعمال جائز معلوم ہوا خواہ ملبوس بنا کر ہو جیسے بوٹوں یا لبس و استعمال ہو جیسے تکیہ اور بچھانے میں تاکہ نمونہ ہو جائے۔ یعنی جنت میں ریشمی لباس ملے گا تو قلیل اس لئے جائز ہے تا کہ اس کی لذت سے آشنا ہو کر آخرت کی کامیابی کی تحصیل میں لگار ہے۔
تو یہاں سوال تھا کہ قلیل ملبوس تو جائز ہے مگر قلیل لبس و استعمال کیوں جائز ہے اور ثانی کو اول پر کیسے قیاس کر لیا گیا جبکہ علت جامعہ موجود نہیں ہے؟ تو اس کا جواب دیا کہ علت جامعہ موجود ہے اور وہ ان دونوں کا نمونہ ہونا ہے۔ تنبیه - صاحب مجمع اور صاحب منظومہ اور قدوری نے امام ابو یوسف کو امام محمد کے ساتھ بیان کیا ہے اور جامع صغیر میں امام صاحب اور محمد کے درمیان اختلاف مذکور ہے۔ اور فقیہ ابواللیث نے ذکر کیا ہے کہ ابو یوسف امام صاحب کے ساتھ ہیں۔ مجمع الا نہ ص ۵۱۴ ج ۲۔ تنبیه ۲ اکثر مشائخ نے صاحبین کے قول کو اختیار کیا ہے اور یہی صحیح ہے سکب الانہرص ۴۵۷ ج ۲
He said: There is no harm in using it as a pillow and sleeping on it according to Abu Hanifa, but they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said it is disliked. In al-Jami' al-Saghir, only Muhammad's statement is mentioned, not Abu Yusuf's; al-Quduri and other mashayikh mentioned it. Similarly, there is disagreement about silk curtains and hanging them on doors. Their (Sahibayn's) proof is the generalities (of prohibitions), and because it is the dress of kings and tyrants, and imitating them is haram. 'Umar said: Beware of the dress of the non-Arabs. Translation: ... Commentary: ... Imam's proof: It is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) sat on a silk cushion, and on the carpet of Ibn 'Abbas there was a silk cushion. The small amount of clothing is permissible like embroidery, so likewise the small amount of wearing and using, and the commonality is its being a sample, as known. Translation: ... Commentary: ... Question: ... Answer: ... Note: ... Note 2: Most mashayikh have chosen the view of the Sahibayn, and this is correct.
Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the use of silk pillows and sleeping on them. Imam Abu Hanifa holds it permissible (la ba'sa), while Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad (the Sahibayn) consider it makruh (disliked). The dispute extends to hanging silk curtains. The Sahibayn rely on general prohibitions against silk for men and the fact that it is the dress of arrogant kings, and imitating them is haram, citing a hadith of 'Umar. Abu Hanifa's evidence includes the Prophet sitting on a silk cushion and the blanket of Ibn 'Abbas having a silk cushion, arguing that a small amount (qalil) is permissible by analogy to permissible small silk detailing on clothing. The commentary resolves a potential qiyas objection by noting that commonality (the sample nature) justifies it. Note 2 states that most later mashayikh prefer the Sahibayn's view, making it the mufta bihi.

Key Terms
توسد (tawassud): Using something as a pillow to rest the head
قليل (qalil): Small amount of silk that is permissible; defined as three or four fingers in width

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) ruling in the Hanafi school regarding a man using a silk pillow?
A) Permissible (mubah) without any dislike
B) Disliked (makruh tanzihi)
C) Prohibited (haram)
D) Recommended (mustahabb)

Key Takeaway
For fatwa purposes, the Sahibayn's view that using a silk pillow is makruh is relied upon, not Abu Hanifa's permissibility.

Permissibility of a Small Amount of Silk for Men
Commentary on Abu Hanifa's proof for small silk usage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on using a small amount of silk (qalil) for men, explain the proof from the Prophet's action, and apply the analogy (qiyas) to other uses.

Core Idea
A small amount of silk is permissible as a sample of Paradise, proven by the Prophet's action.

In this passage, the commentator explains Abu Hanifa's proof for allowing men to use a small amount of silk, such as a badge or cushion. The ruling is based on a hadith of the Prophet sitting on a silk cushion and an analogy to small silk badges. The commentary also addresses an objection about the common cause (illa) and notes later scholarly preference among the Sahibayn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its basis
First, note that the ruling under discussion is the permissibility of a small amount of silk (qalil) for men. Abu Hanifa's proof is derived from a hadith and analogy with badges.
2
Trace the dalil (proof)
Abu Hanifa cites a hadith: the Prophet (peace be upon him) sat on a silk cushion. This action indicates permissibility of limited use. The hadith is of zanni thubut and dalala, as it is not mutawatir.
The passage notes the first hadith is not found, but the second is used.
3
Analyze the qiyas (analogy)
The commentator explains that small silk clothing (like a badge) is permissible. The question is why small silk for other uses (cushion) is also permissible. The answer: the common cause (jami') is that both serve as a sample (numoonah) of Paradise.
The illa is 'being a sample', which is a clear cause (jaliyyah).
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
There is disagreement: some reports place Abu Yusuf with Abu Hanifa, others with Muhammad. The passage cites sources like Majma' al-Nah? and Jami' al-Saghir.
This ikhtilaf affects the authority weight but both sides allow small amounts.
5
Determine the mufta bihi (operative view)
The passage states that most later mashayikh (e.g., author of Siraj al-Anhar) prefer the view of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). This is the relied-upon position for fatwa.
Thus the operative ruling is that a small amount is permissible.

Source Text

According to what is known. Book of Disliked Acts. Translation: And Abu Hanifa's proof is what is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) sat on a silk cushion, and because among clothing, a small amount is permissible like a badge, so similarly wearing a small amount and using it, and the common factor is that it is a sample, according to the detail that is known. Explanation: Imam (Abu Hanifa) presented two hadiths; the first hadith is not found. Nevertheless, using a small amount is deemed permissible, whether made into clothing like badges or worn and used like a cushion and spread, so that it becomes a sample. That is, in Paradise one will get silk garments, so a small amount is permissible to become acquainted with its pleasure and thus strive for the success of the Hereafter. So there was a question: a small amount of clothing is permissible, but why is a small amount of wearing and using permissible, and how is the second analogized to the first when there is no common cause? The answer was given that the common cause exists, and it is that both are a sample. Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a ruling regarding small amounts of silk for men. It opens by presenting Abu Hanifa's proof: a hadith that the Prophet sat on a silk cushion. This indicates that small amounts of silk used as a sample of Paradise are permissible. The commentary then addresses an objection: if small silk clothing (like a badge) is permissible, why is small silk used as a cushion or spread also permissible? The answer is that both serve as a sample, providing the common cause for analogy. The passage concludes with two notes: first, regarding the positions of Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad in relation to Abu Hanifa on this issue; second, that most later scholars prefer the view of the two companions (Sahibayn), which is considered correct.

Key Terms
قلیل (qalil): A small amount of silk, specifically an amount that serves as a sample or decoration, not as full clothing.
ملبوس (malbus): Clothing or an item worn on the body.
نمونہ (numoonah): A sample or token; silk used as a reminder of Paradise.

A) Both involve silk
B) Both are used in war
C) Both serve as a sample (numoonah) of Paradise
D) Both are inherited from the Prophet

Key Takeaway
A small amount of silk is permissible for men as a reminder of Paradise, based on the Prophet's action and analogy with badges.

Ruling on Silk Garments: Warp vs Weft
Clarifies ruling on mixed silk by distinguishing warp vs weft

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for garments with silk warp vs silk weft and explain the legal reasoning based on the Companions' practice.

Core Idea
The prohibition of silk attaches to the weft, not the warp; garments with silk warp are permissible.

This lesson clarifies a common confusion about mixed silk garments. Is a garment with silk threads always prohibited? The Hanafi school distinguishes between the warp (lengthwise threads) and the weft (crosswise threads), relying on the practice of the Companions who wore khazz, a fabric with a silk warp. By the end, you will understand why the weft determines the ruling and how a difference of opinion arises for the reverse case.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage discusses two cases: (1) silk warp + non-silk weft, and (2) non-silk warp + silk weft. Note the ruling for each.
2
State the ruling for each case
For case 1: always permissible (in war and peace). For case 2: permissible only in war (according to Sahibayn) and disliked otherwise (Abu Hanifa).
The second case has an intra-Hanafi dispute.
3
Understand the legal reason
The garment is defined by its weft (luhma) because weaving is based on the weft. Hence the prohibition of silk applies to the weft, not the warp.
This is the core legal principle (ta'lil).
4
Examine the proof (dalil)
Imam Muhammad cites the practice of the Companions who wore khazz, a fabric with a silk warp. This demonstrates that warp-silk is permissible.
The proof is a Sunnah of the Companions (thubut: zanni, dalala: zanni).
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
For the reverse case (silk weft), Abu Hanifa holds it makruh in all situations, while the Sahibayn allow it in war. The mufta bihi follows the Sahibayn.
The difference is based on the weight given to war necessity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبیه - ۳ جس کا تانا ریشم کا اور بانا سوت اون وغیرہ کا ہو تو اس کا استعمال جائز ہے جنگ میں بھی اور ویسے بھی ، اور اگر بانا ریشم کا ہو اور تا ناسوت وغیرہ کا ہو تو جنگ میں اس کا پہننا جائز ہے اور اس کے غیر میں مکروہ ہے۔ کیوں کہ کپڑا بانے کی وجہ سے کپڑا بنتا ہے اور بنائی کا مدار بانے پر لہذا اس کو اصل قرار دیا گیا ہے (وسیاتی )
ایسا کپڑا جس کا تانا ریشم اور بانا غیر ریشم ہو تو کیا حکم ہے
قال ولاباس بلبس ماسداه حریر ولحمته غير حرير كالقطن والخزفى الحرب وغيره لأن الصحابة كانو يلبسون الخزو الخز مسدى بالحرير ولان الثوب انما يصير ثوبا بالنسج والنسج باللحمة فكانت هي المعتبرة دون السدى
ترجمہ محمد نے جامع صغیر میں فرمایا اور کوئی حرج نہیں ایسے کپڑے کو پہنچنے میں جس کا تانا یم اور اس کا با نا غیر ریشم ہو جیسے روئی اور خز جنگ میں اور اس کے غیر میں اس لئے کہ صحابہ تھر پہننے تھے اور خنز کا تانا ریشم کا ہوتا تھا اس لئے کہ کپڑا بنائی کی وجہ سے کپڑا ہوتا ہے اور بنائی جانے کی وجہ سے ہوتی ہے اور بان ہی معتبر ہو گا نہ کہ تا نا۔ تشریح مسئلہ تو واضح ہے اس کو ہم ابھی ذکر کر چکے ہیں۔ جو ایک دریائی جانور کے بالوں سے بنایا ہوا کپڑا مسدہی ، سداء سے اسم مفعول کا صیغہ ہے، بمعنی تانا تننا سدى تانا لحمة بانا۔
Note 3: One whose warp is silk and weft is cotton, wool etc., its use is permissible in war and otherwise. And if weft is silk and warp is cotton etc., then wearing it is permissible in war and disliked elsewhere. Because cloth becomes cloth due to weft, and the basis of weaving is on weft, so it is considered the origin (will come). What is the ruling for a garment whose warp is silk and weft is not silk? He (Imam Muhammad) said: And there is no harm in wearing a garment whose warp is silk and its weft is not silk, like cotton and khazz, in war and otherwise, because the Companions used to wear khazz, and khazz is warped with silk, and because a garment only becomes a garment by weaving, and weaving is by weft, so the weft is considered, not the warp. Translation: Muhammad said in Jami' al-Saghir: And there is no harm in wearing a garment whose warp is silk and its weft is not silk, like cotton and khazz, in war and otherwise, because the Companions used to wear khazz, and khazz' warp was silk, because a garment only becomes a garment by weaving, and weaving is by weft, so the weft is considered, not the warp. Explanation: The issue is clear; we have already mentioned it. Khazz is a cloth made from the hair of a sea animal. Musadda is a passive participle from sada, meaning warp. Sada = warp, luhma = weft.
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This passage clarifies the ruling on mixed silk garments based on which thread is silk. It begins with a note (tanbih) summarizing: if the warp (sada) is silk and the weft (luhma) is not, the garment is permissible always. If the weft is silk and warp not, it is permissible only in war (following the Sahibayn view) and disliked elsewhere. The reason is that a garment is primarily defined by its weft in weaving. The Arabic matn from Imam Muhammad's Jami' al-Saghir explicitly states that a garment with silk warp and non-silk weft is permissible in all circumstances, citing the practice of the Companions who wore khazz (a fabric with silk warp). The commentary explains that the weft is the primary element in weaving, so the prohibition of silk attaches to the weft, not the warp. Hence the reverse case (silk weft, non-silk warp) falls under the ruling of pure silk in non-war situations.

Key Terms
سداء (sada): The warp of a fabric (the threads that run lengthwise in weaving).
لحمة (luhma): The weft of a fabric (the threads woven across the warp).
خز (khazz): A type of fabric traditionally made from sea animal hair, with a silk warp; worn by the Companions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling on a garment whose weft (luhma) is silk and warp (sada) is cotton?
A) Permissible in all circumstances
B) Permissible only in war
C) Disliked even in war
D) Prohibited without exception

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes warp and weft: only the weft determines the silk prohibition; garments with silk warp are always permissible, while those with silk weft are permissible only in war.

Ring-Wearing for Judge and Sultan: Need-Based Ruling
Ruling on ring-wearing based on need

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wearing a silver ring for a judge/sultan versus others, and explain the role of need (hajah) in determining the preferred course.

Core Idea
A ring is permitted for sealing need; without it, leaving it is better.

This passage from al-Hidayah clarifies the Hanafi ruling on wearing signet rings. While wearing a silver ring is generally permissible, the degree of recommendation depends on one's need for sealing documents. For judges and rulers, wearing a ring is recommended due to their official duties; for others, it is better to avoid it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subjects
The passage first mentions the judge (القاضي) and the sultan (السلطان). These are the primary subjects of the ruling.
2
Establish the ruling for them
The passage states they wear a ring (يتختم) due to their need for sealing (لحاجته الى الختم). This indicates a recommended or permissible practice based on need.
The verb 'يتختم' implies they do wear it; the reason 'need' justifies the action.
3
Identify the category of others
The phrase 'فاما غيرهما' introduces the ruling for anyone else (غيرهم).
4
Identify the ruling for others
For others, the passage says 'الافضل ان يترك' — the better (more virtuous) is to leave it. This indicates that while wearing is not prohibited, abstaining is preferable.
The word 'الأفضل' (the better) shows that leaving it is a recommended act, not an obligation.
5
Analyze the underlying principle
The ruling hinges on need. For those with a need for sealing, wearing is recommended; for those without, the better course is to abstain. This reflects the Hanafi maxim that actions are evaluated based on intent and necessity.
This principle applies to other areas of fiqh as well.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وانما يتختم القاضى والسلطان لحاجته الى الختم فاما غيرهما فالافضل ان يترك لعدم الحاجة اليه
And the judge and the sultan wear a signet ring due to their need for sealing. As for other than them, the better is to leave it due to lack of need for it.
Source pages p. 326

Commentary
This passage addresses the wearing of a silver ring by a judge (qadi) and a sultan (ruler). They are permitted to wear a ring because they have a legitimate need: sealing documents. For anyone else without such a need, it is better (afdal) not to wear a ring, though it is not impermissible. The passage implies that wearing a ring without need is not haram or makruh, but leaving it is more virtuous.

Key Terms
القاضى والسلطان (al-qadi wa al-sultan): Judge and ruler who require a seal for official purposes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Who is permitted to wear a silver ring according to this passage?
A) Any Muslim man as a form of sunnah.
B) Only the judge and the sultan due to need for sealing.
C) All men regardless of need.
D) Only women.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on ring-wearing is contingent on need: recommended for those with a sealing requirement, and better to abstain for those without.

Gold Nail in Ring: The Principle of Tabi' (Followership)
Ruling on gold nail in ring setting with reasoning via tabi'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on using a gold nail in a ring setting and explain its permissibility based on the principle of tabi' (followership).

Core Idea
A gold nail in a ring is permissible because it follows the ruling of its setting, just like gold embroidery on fabric.

This short passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a practical question: may a man use a gold nail to secure a gemstone in his ring? The ruling is that it is permissible, and the reasoning introduces a key concept in Hanafi fiqh: the principle of tabi' (followership). We will unpack this principle, see how it applies here, and test our understanding with examples.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text rules on placing a gold nail (mismar al-dhahab) into the hole (juhr) of a ring's setting (fass). The ruling is 'la ba'sa' — there is no legal objection; it is permissible.
The ruling is not 'mustahabb' or 'wajib'; it is simply permissible.
2
Analyze the reasoning using 'tabi''
The author gives the reason: the gold nail is a follower (tabi'). It is not the primary object; it is subsidiary to the stone and the ring. As a follower, it does not change the overall ruling of the ring.
The term 'tabi'' is a legal term for an element that is incidental to the main object.
3
Understand the analogy to embroidery
The text compares the gold nail to gold embroidery ('alam) on a garment. Embroidery does not turn the garment into gold; it remains cloth. Similarly, a gold nail does not turn the ring into a gold ring.
The analogy (qiyas) is based on the shared attribute of being subsidiary.
4
Generalize the ruling
The principle of tabi' extends to other cases: any gold that is incidental and not the primary substance follows the ruling of the main item, provided it does not become independent or significant.
This principle prevents overly strict application of the prohibition of gold for men.

Source Text

This passage discusses a gold nail (mismar al-dhahab) used to secure a stone setting in a ring. The ruling is that there is no legal objection (la ba's) because the gold nail is a follower (tabi')—it is not the primary part. It is analogous to gold embroidery on a garment, which is not considered wearing gold. Therefore, the person is not considered to be wearing gold and the ring remains permissible.

Binding Teeth with Gold: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on gold for teeth binding

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf on binding teeth with gold, and explain the reasoning behind each view.

Core Idea
Gold for teeth is prohibited by Abu Hanifa because silver suffices; the Sahibayn permit it by analogy to the prophetic nose case.

In this passage from al-Hidayah, the author presents a difference of opinion among the three leading Hanafi imams on whether gold may be used to bind teeth. Abu Hanifa maintains the original prohibition of gold, while Muhammad and Abu Yusuf (in one narration) see it as permissible by analogy to a prophetic precedent. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply the principle of necessity (darurah) and to distinguish between general and specific precedents.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Rulings
Determine what each imam says about binding teeth with gold and with silver. Abu Hanifa: only silver; Muhammad: gold also permissible; Abu Yusuf: two narrations.
The text explicitly states 'This is according to Abu Hanifa' and 'Muhammad said: no harm in gold'.
2
Examine the Sahibayn's Proof
Read the hadith of Arfajah: his silver nose became foul, so the Prophet ordered gold. This is the basis for permitting gold for medical devices.
The Sahibayn use qiyas: if gold is allowed for a prosthetic nose, it should be allowed for binding teeth.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's Response
Abu Hanifa distinguishes the nose case: necessity was not fulfilled by silver because it caused odor. In teeth binding, silver works, so necessity does not arise, and gold remains prohibited.
The key difference is the fulfillment of need by the cheaper metal.
4
Trace the Thamarah al-Khilaf
What changes in practice? Under Abu Hanifa, patients must use silver; under Muhammad, gold is also fine. This affects cost, availability, and medical effectiveness.
The mufti must know which view is operative for fatwa.
5
Note the Tarjih
According to al-Hidayah, Abu Hanifa's view is stronger and is the mufta bihi position. The school relies on the original prohibition where silver is sufficient.
Abu Hanifa's position is considered more cautious and aligned with the default rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ولاتشد الاسنان بالذهب وتشد بالفضة وهذا عند ابي حنيفة وقال محمد لاباس بالذهب ايضاً وعن ابى يوسف مثل قول كل منهما لهما ان عرفجة بن اسعد اصيب انفعه يوم الكلاب فاتخذ انفامن فضة فانتن فامره النبي عليه السلام بان يتخذ انفا من ذهب ولابي حنيفة ان الأصل فيه التحريم والاباحة للضرورة وقداندافعت بالفضة وهى الادنى فبقى الذهب على التحريم والضرورة فيما روى لم تندفع في الانف دونه هيت انتن
He said: Teeth should not be bound with gold, but should be bound with silver. This is according to Abu Hanifa. And Muhammad said: There is no harm in gold as well. And from Abu Yusuf there is a saying like each of their sayings. Their (the Sahibayn's) proof is that Arfajah ibn As'ad had his nose injured on the day of Kilab. So he made a nose of silver, but it became foul-smelling, so the Prophet ﷺ ordered him to make a nose of gold. And for Abu Hanifa, the original ruling therein is prohibition, and permissibility is due to necessity, and that necessity is fulfilled by silver, which is lower, so gold remains on prohibition; and the necessity in the narrated incident was not fulfilled by silver regarding the nose, because it became foul-smelling.
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf (dispute) regarding binding teeth with gold. Abu Hanifa holds that teeth must be bound with silver only, and gold is not permissible. Muhammad al-Shaybani says gold is also permissible. Abu Yusuf has two narrations: one agreeing with Abu Hanifa and one with Muhammad. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) cite the hadith of Arfajah ibn As'ad, whose silver nose prosthetics caused bad odor, and the Prophet ﷺ ordered him to make it from gold. Abu Hanifa responds by affirming the original prohibition of gold. Necessity can permit it only when silver does not fulfill the need. In Arfajah's case, silver did not work, so gold was permitted by necessity. But in teeth binding, silver works, so gold remains prohibited.

Key Terms
شد الاسنان (shadd al-asnan): Binding or fastening teeth with metal wires for support.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why is gold not permissible for binding teeth?
A) Because silver is cheaper.
B) Because necessity is fulfilled by silver, so gold remains prohibited.
C) Because gold is not strong enough.
D) Because the Prophet prohibited binding teeth with any metal.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi prohibits gold for teeth binding because silver suffices, unless silver fails to meet the necessity.

The Gold Nail in a Gemstone's Socket: The Principle of Subordination
Ruling on a gold nail in a gemstone hole

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on a gold nail in a gemstone hole for men and explain how the principle of subordination (tābiʿ) determines the ruling.

Core Idea
A gold nail in a gemstone is permissible because the ruling follows the primary object, not the subordinate.

Many students assume any use of gold by men is prohibited. This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies a specific case: a gold nail used to secure a gemstone. By applying the Hanafi principle of subordination (tābiʿ), the ruling shifts from prohibition to permissibility. Let's examine how this principle works in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is placing a gold nail into the hole of a gemstone (in a ring). The ruling is that it is permissible (lā ba'sa).
2
Locate the legal principle
The author states the reasoning: 'because it is subordinate (tābiʿ) like embroidery on a garment'. Identify the principle: the ruling follows the primary object (matbūʿ), not the subordinate.
This is a classic Hanafi legal maxim: 'al-hukm li'l-matbūʿ lā li'l-tābiʿ'.
3
Apply the analogy
The gold nail is analogized to embroidery (naqsh). Embroidery on a garment does not change the garment's ruling. Similarly, the gold nail does not change the ruling of the ring because the primary object is the gemstone.
4
Distinguish the case of women
The passage notes that women are excluded because their purpose is adornment. For women, gold is not prohibited, so the subordination principle is not needed; they may wear gold freely.
This distinction highlights that the ruling is specific to the context of men's prohibition of gold.
5
Conclude the muftā bihi
The operative ruling (muftā bihi) is that a gold nail in a gemstone's hole is permissible for men, provided the gold is merely a means and not an independent ornament. The key condition is that the gold is tābiʿ (subordinate) to the gemstone.
This ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah as transmitted by Imam Muhammad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ولا باس بمسمار الذهب يجعل في جحر الفص اى فى ثقبه لانه تابع كالعلم فى الثوب فلا يعد لابسا له ترجمہ محمد نے فرمایا اور کوئی حرج نہیں سونے میں جس کو ٹھوک دیا جائے نگینہ کے سوراخ میں اس لئے کہ وہ (سونے کی شیخ ) تابع ہے جیسے کپڑے میں نقش و نگار تو اس کو سونے کا پہننے والا شمار نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ تشریح ماقبل میں گذر چکا ہے کہ حکم متبوع پر لگتا ہے نہ کہ تابع پر لہذا اگر نگینہ میں سونے کی منی ٹھکوالی تو اس میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ مقصد ختم یا نمونہ ہے نہ کہ ترین اور عورتیں باہر رکھیں اس لئے کہ ان کا مقصد تر ین نے اور ترین پشت کی جانب رکھنے میں ہے۔
He said: There is no harm in a gold nail placed in the hole of the gemstone, because it is a subordinate like embroidery on a garment, so the wearer is not considered to be wearing gold. Translation: Muhammad said: There is no harm in a gold nail being hammered into the hole of the gemstone, because it is a subordinate, like embroidery on cloth, so the wearer is not counted as wearing gold. Explanation: It has passed before that the ruling applies to the primary object, not the subordinate. Hence if a gold nail is hammered into the gemstone, there is no harm, because the purpose is the gemstone, not the gold. And women are excluded because their purpose is adornment and the gold is placed on the back of the ring.
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This is a ruling statement: It is permissible to use a gold nail to secure a gemstone in its setting. The legal principle is that the ruling follows the primary object (the gemstone), not the subordinate (the gold nail). The gold nail is compared to embroidery on a garment, which does not change the garment's ruling. The key condition is that the gold is merely a means of securing the gemstone and not an independent ornament. This ruling is specific to men; women may use gold freely.

Key Terms
تابع (tābiʿ): A subordinate or accessory that is not the primary object of consideration.
متبوع (matbūʿ): The primary object or entity; the main subject that carries the ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi passage, why is a gold nail in a gemstone's hole permissible for men?
A) Because gold is always permissible in small amounts.
B) Because the gold nail is a subordinate (tābiʿ) to the gemstone, and the ruling follows the primary object.
C) Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) specifically allowed it.
D) Because it is a necessity for keeping the gemstone in place.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits a gold nail in a gemstone hole for men because the gold is subordinate (tābiʿ) and the ruling follows the primary object (matbūʿ).

Binding Teeth with Gold or Silver: The Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on gold/silver for teeth

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on binding teeth with gold vs silver, explain the proofs of Abu Hanifah and Sahibayn, and identify the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Gold is prohibited unless necessity demands it; if silver suffices, gold remains prohibited.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the permissibility of using gold wire to bind teeth when silver is available. Imam Abu Hanifah holds that only silver is permissible, while Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani permits gold as well, relying on the hadith of Arfajah. Understanding this dispute clarifies how the Hanafi school applies the principle of necessity (darurah) to override the original prohibition of gold for men.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling of Abu Hanifah: teeth should be bound with silver, not gold, because gold is originally prohibited for men.
This is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position.
2
Identify the opposing view
Recognize that Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani permits gold as well, and Abu Yusuf has two narrations (one agreeing with each).
The Sahibayn differ from Abu Hanifah.
3
Analyze the opposing proof
Examine the hadith of Arfajah ibn As'ad: the Prophet allowed him to use a gold nose when silver caused a foul smell.
This is a specific case of necessity.
4
Analyze Abu Hanifah's response
Understand Abu Hanifah's distinction: the original prohibition of gold is lifted only when necessity is not met by a permissible alternative. Since silver fulfills the need, gold remains prohibited.
The hadith is not generalizable because silver failed there.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Conclude that the relied-upon ruling is that of Abu Hanifah: only silver is permissible unless silver itself fails to address the need.
This is the operative fatwa.

This is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding binding teeth with gold or silver wires. Muhammad al-Shaybani says gold is also permissible, relying on the hadith of Arfajah who was allowed to use a gold nose when silver caused a foul smell. Abu Yusuf has two narrations, agreeing with both. The Hanafi position (Abu Hanifah) is that necessity must be genuine; since silver works, gold remains prohibited. The hadith is specific to a case where silver failed, so it does not generalize. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is Abu Hanifah's – silver only, unless silver fails, then gold may be used.
