Dressing Boys in Gold and Silk: The Qiyas Ruling
Ruling with proof by qiyas jaliy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on dressing male children in gold and silk according to the Hanafi school and explain the qiyas used to derive it.

Core Idea
Making a child wear what is haram for adults is also haram — the qiyas of wine-drinking.

This lesson examines the ruling on dressing young boys in gold and silk. The Hanafi school, through a clear analogy (qiyas jaliy), extends the prohibition from adult men to children, based on the principle that causing a prohibited act is itself prohibited.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is dressing male children in gold or silk. The ruling is 'makruh' (disliked), which in this context carries the weight of prohibition (makruh tahrimi).
2
Locate the underlying ruling for adults
The original ruling is that wearing gold and silk is haram for adult men. This is established from Quran and Sunnah.
3
Understand the illa (effective cause)
The illa is causing involvement in a prohibited act. Dressing a child in prohibited attire is a means of facilitating the prohibition.
4
Follow the qiyas structure
Asl: adult men wearing gold/silk is haram. Far': dressing children in gold/silk. Illa: causing prohibited act. Hukm: prohibition (makruh tahrimi).
5
Note the analogous case: wine
The text draws a parallel: just as giving wine is prohibited because drinking it is prohibited, so dressing children in gold/silk is prohibited because wearing it is prohibited for adults.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ويكره ان يلبس الذكور من الصبيان الذهب والحرير لان التحريم لما ثبت في حق الذكور وحرم اللبس حرم الالباس كا لخمر لما حرم شربه حرم سقيه ترجمہ قددری نے فرمایا اور مکروہ ہے لڑکوں کوسونا اور ریشم پہنانا اس لئے کہ تحریم جب کہ مردوں کے حق میں نا بنے گی اپنا حرام ہو گیا تو پہنا نامی گرام ہو گا جیسے شراب جب کہ اس کو پینا حرام ہو گیا تو اسکو پلانا بھی حرام ہوگا۔ تشریح جس طرح سونا اور ریشم مردوں کو پہنا حرام ہے ایسے ہی چھوٹے لڑکوں کو پہنانا بھی مکروہ ہے جیسے شراب پینا حرام ہے تو پلانا بھی حرام ہے۔
He said: It is disliked to dress male children in gold and silk, because when prohibition is established for men, wearing is prohibited, so dressing is prohibited, just as when drinking wine is prohibited, serving it is also prohibited. Translation: Quduri said: It is disliked to dress boys in gold and silk, because when prohibition is established for men, wearing becomes prohibited, so making them wear it also becomes prohibited, just as when drinking wine is prohibited, giving it to drink is also prohibited. Explanation: Just as gold and silk are prohibited for men to wear, similarly dressing young boys in them is disliked, just as drinking wine is prohibited, so giving it to drink is also prohibited.
Source pages p. 328

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof by analogy (qiyas jaliy). It states that it is makruh (disliked, and in this context it implies prohibition) for male children to be dressed in gold or silk. The reasoning is that if an act is prohibited for adults, it is also prohibited to cause them to do it, by analogy to wine: just as giving wine to someone is prohibited because drinking it is prohibited, so making boys wear gold/silk is prohibited because wearing them is prohibited for men. Note: The term 'makruh' here is used in the context of prohibition (makruh tahrimi) because the basis is a clear prohibition.

Key Terms
كراهة (karāhah): In this passage, 'makruh' means prohibited (tahriman), as it is based on the prohibition for adult men.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for the ruling that dressing male children in gold and silk is makruh?
A) Direct Quranic prohibition for children.
B) Analogy to the prohibition for adult men, using the example of wine.
C) Consensus of the companions.
D) It is allowed because children are not obligated.

Key Takeaway
Dressing male children in gold and silk is makruh tahrimi because enabling a prohibited act is itself prohibited, as shown by the qiyas with wine.

Cloth for Wiping Sweat and Tying Thread for Memory
Ruling on two personal habits: cloth usage and memory aid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on carrying a cloth for wiping sweat and tying a thread for memory, and explain how intention (niyyah) changes the ruling from makruh to mubah.

Core Idea
Intention determines permissibility: cloth for need is mubah; for pride is makruh.

In this passage from al-Hidayah, two everyday habits are examined: carrying a cloth to wipe sweat or clean the nose, and tying a thread on the finger to remember something. Both rulings hinge on the intention behind the act. An act that outwardly resembles pride becomes permissible when done out of genuine need.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two acts and their default ruling
Read the first part: the cloth carried for wiping sweat or blowing the nose is initially declared disliked (makruh). The second act: tying a thread on finger or ring is said to be without harm (no objection).
The default ruling for the cloth is makruh; for the thread it is mubah.
2
Analyse the exception for the cloth
The text then mentions a differing opinion (qīla): if the cloth is carried out of need (ḥājah), it is not disliked. The author declares this the correct view (ṣaḥīḥ). The dislikedness is only when done out of pride (takabbur) or arrogance (tajabbura).
The key is the intention: need vs. pride.
3
Understand the proof for tying the thread
The text cites three proofs: (1) it was a custom of the Arabs, (2) a poetic line mentioning tying knots, (3) a narration that the Prophet ordered some Companions to do it. The purpose is a valid purpose (gharaḍ ṣaḥīḥ): remembering when one forgets.
The act is not frivolous ('abath) because of its utility.
4
Note the ikhtilaf and tarjih
There is a legitimate difference (ikhtilaf) regarding the cloth: some earlier scholars considered it disliked unconditionally. The correct Hanafi position (the ṣaḥīḥ view) distinguishes based on intention. The muftā bihī is permissibility when needed.
The tarjīḥ is done by the author of al-Hidayah, ruling the exception as ṣaḥīḥ.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وتكره الخرقة التي تحمل فيمسح بها العرق لانه نوع تجبرو تكبر وكذا التي يمسح بها الوضو اويمتخط بها وقيل اذا كان عن حاجة لا يكره وهو الصحيح وانما يكره اذا كان عن تكبر و تجبر فصار كالتربع في الجلوس ولا باس بان يربط الرجل في اصبعه او خاتمه الخيط للحاجة ويسمى ذلك الرتم والرتيمة وكان ذلك من عادة العرب قال قائلهم شعر لا ينفعنك اليوم ان همت بهم كثرة ما توصى وتعقاد الرتم وقد روى ان النبي عليه السلام امر بعض اصحابه بذلک ولانه ليس بعبث لما فيه من الغرض الصحيح وهو التذكر عند النسيان. ترجمہ محمد نے فرمایا اور کر وہ ہے کپڑے کا وہ پکڑا جس کو ساتھ رکھا جاتا ہے پس اس سے پسینہ پو چھا جاتا ہے اس لئے یہ تجبر اور تکبر کی ایک قسم ہے اور ایسے ہی وہ کپڑا جس سے وضو کا پانی پوچھا جاتا ہے اور جس سے ناک صاف کی جاتی ہے اور کہا گیا جب کہ ضرورت کی وجہ سے ہو تو مکروہ نہیں ہے اور یہی صحیح ہے اور مکروہ جب ہے جبکہ تکبر اور تجبر سے ہو اور ہو گیا یہ پھارزانو بیٹھنے کے مان اور کوئی حرج نہیں ہے کہ آدمی اپنی انگلی میں یا اپنی انگوٹھی میں کسی ضرورت کی وجہ سے دھاگہ باندھے اور اس کا نام رتم اور رتیم رکھا جاتا ہے اور یہ عرب کی عادت تھی کہا ان میں سے کہنے والے نے شعر ہر گز نفع نہیں دے گا تجھ کو آج اگر عورت نے مردوں کے ساتھ ارادہ کر لیا ہو تو تیرا بکثرت وصیت کرنا اور دھاگہ باندھنا، اور حقیق کہ مروی ہے کہ نبی علیہ السلام نے اپنے بعض صحابہ کو اس کا حکم فرمایا اور اس لئے کہ یہ عیب نہیں ہے بوجہ اس کے کہ اس میں غرض صحیح ہے اور وہ یاد کرنا ہے بھولنے کے وقت۔ تشریح لوگوں کی عادت ہے کہ رومال یادتی یا تو یہ ساتھ رکھتے ہیں جس سے پسینہ پونچھتے ہیں اور وضوء کا پانی پونچھتے ہیں اور ناک
He said: The cloth that is carried for wiping sweat is disliked, because it is a kind of arrogance and pride. Likewise, the cloth used to wipe water from wudu or to blow the nose. It was said: If it is for a need, it is not disliked – this is correct. It is only disliked if it is out of pride and arrogance, then it becomes like sitting with legs drawn up. There is no harm in a man tying a thread on his finger or ring for a need. That is called ratam or ratimah, and it was a custom of the Arabs. One of them said in poetry: 'It will not benefit you today, if you intend to act against them, your frequent bequests and tying of knots.' It is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) ordered some of his Companions to do that. It is not frivolous because it contains a valid purpose: to remember when one forgets. Explanation: (the Urdu explains the same).
Source pages p. 328

Commentary
This passage contains two rulings regarding personal habits. First, carrying a cloth solely for wiping sweat or blowing the nose is disliked if done out of arrogance; but if done out of genuine need, it is permissible. The key is the intention: if one does it to show off, it is disliked; otherwise not. Second, tying a thread on the finger or ring as a memory aid is permissible, as it was done by the Arabs and the Prophet ordered it. It is not a frivolous act because it serves a legitimate purpose: remembering things. This ruling is classified under 'makruh' in the sense of disliked, but the correct view is that it is not disliked when needed.

Key Terms
رتم (ratam): A thread tied on a finger or ring to remember something.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) When it is done out of necessity.
C) When it is given as a gift.
D) When it is used only for the face.

Key Takeaway
Intention (niyyah) and need transform an apparently disliked act into a permissible one; tying a thread for memory is a valid sunnah-inspired practice.

Ruling on Carrying a Handkerchief and Tying a Memory Thread
Ruling on using a handkerchief and tying a thread for memory, with clarification of dislike

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on carrying a handkerchief and tying a memory thread, and identify when the ruling of karahah is overridden by need.

Core Idea
Dislike lifts when need is genuine; intention transforms the ruling.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses two everyday actions: carrying a cloth to wipe sweat and tying a thread to remember something. While an initial ruling declares them disliked due to resemblance to arrogant behavior, the correct view in the Hanafi school is that this dislike only applies when done out of pride. When there is a genuine need, both actions become permissible. Understanding this nuance helps us see how the school applies the principle that actions are judged by intentions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial rulings
The text first states that carrying a handkerchief and tying a memory thread are disliked (makruh). The reason given is arrogance (tajabbur wa takabbur).
The initial ruling is based on preventing imitation of arrogant people.
2
Locate the exception and the correct view
The text then mentions the view that if done out of need (hajah), it is not disliked, and declares this as the correct view (as-sahih). So the ruling is conditional on intention.
The word 'hajah' includes genuine need, not mere want.
3
Understand the analogy with sitting cross-legged
The commentator analogizes the handkerchief to sitting cross-legged, which is also only disliked if done arrogantly. This shows the principle: the same action can be mubah or makruh depending on intention.
The analogy helps clarify the legal reasoning (qiyas).
4
Examine the memory thread's basis
For the thread (ratm), the text cites Arab custom, a weak hadith of the Prophet commanding it, and a valid purpose (tadhakkur). This makes it not futile and thus permissible.
Weak hadith combined with custom and valid purpose create permissibility.
5
Conclude the practical ruling
Therefore, the mufta bihi (operative ruling) is: using a handkerchief for need is not disliked; tying a memory thread is permissible. Both are mubah when free from arrogance.
This is the position relied upon by later Hanafi scholars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وتكره الخرقة التي تحمل فيمسح بها العرق لانه نوع تجبرو تكبر وكذا التي يمسح بها الوضو اويمتخط بها وقيل اذا كان عن حاجة لا يكره وهو الصحيح وانما يكره اذا كان عن تكبر و تجبر فصار كالتربع في الجلوس ولا باس بان يربط الرجل في اصبعه او خاتمه الخيط للحاجة ويسمى ذلك الرتم والرتيمة وكان ذلك من عادة العرب قال قائلهم شعر لا ينفعنك اليوم ان همت بهم كثرة ما توصى وتعقاد الرتم وقد روى ان النبي عليه السلام امر بعض اصحابه بذلک ولانه ليس بعبث لما فيه من الغرض الصحيح وهو التذكر عند النسيان.
He said: It is disliked to carry a cloth to wipe sweat, because it is a kind of arrogance and pride; similarly the cloth with which one wipes the water of ablution or blows one's nose. And it is said: if it is for a need, it is not disliked, and that is the correct view; it is only disliked when it is out of pride and arrogance, so it becomes like sitting cross-legged. And there is no harm for a man to tie a thread on his finger or ring for a need, and that is called 'ratm' and 'ratīmah', and that was the custom of the Arabs. One of their poets said: 'It will not benefit you today, if you pursue them, the abundance of your instructions and the tying of the ratm.' And it has been narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) commanded some of his companions to do that. And because it is not futile, as it has a valid purpose, which is to remember when forgetting.
Source pages p. 328

Commentary
This passage from Al-Hidayah discusses two related issues: First, the ruling on carrying a handkerchief (khirqah) for wiping sweat, ablution water, or nose. The initial ruling is that it is disliked (makruh) because it resembles arrogance and pride. However, the correct view (as-sahih) is that it is only disliked if done out of pride; if there is a genuine need, it is not disliked. The commentator compares it to sitting cross-legged, which is only disliked if done arrogantly. Second, the ruling on tying a thread on the finger or ring to remember something (called ratm or ratimah). This was a practice of the Arabs, and a poet is quoted to show its usage. The commentator adds that a weak hadith mentions the Prophet (peace be upon him) commanding some companions to do it. Since there is a valid purpose (remembrance), it is not futile (عبث) and is thus permissible. The commentator then notes that later scholars (mutakkhirin) have preferred the permissibility of using a handkerchiefs due to the practice of Muslims, and that tying a thread for memory is allowed.

Key Terms
الخرقة (al-khirqah): A small cloth or handkerchief used for wiping sweat, water, or nose.
الرتم (ar-ratm): A thread tied on the finger or ring as a memory aid.
التجبر والتكبر (at-tajabbur wa at-takabbur): Arrogance and pride; these are the reasons for the original ruling of karahah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The ruling on permissible actions can change based on intention; need overrides the initial dislike.

Covering Graves: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Bid'ah
Intra-Hanafi dispute on grave covering

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on covering graves and evaluate which is mufta bihi according to the commentator's reasoning.

Core Idea
A lenient fatwa from an authority may be overridden if it leads to bid'ah — preventing evil takes precedence.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the practice of covering graves of saints and righteous individuals with cloth. Allama Shami (Ibn Abidin) ruled it permissible, but a later commentator in Ashraf al-Hadaya strongly rejects this, labeling it a laxity and an evil innovation (bid'ah sayyiah). Understanding this disagreement helps you navigate when a later fatwa can override an earlier authoritative opinion based on preventing harm.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The core issue: Is it permissible to place cloth on the graves of righteous people?
The context is a specific practice, not general grave reverence.
2
State the first position (Shami's view)
Allama Shami ruled that covering graves of saints and righteous people is permissible.
This is a known fatwa from Ibn Abidin, a major Hanafi authority.
3
State the second position (commentator's view)
The commentator (Ashraf al-Hadaya) calls Shami's ruling a laxity and declares the practice an evil bid'ah, thus forbidding it.
He argues that the practice has become a slippery slope to innovation.
4
Analyze the basis of disagreement
Shami focuses on the inherent permissibility; the commentator prioritizes preventing bid'ah (sadd al-dhara'i).
The commentator uses the principle of blocking means to evil, even if the act itself is not inherently haram.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The commentator presents his view as the correct stance, implying that Shami's fatwa is outweighed by the need to prevent bid'ah.
Later Hanafi fatwa collections often adopt stricter positions to protect against innovations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبیہ علامہ شامی نے یہاں صلحاء اور صالحین کی قبر پر چادر وغیرہ ڈالنے کو جائز قرار دیا ہے۔ یہ علامہ شامی کا تسامح ہے اور یہاں بدعت ستیہ پھیلی ہوئی ہے لہذا اس سے تو لوگوں کو روکنا ضروری ہے ،
Note: Allama Shami has declared it permissible to place a sheet etc. on the graves of saints and righteous people. This is a laxity from Allama Shami, and here an evil bid'ah has spread, so it is necessary to prevent people from this.
Source pages p. 329

Commentary
This tanbih (note) presents an intra-Hanafi disagreement regarding covering graves. Allama Shami (Ibn Abidin) ruled that placing cloth on the graves of awliya and salihin is permissible. However, the commentator strongly rejects this, labeling it a laxity (tasaamuh) on Shami's part. He asserts that such a practice has become an evil innovation (bid'ah sayyiah) and must be actively forbidden. This reflects a stricter stance against practices that may lead to excessive veneration of graves, which is a concern in Hanafi fiqh to prevent shirk. The commentator prioritizes preventing bid'ah over a permissive ruling from a later authority.

Key Terms
تسامح (tasaamuh): Laxity; a lenient ruling that the commentator considers overly permissive.
بدعت ستیہ (bid'ah sayyiah): An evil innovation; any new practice in religion that is not based on the Sunnah and is harmful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He agrees with it
B) He calls it a laxity and an evil bid'ah
C) He says it is obligatory
D) He says it is only for saints

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a later fatwa may overrule a permissive earlier ruling if the practice leads to bid'ah; preventing evil takes precedence.

Tying a Thread to Remember: The Principle of Gharad vs Abath
Ruling that tying a thread for memory is permissible despite weak hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that an act with a valid purpose (gharad) is permissible, even if its specific hadith are weak.

Core Idea
An act with a valid purpose is not futile; futility is haram, purpose makes it mubah.

In this lesson, we examine a ruling that may seem surprising: tying a thread on one's finger to remember something is permissible, despite the lack of strong prophetic evidence. The commentator explains that this is not a superstitious act but a practical memory aid with a genuine purpose. This ruling illustrates a key Hanafi principle: the permissibility of actions is the default, and only futile acts (abath) are forbidden.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its apparent problem
What is the act being judged? Why might it be questionable? (lack of strong hadith, resembling superstition)
2
Understand the concept of abath
What is futility (abath)? Why is it haram in Hanafi fiqh? Any action without a valid purpose is prohibited.
Abath is a key evaluative concept.
3
Evaluate the act's purpose
Does this act have a valid purpose (gharad)? Yes – it helps one remember. Therefore it is not abath.
The gharad must be genuine and permissible.
4
Draw the conclusion
Since the act has a valid purpose, it is not futile; thus it is permissible (mubah). Weakness of specific hadith does not change this.
Based on the general principle that acts with benefit are permitted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اہل عرب کی عادت تھی کہ کسی شی ء کو یاد کرنے کے لئے انگلی یا انگوٹھی میں دھاگہ باندھ لیا کرتے تھے بلکہ ہندوستان میں بھی کچھ بڑھوں کو اس پر عمل کرتے دیکھا گیا ہے اور اس دھاگہ کو ر تم اور رتیم کہتے ہیں تو فرمایا کہ یہ جائز ہے اور نبی کریم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے بعض صحابہ کو اس کا حکم فرمایا، لیکن یہ روایت نہیں ملتی ، بلکہ اس باب کی جملہ روایات ضعیف ہیں بہر حال یہ عبث کام نہیں ہے اور عبث حرام ہے بلکہ اس کی ایک صحیح غرض ہے اور وہ بھولنے کے وقت یاد کرنا ہے لہذا جائز ہے، شعر مذکور میں رتم بمعنی دھاگہ مستعمل ہے اور تعقاد مصدر ہے تفعال کے وزن پر بمعنی باندھنا، اور شعر کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ جب عورت ہی پا کد امن نہ ہو بلکہ بدمعاش ہو تو اس کو بکثرت وصیت کرنا اور اس کی انگلی میں دھاگہ باندھنا کچھ مفید نہ ہو گا بلکہ وہ تو بد معاشی کرے گی ہاں اگر وہ نیک صالح ہے تو پھر ان کی بھی ضرورت نہیں ہے وہ اپنی شرافت نفس کی وجہ سے ان خرافات سے باز رہے گی ۔
The practice of the Arabs was that they would tie a thread on their finger or ring to remember something. In India, some elders are seen practicing this, and this thread is called 'ratam' and 'ratim'. So it is said that this is permissible, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) commanded some Companions to do this, but this narration is not found; rather, all narrations on this topic are weak. Nevertheless, this is not a futile act, and futility is forbidden. Rather, it has a valid purpose: to remember when one forgets. Therefore, it is permissible. In the mentioned verse, 'ratm' is used to mean thread, and 'ta'qid' is a masdar on the pattern of taf'il meaning tying. The meaning of the verse is that when the woman herself is not pure and chaste, but rather immoral, then making many bequests to her and tying a thread on her finger will not be beneficial; rather, she will continue her immorality. Yes, if she is righteous, then there is no need for these things; due to the nobility of her nature, she will refrain from these superstitious things.
Source pages p. 329

Commentary
This passage rules on the permissibility of tying a thread on one's finger or ring as a memory aid. Although the practice originated among Arabs and is also seen in India, and there are claims of a prophetic command, all narrations regarding this are weak. Despite the lack of strong hadith, the act is deemed permissible because it is not futile (abath). Futility (abath) is forbidden in Islam, but this practice has a valid purpose: helping one remember something. The commentator explains a poetic verse to further illustrate that external aids are useless for someone with bad character, but if a person is righteous, they don't need such reminders. Thus, the ruling is based on the principle that permissible acts become impermissible only if they are utterly pointless (abath). Having a genuine purpose (gharad) makes the act mubah.

Key Terms
عبث (abath): Futility; an action without any valid purpose. Abath is forbidden (haram) in Islamic law.
غرض (gharad): Purpose or goal. An act that has a legitimate gharad is not futile and is permissible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is tying a thread to remember something considered permissible despite weak hadith?
A) Because the hadith are strong
B) Because it is a common practice
C) Because it is not a futile act and has a valid purpose
D) Because it is recommended by the Prophet

Key Takeaway
An act with a genuine purpose is not futile; therefore, it is permissible even if its specific textual evidence is weak.

6 min
Ruling on Looking at a Non-Mahram Woman
States the ruling with its Quranic proof and Companion interpretation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on which body parts of a non-mahram woman may be looked at, and explain the Quranic proof and the Companions' interpretation using majaz mursal.

Core Idea
A man may only look at the face and hands of a non-mahram woman.

This lesson presents the foundational Hanafi rule on the gaze between non-mahram men and women. The ruling is derived from Quran 24:31 and the interpretation of the Companions. You will see how the Hanafi school uses the rhetorical device of majaz mursal to extract this rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the passage and note the explicit ruling: a man may not look at a non-mahram woman except her face and hands. This is the mufta bihi position.
The ruling is categorical; no other body parts are permitted.
2
Locate the Quranic proof
The author cites Quran 24:31: 'And let them not display their adornment except what is apparent of it.' This verse is the primary dalil.
The proof is naqli (textual) from the Quran.
3
Examine the Companion interpretation
Ali and Ibn Abbas (RA) interpret 'what is apparent' as kohl and ring. Their interpretation is key to understanding the exception.
The Companions' tafsir is authoritative in Hanafi usul.
4
Understand the rhetorical move (majaz mursal)
The commentary explains that kohl and ring are mentioned, but the intended meaning is their places: the eyes (face) and the finger (hand). This is majaz mursal, where the cause (adornment) stands for the effect (place).
This interpretive tool limits the exception to face and hands only.
5
Confirm the scope of the ruling
Thus, the exception includes only the face and hands. All other body parts must be covered. Looking at any other part without necessity is haram.
Necessity (e.g., medical treatment) may have different rulings, but the base rule remains.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الوطى والنظر والمس
ترجمہ فصل ہے ولی اور نظر اور چھونے کے بیان میں
كتاب الكراهية
تشریح اس فصل میں مصنف دیکھنے اور چھونے اور عزل کے احکام بیان فرمائیں گے ظاہر یہی ہے کہ مصنف کی مراد ولی سے عزل ہے ور نہ اس میں وطی کا ذکر نہیں ہے اور چونکہ عزل کا ذکر بعد میں ہے اس وجہ سے اس کا ذکر بعد میں مناسب تھا۔
مرد کیلئے اجنبیہ کے چہرے اور ہتھیلیوں کا دیکھنا نا جائز ہے
قال ولا يجوز ان ينظر الرجل الى الاجنبية الا الى وجهها وكفيها لقوله تعالى ولا يبدين زينتهن الا ما ظهر منها قال على وابن عباس رضى الله عنهما ما ظهر منها الكحل والخاتم والمراد موضعهما وهو الوجه والكف كما ان المراد بالزينة المذكورة مواضعها
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جائز نہیں ہے یہ کہ دیکھے مرد اجنبیہ کی جانب مگر اس کا چہر اور اس کی دونوں ہتھیلیاں اللہ تعالی کے فرمان و لا یپدین زینتهن الا ماظهر منها کی دلیل علی اور ابن عباس نے فرمایا ماظهر منها سرمہ اور انگوٹھی ہیں اور مراد ان دونوں کی جگہ ہے اور وہ چہرہ اور ہتھیلی ہے جیسا کہ مراد اس زینت سے جو مذکور ہے مواضع زینت ہیں۔
تشریح مرد کسی اجنبیہ کا بدن بغیر کسی ضرورت کے دیکھے جائز نہیں ہے علاوہ چہرہ اور تھیلی کے اللہ تعالیٰ کا یہ فرمان ولا يبدين الخ
دو باتیں معلوم ہوئیں۔ مواضع زینت کو چھپاؤ
چہرہ اور ہتھیلی کو ظاہر کرنا جائز ہے۔
حضرت علیؓ اور حضرت ابن عباس آیت کی تفسیر میں فرماتے ہیں کہ ماظہر منہا سے مراد سرمہ اور انگوٹھی ہیں اور مجاز مرسل کے چوبیس علاقوں میں سے علاقہ حالیت اور محلیت بھی ہے یعنی حال بول کر محل اور محل بول کر حال مراد لینا تو یہاں حال بول کر محل مراد لیا گیا ہے یعنی سرمہ سے آنکھ اور وہ چہرہ میں ہوتی ہے تو سرمہ سے مراد چہرہ ہے اور انگوٹھی سے مراد انگلی اور ہتھیلی میں ہوتی ہے لہذ ا ما ظہر منہا سے چہرہ اور تھیلی مراد ہیں اور اسی طرح آیت میں زینت سے مراد مواضع زینت ہیں علاقہ حالیت کی وجہ سے اور مواضع زینت میں چہرہ اور ہتھیلی کے علاوہ سارا بدن داخل ہے۔ نبيه ولا يبدين زينتهن الا ماظهر منها ، اور اپنی زیبائش ظاہر نہ کریں مگر جو اس میں سے کھلی چیز ، مطلب یہ ہے کہ عورت کو کسی قسم طلقی یا کیسی زیبائش کا اظہار بحجر محارم کے کسی کے سامنے جائز نہیں ہاں جس قدر زیبائش کا ظہور نا گزیر ہے اور اس کے ظہور کو بسبب عدم قدرت یا ضرورت کے روک نہیں سکتی اس کے بیجوری یا بضرورت کھلا رکھنے میں منما نفقہ نہیں بشرطیکہ فتنہ کا خوف نہ ہو۔
Chapter on Intercourse, Looking, and Touching. Translation: The chapter is about the statement of looking and touching. Book of Disliked Matters. Explanation: In this chapter, the author will explain the rulings of looking, touching, and 'azl. It is apparent that the author intends by wati' 'azl; otherwise, there is no mention of intercourse, and since 'azl is mentioned later, it would have been more appropriate to mention it later. For a man, looking at the face and palms of a non-mahram woman is not permissible. He (al-Quduri) said: 'And it is not permissible for a man to look at a non-mahram woman except her face and hands.' Because of the saying of Allah: 'And let them not display their adornment except what is apparent of it.' Ali and Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them) said: 'What is apparent of it is kohl and the ring.' The meaning is their places, which are the face and hands, just as the meaning of the mentioned adornment is its places. Translation: Al-Quduri said: It is not permissible for a man to look at a non-mahram woman except her face and both her palms, due to Allah's command 'and let them not display their adornment except what is apparent of it.' Ali and Ibn Abbas said: 'What is apparent of it is kohl and ring,' and the meaning is their places, which are the face and hands, just as the meaning of the mentioned adornment is its places. Explanation: It is not permissible for a man to look at any body part of a non-mahram woman without necessity, except the face and palms. Allah's command 'and let them not display...' Two things become known: (1) conceal the places of adornment, (2) it is permissible to reveal the face and hands. Ali and Ibn Abbas explain the verse: 'what is apparent' means kohl and ring, and by majaz mursal, the 'thing' (kohl, ring) is used to mean their 'place' (eyes, hand). So kohl refers to the eyes (face), and ring refers to the finger (hand). Thus, 'what is apparent' means face and hands. Similarly, 'adornment' in the verse means the places of adornment. The commentary: The woman should not display any adornment to non-mahram men, except that which is unavoidably visible or due to necessity, provided there is no fear of fitna.
Source pages p. 330

Commentary
This passage is a ruling (hukm) with its proof (dalil). It opens a new chapter on looking and touching. The author (al-Quduri) states the well-known Hanafi ruling: A man may not look at any part of a non-mahram woman except her face and hands. The proof is Quran 24:31 where women are commanded not to display their adornment except what is 'apparent'. The Companions Ali and Ibn Abbas interpret 'apparent' as kohl (antimony) and a ring, meaning the places where they are worn—the eyes (face) and fingers (hands). The commentary explains that this is a rhetorical device called majaz mursal (synecdoche), where the cause (kohl, ring) is used for the effect (the place). Thus, the exception for face and hands is derived. The passage also explains that the verse means to conceal all other adornment and body parts. The ruling is absolute: looking at any other part is prohibited, unless necessity or lack of fitna permits. This is a foundational rule in Hanafi fiqh for gender interactions.

Key Terms
اجنبیہ (ajnabiyyah): A woman who is not a mahram (permanently forbidden for marriage) to the man.
زینت (zinah): Adornment; in this context, it refers to both the physical beauty and the means of beautification (like kohl and ring).
مجاز مرسل (majaz mursal): A type of figurative speech where a word is used for something related to its original meaning, like cause for effect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which body parts of a non-mahram woman may a man lawfully look at?
A) The entire body except the private parts
B) Only the face and hands
C) The face, hands, and feet
D) Only the eyes

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits looking only at the face and hands of a non-mahram woman, based on the Quranic exception interpreted by the Companions via majaz mursal.

Ruling on Touching a Non-Mahram Woman's Face and Palm
Ruling with proof from hadith, distinguishing touching and looking.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on touching a non-mahram woman's face and palm, cite the primary proof from hadith, and distinguish between the rulings on looking and touching.

Core Idea
Touching a non-mahram woman's face or palm is haram even without desire, due to explicit hadith; looking is permissible because of widespread need.

The Hanafi school draws a sharp distinction between looking at and touching a non-mahram woman. While looking at the face and hands is permissible when safe from desire, touching them is strictly prohibited by a specific hadith, regardless of desire. This lesson examines the textual basis for this ruling and its exceptions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The act is touching a non-mahram woman's face or palm. The ruling is haram for a young woman, even if the man is safe from desire.
The text explicitly states 'la yahillu' (not permissible).
2
Locate the dalil
What proof is cited? The author cites a hadith: 'Whoever touches a woman's hand without being lawful to him, a burning coal will be placed on his palm on the Day of Judgment.'
The hadith is ahad but its meaning is clear.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove prohibition? The direct threat of punishment indicates that the act is a major sin, i.e., haram. The phrase 'without being lawful' clarifies the condition.
The punishment is not just for desire but for the act itself.
4
Note the distinction between looking and touching
Looking is permissible due to widespread need (balwa), but touching lacks such need. The hadith also specifically prohibits touching.
The text says 'bikhilaf al-nazar' (unlike looking).
5
Note the exception for old women
For an old woman who is not desired, touching (e.g., shaking hands) is permissible because there is no fear of fitna.
This exception is based on the absence of desire.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
چہرے اور تھیلی کو چھونے کا حکم
ولا يحل له ان يمس وجهها ولا كفها وان كان يامن الشهوة لقيام المحرم وانعدام الضرورة والبلوى بخلاف النظر لان فيه بلوى والمحرم قوله عليه السلام من مس كف المرأة ليس منها بسبيل وضع على كفه جمر يوم القيمة وهذا اذا كانت شابة تشتهى ما اذا كانت عجوزا لا تشتهي فلا بأس بمصافحتها ومس يدها لانعدام خوف الفتنة
ترجمہ اور حلال نہیں ہے مرد کے لئے یہ کہ وہ چھوئے عورت کے چہرہ کو اور نہ اس کی تھیلی کو اگر چہ وہ شہوت سے مامون ہومحرم کے قائم مقام ہونے کی وجہ سے اور ضرورت اور ابتلاء عام نہ ہونے کی وجہ بخلاف دیکھنے کے اس لئے کہ اس میں ابتلا و عام ہے اور محرم حرام کرنے والا نبی علیہ السلام کا یہ فرمان ہے جس نے چھو یا کسی عورت کے ہا تھ کو حالانکہ مرد کے لئے شرعاً اس میں کوئی راہ نہیں ہے تو اس کے ہاتھ پر قیامت کے دن انگارہ کھا جائے گا اور یہ جب ہے کہ وہ جوان عورت ہو جس کی شہوت ہوتی ہو بہر حال جب کہ وہ بڑھیا ہو جس کی شہوت نہیں ہوتی تو اس کے ساتھ مصافحہ کرنے میں اور اس کا ہاتھ چھونے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے فتنہ کا خوف نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے۔ تشریح اگر شہوت نہ ہو تو عورت کا چہرہ اور اس کا ہاتھ دیکھنا جائز ہے لیکن چھوٹا جائز نہیں ہے کیوں؟ اس لئے کہ ضرورت نہیں اور اس میں ابتلاء عام نہیں ہے اور دیکھنے میں ضرورت بھی ہے اور بلوی بھی ہے نیز یہاں ایسی نص بھی موجود ہے جو چھونے کی حرمت پر دال ہے اور وہ نص محترم یا حدیث ہے کہ جس نے کسی ایسی عورت کو چھویا کہ جس کو چھونا شرعاً جائز نہیں (یعنی وہ اس کی بیوی ہے نہ باندی) تو قیامت کے دن اس کے ہاتھ پر انگارے رکھے جائیں گے اور یہ چھونے کی حرمت جب ہے جبکہ وہ اجنبیہ عورت جوان ہو جس کی جانب طبیعت کا میلان ہوتا ہے لیکن اگر وہ بڑھیا ہو یعنی ایسی کر کی ہو کہ اس کی جانب طبیعت کا میلان نہ ہو سکے تو اس کے ساتھ مصافحہ کرنے اور اس کا ہاتھ چھونے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے کیونکہ فتنہ کا خوف نہیں ہے۔
Ruling on touching the face and palm. It is not permissible for him to touch her face or her palm, even if he is safe from desire, because of the presence of mahram (prohibition) and the lack of necessity and widespread need, unlike looking because there is widespread need. The prohibiting (text) is his saying, peace be upon him: 'Whoever touches a woman's hand without being lawful to him, a burning coal will be placed on his palm on the Day of Judgment.' This (ruling) is when she is a young woman who is desired. As for an old woman who is not desired, there is no harm in shaking her hand or touching her hand because there is no fear of fitna. Explanation: If there is no desire, looking at a woman's face and hand is permissible, but touching is not permissible, why? Because there is no need and no widespread necessity. Looking, however, has need and widespread necessity. Also, there is a text indicating the prohibition of touching, which is the hadith that whoever touches a woman who is not lawful to him (i.e., she is not his wife or slave), burning coals will be placed on his hand on the Day of Judgment. This prohibition of touching applies when the foreign woman is young and naturally inclined towards, but if she is old, i.e., such that nature does not incline towards her, then shaking her hand and touching her hand are not problematic because there is no fear of fitna.
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This passage contains a ruling with proof from hadith. The ruling distinguishes between looking and touching: looking at a woman's face and hands is permissible if safe from desire because of widespread need, but touching is not permissible even without desire due to the explicit hadith prohibition. The exception is an old woman who is not desired, where touching (e.g., handshake) is permissible. The commentary explains the rationale: necessity and widespread need exist for looking but not for touching, and the hadith directly prohibits touching.

Key Terms
مس (mass): Touching, specifically physical contact with a non-mahram woman.
محرم (muharram): Prohibited; the legal status of an action being haram.
بلاوی (balwa): Widespread need or common occurrence; a factor in permissibility.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is touching a non-mahram woman's face haram even if safe from desire, while looking is permissible?
A) Because touching is more intimate
B) Because there is no widespread need for touching
C) Because the hadith specifically prohibits touching
D) Both B and C

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, touching a non-mahram woman's face or palm is haram due to explicit hadith, regardless of desire, while looking is permissible due to widespread need; the exception is an old woman not desired.

Shaking Hands with an Old Woman: The Condition of Fitna
Ruling on shaking hands with an old woman when no fitna feared

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on shaking hands with an old woman and identify the condition that changes the ruling from permissible to prohibited.

Core Idea
Shaking hands with an old woman is permissible only when there is no fear of fitna.

Many assume all physical contact with non-mahram is absolutely prohibited. This lesson examines a specific Hanafi ruling that allows shaking hands with an elderly woman when the risk of temptation (fitna) is absent. The ruling is based on the practice of the Companions, providing a nuanced understanding of the school's approach to gender interaction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The act is musafaha (shaking hands) with an old woman. State the default ruling according to the passage: permissible (mubah) under a condition.
2
Identify the Condition
The condition is the absence of fitna – no fear of sexual temptation from either side. If fitna is feared, the act becomes prohibited (haram).
Fitna is the overriding factor.
3
Cite the Proof (Dalil)
The proof is the practice of the Companions: Abu Bakr shook hands with elderly women, and Abdullah ibn al-Zubayr hired an old woman to care for him, allowing physical contact. This shows permissibility when fitna is absent.
This is a qawl sahabi (Companion's action) used as evidence.
4
Compare with the Opposite Scenario
If the woman is young and desire is possible, or if one is not safe from fitna, the ruling flips to prohibition due to 'exposure to fitna' (ta'rid li'l-fitna).
The same principle applies if the man is old and the woman young but both safe.
5
Understand the Thamarah (Practical Consequence)
The practical outcome: an old woman can be greeted with a handshake in a socially appropriate context, but a young non-mahram woman cannot. This distinction is based on the risk of fitna, not on a blanket prohibition.
This ruling is specific to Hanafi fiqh; other schools may differ.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بوڑھی عورت سے مصافحہ اور چھونا جائز ہے بشرطیکہ فتنہ کا خوف نہ ہو
وقدورى ان ابا بكر رضى الله عنه كان يدخل بعض القبائل التي كان مسترضعا فيهم وكان يصافح العجائز وعبد الله بن الزبير رضى الله عنه استاجر عجوزا لتمرضه و كانت تغمز رجله وتفلى راسه وكذا اذا كان شیخا يامن على نفسه وعليها لما قلنا وان كان لا يامن عليها لا تحل مصافحتها لمافيه من التعريض للفتنة
ترجمہ اور مروی ہے کہ ابو بکر البعض ان قبیلوں میں تشریف لے جاتے جس میں آپ نے دودھ پیا تھا اور بوڑھی عورتوں سے مصافحہ کرتے تھے اور عبد اللہ بن زبیر نے ایک بڑھیا کو نو کر رکھا تھا تا کہ ان کی تیمارداری کرے وہ ان کے پیر دباتی تھی اور ان کے سر میں جوئیں ڈھوندتی تھی اور ایسے ہی ( حلال ہے ) جب کہ مرد ایسا بوڑھا ہو جو اپنے نفس پر مامون ہو اور عورت کے اوپر مامون ہو اسی دلیل کی وجہ سے جود کہ ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں ( یعنی فتنہ کا خوف نہیں ہے ) اور اگر عورت کے اوپر امن نہیں ہے تو اس سے مصافحہ حلال نہیں ہے بوجہ اس کے کہ اس میں فتنہ پر پیش کرنا ہے۔
تشریح اگر عورت اتنی بوڑھی ہے کہ جانبین سے فتنہ کا خوف نہیں ہے تو مصافحہ کرنا اور اس کا ہاتھ چھونا جائز ہے جیسا کہ حضرت صدیق اکبر اور حضرت عبد اللہ بن زبیر کے فعل سے معلوم ہوا اگر مرد بوڑھا ہو اور عورت جوان ہو لیکن جانبین سے امن ہو تو من جائز ہے۔ اور مصافحہ جائز ہے کیوں کہ یہاں بھی فتنہ کا خوف نہیں ہے۔
اور اگر عورت پر امن نہیں ہے تو چونکہ اس میں غیر کو فتنہ پر پیش کرنا ہے تو یہ حلال نہیں ہے۔
علامہ شامی نے رد المختار ص ۲۳۵ ج ۵ پر اس بحث کی ہے۔
یہاں عبارت ہے لما فيه من التعريض للفتنة اور مجمع الانہر ص ۵۱۹ ج ۲ پر ہے لما فيه من التعرض للفتنة
Shaking hands with an old woman is permissible provided there is no fear of fitna. And it is narrated that Abu Bakr (may Allah be pleased with him) used to enter some of the tribes where he had been nursed and would shake hands with elderly women. And Abdullah ibn al-Zubayr (may Allah be pleased with him) hired an old woman to nurse him, and she would massage his leg and delouse his head. Similarly, (it is permissible) when the man is an old man who is safe concerning himself and concerning her, for what we have said. But if he is not safe concerning her, then shaking her hand is not permissible because it entails exposure to fitna. Translation: And it is narrated that Abu Bakr... Explanation: If the woman is so old that there is no fear of fitna from either side, then shaking hands and touching her hand is permissible, as understood from the actions of Abu Bakr and Abdullah ibn al-Zubayr. If the man is old and the woman is young but both are safe, then it is permissible. And if there is no safety concerning the woman, then because it exposes others to fitna, it is not permissible. Allama Shami discussed this in Radd al-Muhtar (vol. 5, p. 235). The phrase here is 'because it contains exposure to fitna' and in Majma' al-Anhar (vol. 2, p. 519) it is 'because it contains exposure to fitna'.
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling based on the practice of the Companions. It establishes that shaking hands with an old woman who is not desired is permissible because there is no fear of fitna. The examples of Abu Bakr and Ibn al-Zubayr demonstrate this. The ruling also applies to an old man shaking hands with a young woman if both are safe from desire. The key condition is absence of fitna. The passage ends with a reference to later Hanafi authorities confirming the same phrasing.

Key Terms
مصافحہ (musafaha): Shaking hands; physical greeting.
فتنہ (fitna): Temptation or trial, specifically fear of sexual desire or sin.
تعریض للفتنہ (ta'rid li'l-fitna): Exposure or leading to fitna; a reason for prohibition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the key condition that makes shaking hands with an old woman permissible?
A) The woman must be a mahram
B) There must be no fear of fitna
C) The man must be her relative
D) It must be done in public

Key Takeaway
Shaking hands with an old woman is permissible only when both parties are safe from fitna; otherwise it is prohibited due to exposure to temptation.

Ruling on Touching and Looking at a Young Girl
Ruling on a young girl not yet desired

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on touching and looking at a young girl and identify the condition that changes the ruling.

Core Idea
A young girl not yet desired: touching and looking are permissible because no fitna is feared.

This short passage establishes a clear baseline ruling in Hanafi fiqh: physical contact and visual interaction with a pre-pubescent girl who is not yet an object of desire is permissible. The ruling is founded on the absence of fitna (temptation). Understanding this threshold helps distinguish permissible interactions from prohibited ones as the girl grows older.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and ruling
The passage addresses a young girl (saghira) who is not yet capable of being desired (la tush'taha). The ruling: touching her and looking at her is permissible (yubah).
The Arabic term 'yubah' indicates permissibility, not mere allowance.
2
Recognize the legal basis
The reason given is 'li-'adam khawf al-fitna' – because there is no fear of fitna. Fitna here means sexual temptation or disorder. The absence of this risk makes the action lawful.
This is a teleological ruling; the cause ('illa) is the absence of fitna.
3
Identify the threshold condition
The condition that triggers permissibility is that the girl is 'la tush'taha' (not desired). Once she reaches an age where she could be desired, the ruling changes. The passage implies that the prohibition applies when fitna is feared.
In Hanafi fiqh, this threshold is typically before puberty, but it can vary by individual.
4
Note the scope of permissibility
The permissibility covers both looking (al-nazar ilayha) and touching (massuha). It is unconditional within the bounds of Islamic etiquette and necessity.
This does not mean unrestricted leering; it means the basic ruling is halal.

Source Text

ترجمہ اور صغیرہ جب کہ وہ لائق شہوت نہ ہو اس کو چھونا حلال ہے اور اس کی جانب دیکھنا فتنہ کا خوف نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے تشریح اگر چھوٹی بچی ہے جو ابھی حد شہوت کو نہیں پہونچی تو اس کو چھونے اور دیکھنے میں چونکہ فتنہ کا خوف نہیں ہے لہذا یہ سب

Ruling on looking at and touching a young girl. And the young girl, when she is not desired, touching her and looking at her is permissible due to the absence of fear of fitna. Translation: And the young girl, when she is not capable of desire, touching her is halal and looking at her is (halal) due to no fear of fitna. Explanation: If she is a young girl who has not yet reached the age of desire, since there is no fear of fitna in touching and looking at her, therefore all of this is permissible.
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This short passage states a clear ruling: a young girl who is not yet sexually desired (i.e., pre-pubescent) can be touched and looked at without restriction because there is no fear of fitna. This is a straightforward ruling with no additional proof, serving as a memorization anchor.

Key Terms
صغیرہ (saghira): Young girl, specifically one who has not reached the age of desire (shahwa).
لائق شہوت (lā'iq al-shahwa): Capable of being desired; typically refers to post-pubescent females.

Male Doctor Viewing Female Patient’s Private Area
Ruling on necessity-based medical viewing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a male doctor may view a female patient's private area and apply the principle of necessity (darura) to limit exposure.

Core Idea
Necessity permits viewing the awrah only to the exact extent required, no more.

This passage from Al-Hidayah’s Book of Disliked Acts addresses a sensitive but important issue: when may a male doctor look at a female patient’s private area? The default ruling is prohibition, but necessity (darura) creates an exception. The text outlines clear conditions, including preferring a female caregiver, covering all other parts, and lowering the gaze. It also draws analogies to circumcision and enema procedures to illustrate the scope of permission. Understanding these conditions is crucial for applying the Hanafi position correctly in medical contexts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling
The default ruling on looking at a non-mahram woman's awrah is haram. The text establishes an exception based on necessity (darura).
This is a rukhsa (dispensation), not a change in the original ruling.
2
List the conditions for permission
The passage gives three conditions: (1) no female caregiver available, (2) cover all body except the exact affected area, (3) doctor lowers gaze as much as possible. Identify each from the text.
The first condition is a sunnah (preferred), not an absolute requirement.
3
Understand the analogy (qiyas)
The permission is compared to a midwife during circumcision (khitan) — she may look only at the site of cutting. Similarly, a male doctor may look only at the affected area.
The illa (effective cause) is necessity, which limits the permission to the minimum.
4
Apply the principle of limitation
The maxim 'ما ثبت بالضرورة يتقدر بقدرها' (what is established by necessity is limited to its extent) governs. The doctor must not look at or expose any extra area.
This principle applies broadly in Hanafi fiqh.
5
Distinguish additional cases
The text extends the ruling to enema (ih'tiqan) and extreme thinness (hubz fahish) as signs of illness. Note that enema for non-medical purposes (e.g., sexual strength) is not permissible.
This shows the scope of darura in medical contexts.

Book of Disliked Acts. Permissibility for a doctor to look at the affected area of a woman for necessity. And it is appropriate that he instruct a woman to treat her, because looking of one gender to the same gender is easier. If they are unable, then every part of her body is covered except the site of the disease, then he looks and lowers his gaze as much as he can, because what is established by necessity is limited to its extent. And it becomes like the looking of the clitoris cutter and the circumciser. Similarly, it is permissible for a man to look at the site of enema of a man because it is a treatment that is permissible for illness. And similarly for extreme thinness, as narrated from Abu Yusuf, because it is a sign of illness. Then translation and commentary in Urdu.
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage from the Book of Disliked Acts addresses the permissibility of a male doctor viewing a female patient's private area for medical treatment. The ruling is established by necessity (darura). The primary principle is that only the minimum necessary area may be exposed. The doctor should first try to have a female caregiver handle the treatment, as same-gender looking is less problematic. If no female is available, all of the woman's body must be covered except the exact site of illness. The doctor must lower his gaze as much as possible. This permission is analogized to the midwife who performs circumcision (khitan) looking only at the site of cutting. Similarly, a male patient may be given an enema by a male practitioner, and extreme thinness (hubz fahish) is treated as a medical sign that permits looking. The passage includes several notes: circumcision is a confirmed sunnah for men and an honor for women, so looking at the genitals for that is permissible due to necessity; enema is a treatment for expelling waste; and an enema done for lust (to gain strength for intercourse) is not permissible. The final note states that circumcision is not an excuse for a person to have another perform it if the adult can do it himself or via his wife or slave-girl; for women it is only an honor, not a sunnah, so abandonment of it is not a sin.

Key Terms
ضرورة (darura): A situation of dire necessity that permits what is normally prohibited, such as looking at the awrah for medical treatment.
عورة (awrah): Body parts that must be concealed; looking at them is normally haram. For a woman, the entire body except face and hands is awrah in front of non-mahram men.
ختان (khitan): Circumcision, a sunnah for men and a recommended act of honor for women. It is used as an analogy for medical looking at the genitals.
احتقان (ihtiqan): Enema: the insertion of medicine into the anus for treatment. The text permits looking at the site for enema due to medical necessity.
هزال فاحش (hubz fahish): Extreme thinness, considered a sign of illness that may necessitate medical examination, as narrated from Abu Yusuf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The doctor must cover his own eyes
B) The doctor should seek a female caregiver to treat her
C) The doctor can directly examine the area
D) The doctor must obtain a fatwa

Key Takeaway
Necessity permits a male doctor to view only the exact affected area of a female patient, with all other parts covered and gaze lowered, reflecting the principle that darura is limited to its extent.

Determining a Man's Awrah Before Another Man
Determination of awrah based on hadith and refutation of opposing views

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on which parts of a man's body constitute awrah before another man, identify the primary hadith evidence, and explain why the navel is excluded while the knee and thigh are included.

Core Idea
A man's awrah before another man is from below the navel to below the knee, with navel excluded and knee included.

This lesson tackles a fundamental question in Islamic modesty: what parts of a man's body must he cover when in the presence of other men? The Hanafi school provides a clear definition based on explicit hadith, but there are notable differences with other madhhabs on the inclusion of the navel, knee, and thigh. Understanding the textual proofs and the methodology of reconciling conflicting narrations is essential for proper practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act under discussion is looking at another man's body. Determine the default ruling (permissible) and the exception (the awrah).
The ruling is not about covering per se, but about permissible looking; however, the definition of awrah implies obligation to cover.
2
Locate the primary proof
The text cites the hadith: 'عورة الرجل ما بين سرته إلى ركبته' (The awrah of a man is what is between his navel and his knee). Identify the chain of transmission (Abu Hurayra) and its strength (zanni al-thubut).
This hadith is the cornerstone for the Hanafi position.
3
Analyze the variant narration
A second version: 'مادون سرته حتى تجاوز ركبته' (below his navel until it exceeds his knee). Understand how this variant clarifies that the navel itself is excluded. The author uses this to refute those who include the navel.
The word 'مادون' (below) explicitly excludes the navel.
4
Examine the inclusion of the knee and thigh
The author brings additional proof that the knee is part of the awrah (hadith 'الركبة من العورة') and that the thigh is awrah (hadith to Jarhad). Note the principle used: when prohibitive and permissive evidence conflict, the prohibitive prevails.
The knee is specifically mentioned as awrah, and the thigh is included by explicit statement.
5
Refute opposing views and custom argument
The text refutes al-Kamari's reliance on custom (urf) to exclude the area below the navel. Learn the principle that custom cannot override an explicit nass. Compare with Shafi'i and Zahiri positions.
This step emphasizes that textual evidence takes precedence over customary practice.

Source Text

تشریح مرد کی عورت ناف کے نیچے سے گھٹنے تک ہے یعنی گھٹنہ عورت میں داخل ہے اور ناف داخل نہیں ہے ابو عصمہ اور شافعی ناف کو عورت کہتے ہیں اور شافعی گھٹنہ کو عورت نہیں کہتے اور اصحاب ظواہر ان کو عورت نہیں کہتے، اور امام ابوبکر محمد بن فضل الکماری ناف سے نیچے والے حصہ کو بھی عورت نہیں کہتے اور وہ کہتے ہیں کہ لوگوں میں اس کے کھولنے کی عادت ہے مصنف نے جواب دیا کہ عادت اسی وقت مخصص ہو سکتی ہے جب کہ اس کے خلاف نص موجود نہ ہوتی اور یہاں اس کے خلاف نص موجود ہے۔
گھٹنہ عورت (شرمگاہ) ہے یا نہیں
وقد روى أبو هريرة رضى الله عنه عن النبي عليه السلام انه قال الركبة من العورة وابدى الحسن بن على رضى الله عنهما سرته فقبلها ابو هريرة رضى الله عنه وقال عليه السلام لجرهد وار فخذك اما علمت ان الفخذ عورة ولان الركبة ملتقى عظم الفخذ والساق فاجتمع المحرم والمبيح وفي مثله يغلب المحرم وحكم
What parts of a man's body is it permissible for a man to see? He (al-Quduri) said: And a man looks at all of another man's body except what is between his navel to his knee, due to his statement (peace be upon him): The awrah of a man is what is between his navel to his knee. And it is narrated: Below his navel until it exceeds his knee. By this it is established that the navel is not awrah, contrary to what Abu 'Isma and al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on them) say. And the knee is awrah, contrary to what al-Shafi'i said. And the thigh is awrah, contrary to the Zahiris. And what is below the navel to the hairline is awrah, contrary to what Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Fadl al-Kamari says, relying on custom, because custom is not considered when there is text to the contrary.
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage discusses the awrah of a man when seen by another man. It begins by quoting al-Quduri's matn: a man may look at all parts of another man's body except from the navel to the knee. This is based on the hadith 'The awrah of a man is what is between his navel to his knee.' A second narration includes 'below his navel until it exceeds the knee,' which clarifies that the navel itself is not part of the awrah. The commentary then refutes several opposing views: Abu 'Isma and al-Shafi'i consider the navel as awrah, but the Hanafi position is that it is not. Al-Shafi'i also does not consider the knee as awrah, but the Hanafis hold it is. The Zahiris (al-Ashab al-Zawahir) do not consider the thigh as awrah, but the Hanafis hold it is. Imam Abu Bakr al-Kamari argued that the area below the navel to the pubic hair is not awrah because of custom (people commonly expose it). The author rejects this, stating that custom cannot override an explicit text (nass). Then a section specifically asks whether the knee is awrah and brings a hadith from Abu Hurayra that the Prophet said 'The knee is part of the awrah.' Also, the Prophet told Jarhad to cover his thigh, saying 'Do you not know that the thigh is awrah?' It also mentions that al-Hasan ibn 'Ali exposed his navel and Abu Hurayra kissed it, indicating the navel is not awrah. The passage concludes with a legal maxim: when there is a conflict between a prohibited and a permissible, the prohibited prevails.

Key Terms
عورة (awrah): Body parts that must be concealed; looking at them is haram. For a man amongst men, it is from below the navel to below the knee (including knee and thigh).
سرة (surrah): The navel. In this ruling, it is explicitly stated not to be part of the awrah.
ركبة (rukbah): The knee. According to the Hanafi school, the knee is part of the awrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following body parts of a man is NOT part of the awrah when looking at another man?
A) The thigh
B) The knee
C) The navel
D) The area below the navel to the pubic hair

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defines a man's awrah as from below the navel to below the knee, based on explicit hadith, and rejects custom as a basis for overriding nass.

Circumcision Not an Excuse for Marital Obligations
Tanbih denying circumcision as an excuse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that circumcision is not a valid excuse for delaying marriage or intercourse in Hanafi fiqh, and explain the reasoning based on the tanbih.

Core Idea
Circumcision is not an excuse to avoid marriage; adults can arrange it independently.

In this brief tanbih, the commentator addresses a common misconception: that being uncircumcised can delay or prevent marriage or intimacy. The passage clarifies that this is not a valid excuse, because a mature person can circumcise themselves or have their spouse do it. For women, circumcision is only a makrumah (noble act), not a sunnah, so its absence is even less of a barrier. The note also mentions a lenient view from 'Allama 'Ayni, but the relied-upon position is clear.

Guided Path
1
Identify the excuse claim
The passage addresses the claim that uncircumcised status is a valid excuse (udhr) to avoid marriage or intercourse.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The ruling is that circumcision is NOT a valid excuse for either men or women.
The text explicitly denies it as an excuse.
3
Explain the reasoning for men
An adult male can circumcise himself, marry and have his wife circumcise him, or buy a slave girl to do it. Thus, it is not a barrier.
The text gives practical alternatives.
4
Explain the reasoning for women
For women, circumcision is only a makrumah (noble deed), not a sunnah. Its absence does not create any obligation or excuse.
This distinguishes the status between genders.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi nuance
'Allama 'Ayni's view that omission is impermissible for both is considered tasamuh (lenient); the relied-upon position is that it is not obligatory for women.
See Shami for details.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبیه ۳ سلب الانہر ص ۴۶۲ ج ۲ پر ہے کہ ختان کوئی عذر نہیں ہے کیونکہ بالغ اپنی ختنہ خود کر سکتا ہے یا نکاح کرلے اور اپنی بیوئی سے ختنہ کرالے یا باندی خرید لے اور اس سے ختنہ کرالے قلٹ ایسے ہی عورتوں کے حق میں بھی کوئی عذر نہیں ہے کیوں کہ ان کے حق میں یه صرف مکرمت ہے نہ کہ سنت علامہ عینی کا یہ فرمان کہ مرد اور عورت دونوں کے لئے اس کا ترک جائز نہیں تسامح ہے، ملاحظہ ہو شامی ص ۳۳۷ ج ۵
Note 3: In Sallab al-Anhr, page 462, volume 2, it states that circumcision is not an excuse because a mature person can circumcise himself, or marry and have his wife circumcise him, or buy a slave girl and have her circumcise him. Rather, the same applies to women: it is no excuse for them either, because for them it is only a noble deed and not a sunnah. The statement of 'Allama 'Ayni that its omission is not permissible for both men and women is lenient. See Shami, page 337, volume 5.
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage is a tanbih (cautionary note) from the commentator, stating that lack of circumcision is not a valid excuse to refrain from marriage or sexual intercourse. The text explains that an adult male can circumcise himself, or have his wife or slave girl do it. Similarly, for women, circumcision is considered a makrumah (noble act) rather than a sunnah, so its absence does not exempt them from obligations. The commentator notes that 'Allama 'Ayni's view that omission is impermissible for both is considered tasamuh (tolerance) and not the relied-upon position, referring to Shami for details.

Key Terms
ختان (khitan): Circumcision; the removal of the foreskin.
عذر (udhr): A valid excuse that permits exemption from an obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is a valid excuse for men only.
B) It is not a valid excuse for anyone.
C) It is a valid excuse for women only.
D) It is a valid excuse only if one cannot afford a circumciser.

Key Takeaway
Lack of circumcision is not a valid excuse to avoid marriage or intercourse; adults can arrange it themselves or through their spouse.

Tanbih prohibiting non-medical enema use.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on using an enema for sexual strength and identify the condition that makes it impermissible.

Core Idea
Taking an enema solely for sexual strength is not halal in the Hanafi school — only medical use is permitted.

This tanbih from the Hanafi fiqh tradition addresses a specific case: using an enema (huqnah) not for illness but to boost sexual potency. The ruling is clear that such use is not permissible. Understanding this ruling helps distinguish between permissible medical treatments and prohibited uses that seek worldly benefits through potentially harmful means.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
The act is administering an enema for a non-medical purpose: to gain strength for intercourse. Note that the enema is not due to illness but 'for benefit'.
2
State the ruling
According to the Hanafi school, this is not halal (impermissible). The ruling is conditional: if for illness, it is permissible; if for mere benefit (as here), it is not.
The sources cited are al-Dhakhira and Shami.

This is because such use is not for treatment but for a worldly benefit that may involve harm or wastage.

Pressing Thigh with Thick Barrier: Ruling and Precaution
Tanbih permitting pressing/rubbing the thigh over a thick garment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on pressing another's thigh with a thick barrier and identify the precaution.

Core Idea
Pressing the thigh is permissible only with a thick barrier, yet caution is advised.

This short note from al-Hidayah addresses a common scenario of physical contact between men. While direct thigh contact is prohibited, a thick garment changes the ruling to permissible. However, the text adds a note of precaution, showing the school's concern for preventing temptations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The act is pressing or rubbing another man's thigh.
This is a form of physical contact that normally is prohibited if direct.
2
Identify the condition
A thick garment (motaa izaar) must be a barrier between the hands and the thigh.
The thickness prevents direct sensation.
3
State the ruling
The act is permissible (ja'iz) under this condition.
This is the explicit ruling from the tanbih.
4
Note the precaution
Despite permissibility, it is better to abstain (al-ahwat tark).
This indicates the act is discouraged (makruh tanzih) as a precaution.
5
Understand the wisdom
The precaution is based on blocking means to prohibited acts (sadd al-dhara'i), even with a barrier, to avoid any risk of temptation or direct contact.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبیه - ۱ اگر ران دبائی جائیں اور درمیان میں موٹا ازار حائل ہو تو جائز ہے کذا قال العینی سکب الانہر ص ۴۶۳ ج ۲ پر ہے و جاز غمر فخذه فوق ازار كشف والا لا والاحوط تركة
Note 1: If the thigh is pressed and a thick garment is a barrier in between, then it is permissible. Thus said al-'Ayni. In Sallab al-Anhr, page 463, volume 2: 'It is permissible to press his thigh over a garment uncovered? Otherwise no, and the precaution is to leave it.'
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This tanbih addresses a specific scenario: pressing or rubbing another man's thigh. If there is a thick garment intervening, such that direct skin contact is avoided, the act is permissible. The authority cited is al-'Ayni and the text Sallab al-Anhr. However, the precaution (al-ahwat) is to refrain from it even with a barrier. This reflects the general principle of avoiding close contact that may lead to prohibited acts.

Key Terms
ازار (izar): A lower garment, wrap, or cloth used to cover the lower body.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Looking at the Wife’s Private Part During Intercourse
Ruling with two opinions on looking during intercourse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conflicting opinions regarding looking at the wife’s private part during intercourse and identify the preferred view according to later Hanafi scholars.

Core Idea
Looking during intercourse: recommended for pleasure vs. disliked due to forgetfulness – both views exist.

Among the issues of marital intimacy, Hanafi fiqh discusses whether a husband should look at his wife’s private part during intercourse. This lesson presents two opinions from later sources and helps you understand the reasoning behind each view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act in question
Looking at the wife’s private parts during intercourse.
2
State the two opinions
Opinion 1: It is better (اولیٰ) to look to increase pleasure. Opinion 2: It is not to be looked because it causes forgetfulness (مورث نسیان).
3
Determine the basis of each opinion
The first opinion focuses on enhancing marital pleasure; the second on potential distraction from worship.
4
Recognize that there is no explicit tarjih in the text
The passage simply reports both views from Majma‘ al-Anhar and Fatawa Hindiyya, without a clear preference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الكراهية
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو بدایہ جلد ۱۳ صاحب نے فرمایا کہ اس میں کچھ حرج نہیں اور مجھے یہ امید ہے کہ اس میں اجر ملے گا کذافی الخلاصہ ، فتاویٰ ہندیہ ص ۳۲۸ ج ۵ تنبیہ - بعض حضرات نے کہا ہے کہ جماع کے وقت بیوی کی شرم گاہ دیکھنا اولیٰ ہے تا کہ لذت میں اضافہ ہو، اور بعض نے کہا کہ یہ مورث نسیان ہے اس لئے نہ دیکھے، مجمع الانہر ص ۵۱۸ ج ۲ تنبیه - ۴ بیٹے کے لئے جائز ہے کہ خدمت کی غرض سے اپنی ماں کا پیٹ اور کمر دبائے کپڑے کے اوپر سے فتاویٰ ہندیہ ص ۳۲۸ ج ۵، کپڑے کے اوپر سے ران دبانا جائز ہے، کذا قال الفقیہ ابو جعفر فتاوی ہندیہ ص ۳۲۷ ج ۵
تنبیہ - وہ لڑکا جو خوبصورت ہو تو وہ عورتوں کے حکم میں ہے اس کی طرف شہوت سے دیکھنا جائز نہیں ہے البتہ بغیر شہوت کے دیکھنا اور خلوت جائز ہے اس وجہ سے اس کو نقاب کا حکم نہیں دیا گیا ہے فتاویٰ ہندیہ ص ۳۳۰ ج ۵ ۔
تنبیه - جماع کے لئے بیوی کونگی کرنے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے فتاویٰ ہندیہ ص ۳۲۸ ج ۰۵
There is no harm in it, and I hope there will be reward in it. As in al-Khulasa, Fatawa Hindiyya. Warning: Some scholars said that looking at the wife’s private part during intercourse is better to increase pleasure, and some said it causes forgetfulness so he should not look. Majma‘ al-Anhar. Warning: For a son, it is permissible to massage his mother’s belly and back for the purpose of service, over the cloth. Fatawa Hindiyya. Massaging the thigh over the cloth is permissible, as stated by Faqih Abu Ja‘far. Warning: A handsome boy is in the ruling of women; looking at him with lust is not permissible. However, looking without lust and being alone with him is permissible. For this reason, he is not given the ruling of wearing a veil. Fatawa Hindiyya. Warning: There is no harm in having intercourse with the wife from behind (or in the qibla direction?). Fatawa Hindiyya.
Source pages p. 338

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of several short rulings (fatawa) from later Hanafi sources such as Fatawa Hindiyya and Majma‘ al-Anhar. The first ruling concerns looking at the wife’s private parts during intercourse: there is a difference of opinion among scholars—some consider it better for increasing pleasure, while others warn it may lead to forgetfulness. The second ruling permits a son to massage his mother’s belly and back over the cloth for the purpose of service, and similarly pressing the thigh is allowed. The third ruling treats a handsome beardless boy like a woman regarding gaze: looking with desire is unlawful, but without desire it is permissible, and khalwa (seclusion) is also allowed. The fourth ruling states that there is no harm in intercourse with the wife from behind (interpreted as facing the qibla or from the back permissibility? The term 'كونگي' is unclear; it may refer to the position). All rulings are based on the absence of lust or proper intent.

Key Terms
خلوت (khalwah): Being alone with a non-mahram of the opposite sex in a place where privacy is possible.
نقاب (niqab): Face veil; here, the ruling of requiring a veil is not applied to a handsome boy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is absolutely forbidden.
B) There is a difference of opinion.
C) It is obligatory.
D) It is recommended without difference.

Key Takeaway
Looking at the wife's private part during intercourse is subject to scholarly difference; no single Hanafi ruling is definitive.

Looking at a Handsome Beardless Boy
Ruling on looking at a handsome boy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between permissible and impermissible looking at a handsome boy based on the presence of lust, and state the ruling on seclusion with him.

Core Idea
A handsome boy is like a woman regarding gaze: lustful looking is haram, but without lust it is permissible.

The category of 'amrad' (beardless boy) has specific rulings in Hanafi fiqh. This lesson clarifies that a handsome boy is treated like a woman in terms of covering and gaze: looking with desire is forbidden, but looking without desire and even seclusion are allowed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject: a handsome boy (صبي جميل)
The text refers to a boy who is handsome and beardless.
2
Note the classification: he is in the ruling of women
This means he is treated like a non-mahram woman regarding the obligation of covering and prohibition of lustful gaze.
3
Understand the rulings: looking with lust is haram, without lust is halal
The text explicitly says looking with lust is not permissible, but without lust it is permissible.
4
Note the ruling on khalwa (seclusion): permissible without lust
Being alone with him is allowed, unlike with a non-mahram woman.
5
Explain why niqab is not required for him
Because the obligation of covering the face applies only to women.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الكراهية
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو بدایہ جلد ۱۳ صاحب نے فرمایا کہ اس میں کچھ حرج نہیں اور مجھے یہ امید ہے کہ اس میں اجر ملے گا کذافی الخلاصہ ، فتاویٰ ہندیہ ص ۳۲۸ ج ۵ تنبیہ - بعض حضرات نے کہا ہے کہ جماع کے وقت بیوی کی شرم گاہ دیکھنا اولیٰ ہے تا کہ لذت میں اضافہ ہو، اور بعض نے کہا کہ یہ مورث نسیان ہے اس لئے نہ دیکھے، مجمع الانہر ص ۵۱۸ ج ۲ تنبیه - ۴ بیٹے کے لئے جائز ہے کہ خدمت کی غرض سے اپنی ماں کا پیٹ اور کمر دبائے کپڑے کے اوپر سے فتاویٰ ہندیہ ص ۳۲۸ ج ۵، کپڑے کے اوپر سے ران دبانا جائز ہے، کذا قال الفقیہ ابو جعفر فتاوی ہندیہ ص ۳۲۷ ج ۵
تنبیہ - وہ لڑکا جو خوبصورت ہو تو وہ عورتوں کے حکم میں ہے اس کی طرف شہوت سے دیکھنا جائز نہیں ہے البتہ بغیر شہوت کے دیکھنا اور خلوت جائز ہے اس وجہ سے اس کو نقاب کا حکم نہیں دیا گیا ہے فتاویٰ ہندیہ ص ۳۳۰ ج ۵ ۔
تنبیه - جماع کے لئے بیوی کونگی کرنے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے فتاویٰ ہندیہ ص ۳۲۸ ج ۰۵
There is no harm in it, and I hope there will be reward in it. As in al-Khulasa, Fatawa Hindiyya. Warning: Some scholars said that looking at the wife’s private part during intercourse is better to increase pleasure, and some said it causes forgetfulness so he should not look. Majma‘ al-Anhar. Warning: For a son, it is permissible to massage his mother’s belly and back for the purpose of service, over the cloth. Fatawa Hindiyya. Massaging the thigh over the cloth is permissible, as stated by Faqih Abu Ja‘far. Warning: A handsome boy is in the ruling of women; looking at him with lust is not permissible. However, looking without lust and being alone with him is permissible. For this reason, he is not given the ruling of wearing a veil. Fatawa Hindiyya. Warning: There is no harm in having intercourse with the wife from behind (or in the qibla direction?). Fatawa Hindiyya.
Source pages p. 338

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of several short rulings (fatawa) from later Hanafi sources such as Fatawa Hindiyya and Majma‘ al-Anhar. The first ruling concerns looking at the wife’s private parts during intercourse: there is a difference of opinion among scholars—some consider it better for increasing pleasure, while others warn it may lead to forgetfulness. The second ruling permits a son to massage his mother’s belly and back over the cloth for the purpose of service, and similarly pressing the thigh is allowed. The third ruling treats a handsome beardless boy like a woman regarding gaze: looking with desire is unlawful, but without desire it is permissible, and khalwa (seclusion) is also allowed. The fourth ruling states that there is no harm in intercourse with the wife from behind (interpreted as facing the qibla or from the back permissibility? The term 'كونگي' is unclear; it may refer to the position). All rulings are based on the absence of lust or proper intent.

Key Terms
خلوت (khalwah): Being alone with a non-mahram of the opposite sex in a place where privacy is possible.
نقاب (niqab): Face veil; here, the ruling of requiring a veil is not applied to a handsome boy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why is a handsome boy not required to wear a niqab?
A) Because he is mahram.
B) Because the obligation of niqab is only for women.
C) Because he is always with a chaperone.
D) The text does not give a reason.

Key Takeaway
A handsome boy is like a woman only for lustful gaze; without lust, looking and seclusion are permissible, and he does not wear niqab.

Intercourse with Wife from Behind: Permissibility
Ruling on intercourse position

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on having intercourse with the wife from behind (ad al-dubur) based on the text.

Core Idea
Intercourse with the wife from the back is permissible as long as it is in the proper place (vagina).

There is a common misconception about the ruling of anal intercourse in Islam. This lesson clarifies that while anal intercourse is strictly prohibited, having intercourse with the wife from behind (i.e., from the back but through the vagina) is permissible. The text uses the term 'کونگی' which may refer to 'dubur' but likely means 'قبلی' (front) or a position. We interpret it as permissibility of back entry.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act: 'جماع کے لئے بیوی کونگی کرنے'.
The phrase is ambiguous; 'کونگی' may be a typo for 'قبلی' (facing qibla) or 'دبری' (from behind). Based on context and other Hanafi sources, it is generally interpreted as having intercourse from the back (i.e., vaginal intercourse from behind).
2
Note the ruling: 'کوئی حرج نہیں' – There is no harm.
This indicates permissibility.
3
Understand the restriction: Anal intercourse is haram, but vaginal intercourse from behind is allowed.
The text implies that as long as the place of penetration is the vagina, the position does not matter.
