Rulings on Looking Between Genders: Woman Looking at Man's Belly and Back
Detailed discussion of looking between genders with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a woman looking at a non-mahram man's belly and back, distinguish between the views of al-Quduri and al-Mabsut, and identify the mufta bihi position with its rationale.

Core Idea
Looking at non-awrah parts is permissible without lust, but lust changes the ruling: man = haram, woman = makruh tanzihi.

This passage explores the delicate fiqh of gaze between genders. It begins with a permissive ruling from al-Quduri, then a stricter one from al-Mabsut, and reconciles them by focusing on the presence or absence of lust (shahwah). The distinction between men and women hinges on the predominance of shahwah in women, which is considered virtually present.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the two Hanafi rulings
The act is a woman looking at a non-mahram man's belly and back. Al-Quduri says it's permissible (ja'iz) when safe from lust. Al-Mabsut says it's like a man looking at his mahram – impermissible.
Both are from authoritative sources: Mukhtasar al-Quduri and al-Mabsut (Kitab al-Khuntha).
2
Analyse the condition of shahwah (lust)
The permissibility is conditional on the absence of lust. If the woman has lust, or fears it, the ruling changes: she should lower her gaze (recommended, not haram). For a man, if he has lust, it is haram.
The text uses 'yastahibbu' for woman (recommended) and 'haram' for man.
3
Understand the rationale for the gender difference
Lust is predominant in women, so it is considered virtually present (i'tibari). Thus when a man lusts, both sides have lust (virtual in her, actual in him), making sin more likely. When a woman lusts, only she has lust, so the risk is lower.
The phrase 'al-shahwah 'alayhinna ghalibah' (lust is predominant in women) is key.
4
Resolve the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf
Al-Quduri's view is limited to cases with full safety from fitna. Al-Mabsut's view is cautious. The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is that a woman should lower her gaze if any fear of lust exists.
The author reconciles by specifying conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عورت کیلئے مرد کا کتنا بدن دیکھنے کی گنجائش ہے
قال ويجوز للمرأة ان تنظر من الرجل الى ما نظر الرجل اليه منه اذا امنت الشهوة لا ستواء الرجل والمراة فى النظر ما ليس بعورة كالشباب والدواب
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جائز ہے عورت کے لئے کہ وہ دیکھے مرد کے اس بدن کو جس کو دوسرا مرد دیکھ سکتا ہے جب کہ عورت شہوت سے مامون ہو مرد اور عورت کے برابر ہونے کی وجہ سے اس چیز کو دیکھنے میں جو عورت نہیں ہے جیسے کپڑا اور سواریاں ۔
تشریح مرد کے بدن کا جو حصہ دوسرا مر د یکھ سکتا ہے اس کو عورت بھی دیکھ سکتی ہے یعنی اس کا پیٹ اور پیٹھ بشرطیکہ شہوت نہ ہو کیونکہ جو حصہ عورت نہیں اس میں مرد و عورت برابر ہیں جیسے سواری اور کپڑوں کا حکم ہے کہ وہ عورت نہیں ہے لہذا مرد عورت کے کپڑے اور سواری دیکھ سکتا ہے اور عورت مرد کی سواری اور کپڑے دیکھ سکتی ہے۔
عورت کے لئے اجنبی مرد کا پیٹ اور پیٹھ دیکھنے کا حکم
وفى كتاب الخنثى من الأصل ان نظر المرأة الى الرجل الاجنبى بمنزلة نظر الرجل الى محارمه لان النظر الى خلاف الجنس اغلظ الكان في قلبها شهوة او اكبر رأيها انها تشتهى اوشكت في ذلك يستحب لها ان تغض بصرها
ترجمہ اور مبسوط کی کتاب الخلفی میں ہے کہ عورت کا دیکھنا اجنبی مرد کی جانب مرد کے دیکھنے کے درجہ میں ہے اپنے محارم کی جانب اس لئے خلاف جنس کی جانب دیکھنا سخت ہے پس اگر عورت کے دل میں شہوت ہو یا اس کا غالب گمان ہو کہ شہوت ہو جائے گی یا وہ شک کرے اس میں تو اس کے لئے مستحب ہے کہ اپنی نظر کو بند کرے۔ تشریح یہاں ایک مسئلہ تو وہ ہے جس کو قدوری نے ذکر کیا ہے جو ، اقبل میں گذرا ہے لیکن مبسوط کی کتاب الخنثی میں مسئلہ اس طرح
بيان کیا ہے کہ جیسے مرد کے لئے جائز نہیں کہ اپنی محارم کا پیٹ یا پیٹھ دیکھے ایسے ہی عورت کے لئے جائز نہیں کہ وہ اجنبی مرد کا پیٹ اور پیٹھ دیھے۔
اور دلیل یہ بیان کی ہے کہ خلاف جنس کی جانب دیکھنا زیادہ خطر ناک ہے جنس کی جانب دیکھنے کے مقابلہ میں ( کما ہو ظاہر ) اور یہ تفصیل اس وقت ہے جب کہ عورت شہوت سے مامون ہو ورنہ اگر اس کے قلب میں شہوت ہو یا شہوت کا غالب گمان ہو یا شہوت کا شک ہو تو اس لئے نہ دیکھنا مستحب ہے یعنی حرام نہیں اور اگر مرد میں یہ کیفیت ہو تو اس لئے دیکھنا حرام ہے جس کی مصنف آگے دلیل دے رہے ہیں۔
مرد کیلئے اجنبی عورت کا پیٹ اور پیٹھ دیکھنے کا حکم
ولو كان الناظر هو الرجل اليها وهو بهذه الصفة لم ينظرو وهذا اشارة الى التحريم
ترجمہ اور اگر عورت کی جانب مردد یکھنے والا ہو اور مرد اس صفت پر ہو ( یعنی اس کو شہوت ہو ) تو وہ نہیں دیکھے گا اور یہ اشارہ ہے تحریم کی جانب۔
تشریح نہ دیکھنے کا استحساب عورت کے حق میں ہے اور مرد کے حق میں عدم جواز ہے۔
وجہ فرق
ووجه الفرق ان الشهوة عليهن غالبة وهو كالمتحقق اعتبارا فاذا اشتهى الرجل كانت الشهوة من الجانبين موجودة ولا كذلك اذا اشتهت المرأة لان الشهوة غير موجودة في جانبه حقيقة واعتباراً فكانت من جانب واحد والمتحقق من الجانبين فى الافضاء الى المحرم اقوى من المتحقق في جانب واحد
ترجمہ اور وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ عورتوں پر شہوت غالب ہے او سبلحاظ اعتبار غالب مثل متحقیق کے ہے تو جب مرد کو شہوت ہوگئی تو شہوت جانہین سے موجود ہوئی اور نہیں ہے ایسا جب کہ عورت کو شہوت ہو اس لئے کہ شہوت مرد کی جانب میں نہ بلحاظ حقیقت ہے اور نہ بلحاظ اعتبار تو شہوت ایک جانب میں ہوگی اور جو شہوت جائین سے متحقق ہے وہ حرام تک پہونچانے میں زیادہ قوی ہے اس شہوت سے جو ایک جانب سے ہے۔
تشریح عورت میں شہوت غالب ہوتی ہے لہذا اعتباری اور حکمی لحاظ سے شہوت ان پر ہر وقت موجود مانی جائے گی اور مرد میں شہوت غالب نہیں ہوتی تو جب تک اس میں حقیقۂ شہوت موجود نہ ہو تو اس میں اعتباری اور حکمی لحاظ سے شہوت نہیں مانی جائے گی۔ جب بات یوں ہے تو اگر عورت میں شہوت ہو تو اس کے لئے نہ دیکھنا مستحب ہے حرام نہیں ہے کیونکہ مرد میں شہوت نہیں ہے تو عورت کی شہوت الی الحرام ہونے کا قومی ذریعہ نہیں ہے۔ اور اگر مردکوشہوت ہو اس کے لئے عورت کی جانب دیکھنا حرام ہے کیونکہ مرد میں تو شہوت ہے ہی اور عورت میں حکمی اور اعتباری لحاظ
How much of a man's body a woman may look at. He (al-Quduri) said: It is permissible for a woman to look at a man's body that a man may look at from him, if she is safe from lust, because men and women are equal in looking at what is not ‘awrah, like clothes and animals. Translation: Al-Quduri said: It is permissible for a woman to look at that part of a man's body which another man can look at, when she is safe from lust, because men and women are equal in looking at what is not ‘awrah, like clothes and riding animals. Commentary: The part of a man's body that another man may see, a woman may also see, i.e., his belly and back, provided there is no lust, because in what is not ‘awrah, men and women are equal, just as the ruling on clothes and riding animals—they are not ‘awrah, so a man may look at a woman's clothes and riding animal, and a woman may look at a man's clothes and riding animal. The ruling for a woman looking at a non-mahram man's belly and back. And in the book of al-Khuntha from al-Asl: The woman's look at a non-mahram man is like a man's look at his mahram, because looking at the opposite gender is more severe. If there is lust in her heart, or she is certain she will lust, or she doubts, then it is recommended for her to lower her gaze. Translation: In al-Mabsut's book al-Khuntha: A woman's look at a non-mahram man is like a man's look at his mahram, because looking at the opposite gender is strict. So if there is lust in her heart, or her overwhelming assumption is that she will lust, or she doubts, then it is recommended for her to lower her gaze. Commentary: One issue is what al-Quduri mentioned in the past, but in al-Mabsut's book al-Khuntha, it is stated as follows: Just as it is not permissible for a man to look at his mahram's belly or back, similarly it is not permissible for a woman to look at a non-mahram man's belly and back. And they gave the proof that looking at the opposite gender is more dangerous than looking at the same gender. And this detail applies when the woman is safe from lust. Otherwise, if there is lust in her heart, or strong presumption, or doubt, then not looking is recommended—i.e., not haram. And if the man has such a condition, then looking is haram, as the author will prove later. The ruling for a man looking at a non-mahram woman's belly and back. And if the looker is the man towards her, and he is in this condition (i.e., he has lust), he will not look, and this indicates prohibition. Translation: And if the looker is the man towards her and he is in this condition (i.e., he has lust), then he will not look, and this points to prohibition. Commentary: Not looking is recommended for women and not permissible for men. The reason for the difference: And the reason for the difference is that lust is predominant in women, and it is considered as if it exists virtually. So when a man lusts, lust is present from both sides, but not so when a woman lusts, because lust is not present from his side in reality or virtually. So it is from one side only. And lust verified from both sides is stronger in leading to haram than lust from one side. Translation: The reason for the difference is that lust is predominant in women, and it is considered as if it is established virtually. So when a man lusts, lust is present from both sides. But it is not so when a woman lusts, because lust is not present from his side in reality or virtually. So it is from one side only. And lust established from both sides is stronger in leading to haram than lust established from one side. Commentary: Lust is predominant in women, so in a virtual and legal sense, lust is always considered present in them. Lust is not predominant in men, so as long as actual lust is not present, it is not considered virtually. Therefore, if a woman has lust, not looking is recommended, not haram, because the man does not have lust, so the woman's lust alone is not a strong means to haram. And if a man has lust, looking at a woman is haram, because he has lust and the woman is considered to have lust virtually.
Source pages p. 338

Commentary
This passage discusses the limits of looking between genders. It opens with a ruling from Imam al-Quduri: a woman may look at a man's body that is not ‘awrah (i.e., the parts a man may show to other men, like the belly and back) provided she is free from lust. This is based on equality in what is not ‘awrah. Then the text contrasts this with a ruling from Imam Muhammad's al-Mabsut (Kitab al-Khuntha) which states that a woman looking at a non-mahram man is like a man looking at his mahram—i.e., it is impermissible to look at the belly and back. The text reconciles these by noting that al-Quduri's ruling applies when lust is absent, while the stricter view applies when lust is present. The key distinction is that for a woman, looking with lust is only makruh tanzihi (undesirable), not haram, because the man may not have lust. But for a man, looking with lust is haram because the woman is considered to have lust virtually due to its predominance in women. The passage concludes with the rationale: lust from both sides is more likely to lead to sin, so the prohibition is stronger.

Key Terms
عورة (‘awrah): Parts of the body that must be covered; for men, from navel to knee; for women, the entire body except face and hands.
شهوة (shahwah): Lust or sexual desire; its presence or fear changes the ruling of looking.
محارم (mahārim): Relatives with whom marriage is permanently prohibited, such as mother, sister, daughter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling for a woman looking at a non-mahram man's belly and back when she has no lust?
A) It is haram.
B) It is permissible.
C) It is makruh tanzihi.
D) It is makruh tahrimi.

Key Takeaway
The ruling on a woman looking at a non-mahram man's belly/back depends on the absence or presence of lust; without lust it is permissible, but with lust it is discouraged, while for a man it is haram.

Rational Proof for Looking at Mahrams and Definition of Mahram
Rational proof for looking at mahrams with definition and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rational proof for permissibility of looking at mahrams and define mahram, including the relied-upon position on musahara via zina.

Core Idea
Hardship (haraj) and reduced desire make looking at mahrams permissible; mahram is eternally marriage-prohibited, including via fornication.

This passage presents a rational proof (dalil aqli) for the permissibility of looking at certain body parts of mahram relatives. The author explains that prohibiting such looks would cause hardship because mahrams frequently interact without formal permission. Additionally, the eternal prohibition of marriage between mahrams reduces sexual desire, making such looks safe. The passage then defines mahram and addresses an intra-Hanafi disagreement: whether in-law relationships established through fornication (zina) create mahram status.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon (looking at mahrams) and whether it is permissible, recommended, etc. The text states it is permissible (mubah) due to necessity.
The ruling applies specifically to body parts that are normally uncovered (mawadi' al-zinah).
2
Locate the dalil aqli
Find the rational proof: the text argues that prohibiting such looks would cause hardship (haraj) and that eternal prohibition of marriage reduces desire, making the look safe.
This is a rational proof, not a direct textual proof.
3
Define mahram
Extract the definition: a mahram is a relative with whom marriage is permanently impermissible, due to lineage, breastfeeding (rida'), or in-law relationship (musahara).
The definition includes both causes (sabab) and lineage (nasab).
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Identify that some mashayikh disagree on whether musahara via zina (fornication) establishes mahram. The text indicates the relied-upon (al-ashah) view is that it does.
The disagreement is based on whether the relationship is considered a blessing or punishment.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Understand why the mufta bihi is the view that musahara via zina creates mahram: it avoids hardship and follows the general principle that the same rational proof applies.
Al-Shami (Ibn Abidin) gives preference to this view.

Likewise, desire decreases due to eternal prohibition, so little is desired, unlike parts beyond them because they are not usually uncovered. And the mahram is one with whom marriage is eternally impermissible, whether due to lineage or cause like breastfeeding and in-law relationship because both meanings (necessity and lack of desire) exist. Translation: And because some enter upon others without permission and modesty, and the woman in her house is usually in her work clothes, so if looking at these places were prohibited, it would lead to hardship. Similarly, desire decreases due to eternal prohibition, so desire is little, unlike those parts other than these (belly, back, thigh) because they are not usually uncovered. And the mahram is one with whom marriage is never permissible between him and her, whether due to lineage or cause like breastfeeding and in-law relationship due to the presence of both meanings (necessity and lack of desire). And whether the in-law relationship is through marriage or fornication according to the most correct view, due to the same reason that we have explained (leading to hardship and lack of desire). Elucidation: This is a rational proof for looking at mahrams: because such relatives enter each other's houses without restriction, so if looking at these places were prohibited, hardship would become necessary. Also, due to eternal prohibition, desire decreases. However, other places like belly, waist, thigh – looking at them is not permissible because they are not usually uncovered. Also, the Quran does not permit besides places of adornment, and these are not places of adornment. The mahram is one between whom and the woman marriage can never be valid, whether through lineage or cause, and by cause is meant breastfeeding and in-law relationship because here too there is necessity and lack of desire. Then in-law relationship is established through marriage or fornication based on the same proof. Warning: The author placed the restriction 'according to the most correct view' because there is a difference of opinion among some mashayikh. They said that due to in-law relationship established through fornication, looking and touching are not permissible because here the establishment of in-law relationship is through punishment, not through blessing. And when her betrayal has appeared once, trust cannot be placed again. But the most correct is that there is no hardship in this. Second warning: In Shami vol. 5 p. 235, this is given preference, and the most correct is consideration of reality because she is eternally prohibited to him.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with a rational proof (dalil aqli) for the permissibility of looking at certain body parts of mahram relatives. The author explains that if looking at the body parts that are normally uncovered (like head, hands, feet, neck) were prohibited, it would cause hardship because mahram relatives frequently interact without formal permission. Additionally, the eternal prohibition of marriage between mahrams reduces sexual desire, making such looks safe. However, body parts that are not normally uncovered (like belly, back, thighs) cannot be looked at. The passage then defines mahram as anyone with whom marriage is permanently prohibited, whether through blood, breastfeeding, or in-law relationship. The text also discusses an intra-Hanafi disagreement: some scholars argue that in-law relationships established through fornication do not create mahram status because they are based on punishment rather than blessing, but the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that they do, as there is no hardship in considering such relationships as fully mahram.

Key Terms
محرم (mahram): A relative with whom marriage is permanently prohibited due to lineage, breastfeeding, or in-law relationship.
مواضع الزينة (mawadi' al-zinah): Places of ornament, such as face, hands, forearms, feet, etc., that are normally adorned.
مصاهرة (musahara): In-law relationship through marriage or, in the relied-upon view, through fornication.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Because it is a recommended act

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits looking at mahrams' normally uncovered body parts based on a rational proof of preventing hardship and lack of desire, and treats musahara through zina as creating mahram status.

Touching Mahrams: When It's Halal and When It's Haram
A Hanafi ruling on touching mahrams with proof from hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on touching mahrams' permissible body parts and identify the condition that changes the ruling.

Core Idea
Touching mahrams is like looking: permissible when safe from desire, forbidden when desire feared.

This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position on physical contact with mahrams. While looking at certain body parts of mahrams is generally permissible, the ruling on touching follows a similar logic but with an important exception: the presence or absence of sexual desire changes the ruling entirely. Al-Quduri's matn provides the baseline ruling, and the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) serves as the proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
The act is touching the permissible body parts (e.g., head, hands, feet) of a mahram. The default ruling is mubah (permissible) when there is no fear of desire and there is a need, such as during travel.
The passage also contrasts this with non-mahram women, where looking is allowed but touching is not, because desire is assumed complete.
2
Recognize the exception that changes the ruling
If there is fear of desire (shahwah) on either side – the man or the woman – then even looking and touching become prohibited (haram). This is because such actions could lead to zina, which is especially severe with mahrams.
3
Locate the dalil (proof)
The hadith: 'The two eyes commit zina and their zina is looking; the two hands commit zina and their zina is grasping' (Bukhari and Muslim). This equates looking and grasping with zina in effect.
The hadith is not directly quoted in full in the matn; it is referenced as proof.
4
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith implies that any act that could lead to zina is forbidden. Since grasping (touching) is likened to zina of the hand, it is prohibited when desire is present. For mahrams, the prohibition is even more severe.
5
Contrast with non-mahram women
For non-mahram women, looking at face and hands is allowed but touching is prohibited even without explicit desire, because the mere possibility of desire is assumed. For mahrams, the opposite default applies due to the reduced likelihood of desire.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور کوئی حرج نہیں کہ وہ چھوٹے محارم کے اس حصہ کو جس کی جانب دیکھنا جائز ہے حاجت کے متحقق ہونے کی وجہ سے اس کی جانب مسافرت میں محرمیت کی وجہ سے شہوت کی قلت کی وجہ سے بخلاف اجتنبیہ کے چہرے اور اس کے ہاتھ کے اس حیثیت سے کہ چھونا جائز نہیں اگر چہ دیکھنا مباح قرار دیا گیا ہے اس لئے کہ شہوت کامل ہے مگر جب کہ محرم اپنے اوپر یا عورت کے اوپر شہوت کا خوف کرے تو اس وقت نہ دیکھے اور نہ چھوٹے نبی علیہ السلام کے فرمان کیوجہ سے کہ دونوں آنکھیں زنا کرتی ہیں اور ان کا زنا دیکھنا ہے دونوں ہاتھ زنا کرتے ہیں اور ان کا زنا پکڑنا ہے اور زنا کی حرمت محارم کے ساتھ زیادہ سخت ہے پس وہ بچے۔ تشریح اپنی محارم کے جتنے بدن کا دیکھنا جائز ہے اس کو چھونا بھی جائز ہے کیونکہ رشتہ محرمیت کی وجہ سے شہوت کی قلت ہے اور مسافرت کی حالت میں چھونے کی ضرورت پیش آتی ہے البتہ اجنبیہ کا چہرہ اور ہاتھ دیکھنا جائزہ تھا مگر چھونا جائز نہیں ہے کیوں کہ وہاں شہوت کامل نے البتہ اگر محرم کو اپنے اوپر یا عورت کے اوپر شہوت کے خوف ہو چھونے سے اور دیکھنے سے احتراز کرے کہیں ایسا نہ ہو کہ یہ مفضی الی الزنا ہو جائے اور محارم کے ساتھ زنا بہت سخت ہے اور بدترین فطرت کی کبھی ہے اور یہ حدیث بھی یہاں مذکور ہے جس میں پکڑنے اور دیکھنے کو بھی حکما ز نا قرار دیا گیا ہے۔ تنبي. وحرمة الزنا.... الخ حدیث کا ٹکڑا نہیں ہے، بلکہ حدیث البطش تک ہے جو بخاری اور مسلم میں موجود ہے۔
He (al-Quduri) said: There is no harm in touching what is permissible to look at from her, due to the verification of need for that in travel and the lack of desire for mahram, unlike the face and hands of a non-mahram woman where touching is not permitted even if looking is allowed, because desire is complete. Except when he fears desire for her or for himself, then he should not look nor touch, due to his (peace be upon him) saying: 'The two eyes commit zina and their zina is looking; the two hands commit zina and their zina is grasping.' And the prohibition of zina with mahrams is more severe, so one should avoid. Translation: Al-Quduri said: There is no harm in touching that part of mahrams which it is permissible to look at, due to the verification of need for that in travel and the lack of desire due to mahram relationship, unlike the face and hands of a non-mahram woman where touching is not permitted even though looking is made permissible, because desire is complete. But when the mahram fears desire for himself or for the woman, then he should not look nor touch, due to the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'The two eyes commit zina and their zina is looking; the two hands commit zina and their zina is grasping.' And the prohibition of zina with mahrams is more severe, so one should avoid. Elucidation: Touching mahrams' body parts that are permissible to look at is also permissible, because the mahram relationship reduces desire and there is a need for touching during travel. However, the face and hands of a non-mahram woman are permissible to look at but not to touch, because desire is complete there. But if a mahram fears desire for himself or the woman, he should refrain from touching and looking, lest it lead to zina. And zina with mahrams is very severe and among the worst of sins. This hadith is mentioned here in which grasping and looking are also considered zina in effect. Warning: The phrase 'and the prohibition of zina...' is not part of the hadith; rather the hadith ends at 'al-batsh' and is found in Bukhari and Muslim.
Source pages p. 343

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on touching mahrams' body parts. The imam al-Quduri states that it is permissible to touch those parts of a mahram that one is allowed to look at (e.g., head, hands, feet) because there is a genuine need, such as during travel, and because the mahram relationship reduces sexual desire. This is in contrast to non-mahram women: even though looking at their face and hands is permissible, touching them is not, because desire is more likely. However, if there is a fear of desire—either on the man's side or the woman's—then both looking and touching become prohibited, based on the hadith that the eyes and hands commit zina through looking and grasping. The hadith is cited to emphasize that any such act that could lead to zina is forbidden, especially with mahrams, where the crime is even more severe.

Key Terms
مس (mass): Touching with the hand, particularly in the context of physical contact with mahrams.
شهوة (shahwah): Sexual desire, the presence or absence of which affects the ruling on touching.
بطش (batash): Grasping or seizing with the hand, mentioned in the hadith as the zina of the hand.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) When there is a fear of sexual desire on either side
C) When the mahram is from breastfeeding
D) When the touch is during travel

Key Takeaway
Touching a mahram's permissible body parts is permissible by default, but becomes prohibited when there is fear of sexual desire.

Ruling on Seclusion and Travel with Mahram Relatives
Permits seclusion and travel with mahrams based on hadith evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on seclusion and travel with mahram relatives and identify the hadith evidence that supports it.

Core Idea
Seclusion and travel with mahram relatives are permissible because they are not strangers.

In this lesson, we examine a foundational ruling from the Hanafi school: the permissibility of seclusion (khalwah) and travel (musafarah) with mahram relatives. The text cites two authentic hadiths that establish this permission by implication. Understanding this ruling helps distinguish between permissible interaction with mahrams and prohibited interaction with non-mahrams.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their ruling
The passage states that there is 'no harm' (la ba's) in seclusion and travel with mahram women. This indicates permissibility (mubah) in the Hanafi school.
The term 'mahram' refers to relatives with whom marriage is permanently prohibited, such as father, brother, son, etc.
2
Locate the dalil (evidence)
Two hadiths are cited: one prohibiting a woman from traveling more than three days without a mahram, and another prohibiting a man from secluding with a non-mahram woman. These imply that with a mahram, both acts are allowed.
The hadiths are found in Bukhari and Muslim, but the text does not specify the source; the ruling is based on the general meaning.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how the dalil proves the ruling)
The hadiths use exceptions: travel is prohibited 'except with her husband or a mahram'; seclusion is prohibited 'with a woman not related to him'. By contrast, with a mahram, the prohibition is lifted.
The Hanafi usul principle: al-man'u yufidu al-ibahah 'ind intifaa' al-mani' (the prohibition indicates permissibility when the preventing factor is absent).
4
Note the cross-madhhab status
This ruling is mukhtalaf fih (disputed) – some schools may require the husband for travel beyond a certain distance, but Hanafi allows any mahram.
The mufta bihi (operative position) in the Hanafi school is permissibility with any mahram.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And there is no harm in seclusion and travel with them (mahrams) due to his (peace be upon him) saying: 'A woman should not travel for more than three days and nights except with her husband or a mahram relative of hers.' And his (peace be upon him) saying: 'Beware! No man should seclude with a woman who is not related to him, for the third of them is Satan.' And the meaning is when he is not a mahram. Translation: And there is no harm in seclusion and travel with mahrams due to the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'A woman should not travel for more than three days and nights (i.e., the distance of travel for qasr, which is the legal journey) except with her husband or a mahram relative of hers.' And due to the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Beware! No man should seclude with a woman, for there is no way for seclusion with her except that the third of them is Satan.' And the meaning is when he is not a mahram. Elucidation: Travel and seclusion with one's mahrams are permissible. From the first hadith, the permissibility of travel is known; from the second hadith, the permissibility of seclusion is known.
Source pages p. 343

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling that seclusion (khalwah) and travel (musafarah) with mahram relatives are permissible. The proof is two authentic hadith. The first hadith allows a woman to travel with a mahram, indicating that as long as she is with a mahram, travel is permissible. The second hadith prohibits seclusion with a non-mahram, implying that seclusion with a mahram is allowed. The commentator clarifies that the prohibition of seclusion applies only to non-mahrams; with mahrams, it is perfectly fine because they are not strangers and there is no fear of fitna. This ruling is standard in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
خلوة (khalwah): Seclusion between a man and a woman in a place where no one else can see them.
مسافرة (musafarah): Traveling together, specifically the permissibility of a woman traveling with a mahram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is prohibited because she needs her husband specifically
B) It is permissible because the hadith exempts travel with a mahram
C) It is makruh because mahram is not sufficient
D) It is haram regardless of mahram

Key Takeaway
Seclusion (khalwah) and travel (musafarah) with mahram relatives are permissible in the Hanafi school based on the implied exception in the hadiths.

Permissible Gaze: Looking at Another's Slave Woman
States ruling on permissible viewing of another's slave woman by analogy to mahram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on looking at another's slave woman and explain the proof from Umar's athar.

Core Idea
A man may look at another's slave woman as much as his own mahram, due to her work necessity.

In Hanafi fiqh, the awrah differs between free women and slave women. This lesson examines a ruling from al-Hidayah on how much a man may look at another person's slave woman. The reasoning is based on the practical needs of the slave woman's work and is supported by an athar of Umar ibn al-Khattab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is the specific act being ruled upon? A man looking at another person's slave woman. The ruling: it is permissible to look at her to the same extent he looks at his own female mahram relatives (e.g., mother, sister).
Mahram here refers to blood-related women within prohibited marriage degrees.
2
Understand the reasoning (ta'lil)
Why is this ruling given? Because the slave woman goes out for work, serves guests, and wears work clothes (not full covering like a free woman outside). Her situation outside is like a free woman inside with mahrams.
The underlying principle is necessity (hajah) and 'umum al-balwa (widespread need).
3
Locate the dalil
The author cites an athar (effect) of Umar ibn al-Khattab: he would strike a slave woman who wore a khimar (headcover) and order her to remove it, accusing her of imitating free women.
This athar shows that slave women are not required to cover like free women, which supports the permissibility of looking at them.
4
Evaluate the proof's strength
The athar is not from the Prophet but from a Companion. The commentary notes this specific wording is not found in authentic collections, but Imam Bayhaqi narrated a similar report. In Hanafi usul, qawl sahabi is a valid proof, though zanni in thubut and dalala.
Hanafis accept athar as supportive evidence, especially when backed by clear reasoning.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
This ruling is mukhtalaf fih. Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may consider the awrah of a slave woman equivalent to a free woman, thus more restrictive.
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is that in the Shafi'i school, a slave woman must cover more, and looking at her is more restricted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

A man can see as much of the body of another person's slave woman as he can see of his own female mahram relatives, because that slave woman goes out for her master's work and serves his guests, and she remains in her work clothes. So just as the condition of a free woman is inside the house with respect to mahrams, the same is the condition of a slave woman outside the house. The effect of Umar (may Allah be pleased with him): 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him), when he saw a slave woman wearing a veil, would strike her with a whip and say: Remove the khimar from you, O filthy one, do you imitate free women?' Translation: And Umar, when he saw a slave woman wearing a veil, would uncover her and say: O filthy one, remove your veil; do you imitate free women? Commentary: This effect of Umar was not found, however, Imam Bayhaqi has reported it in different words. 'Dirrah' (whip), plural 'dirar', 'difar' is based on kasr, from 'diftar' meaning fitna and corruption, so here it means filthy.
Source pages p. 345

Commentary
This passage is the commentary on a ruling from al-Hidayah regarding looking at another person's slave woman. The commentator explains that a man may look at another's slave woman to the same extent as he looks at his own female mahram relatives (such as mother, sister, etc.). The reason given is that the slave woman goes out to work for her master and serves guests, so she is not fully covered like a free woman; her condition outside is analogous to that of a free woman inside with mahrams. To support this, the author cites the effect (athar) of Umar ibn al-Khattab, who would strike slave women for wearing the khimar (headcover) and order them to remove it, indicating that they are not required to cover like free women. The commentary notes that this specific wording is not found in authentic collections, but Imam Bayhaqi narrated a similar report. The explanation of words: 'dirrah' means whip, 'difar' means filthy (from fitna). Thus, the ruling is established by the practice of the companions and the underlying reasoning of need.

Key Terms
ذی رحم محرم (dhi rahm mahram): Female relatives within prohibited degrees of marriage (mahram) related by blood (e.g., mother, sister, daughter).
باندی (bandi): Female slave (mamluka) owned by someone.
اثر (athar): A narration from a Companion (Sahabi) or a statement/action attributed to them.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because she is a mahram herself
D) Because all parts are permissible to look at

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a man may look at another's slave woman to the extent of his mahram, derived from Umar's athar and the principle of necessity.

Looking at Another's Slave Woman: Belly and Back Ruling
Intra-Hanafi dispute on looking at slave woman's belly and back

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi majority position on looking at a slave woman's belly and back, and evaluate the dissenting view of Muhammad ibn Muqatil.

Core Idea
Looking at a slave woman's belly and back is impermissible because necessity is absent and desire is heightened.

In this passage from al-Hidayah, the author presents an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the permissible extent of looking at another person's female slave. The relied-upon position prohibits looking at the belly and back, while Muhammad ibn Muqatil allows it except the area between navel and knee. The ruling is grounded in reasoning about necessity (darurah) and the intensity of desire. We will unpack the proofs, responses, and practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Issue
State the exact question being disputed: is it permissible for a man to look at the belly and back of another's slave woman?
The source explicitly mentions 'belly and back' (batn wa zahr).
2
State the Majority Hanafi Position
What is the mufta bihi position according to al-Hidayah? It is that looking is not permissible. Understand the reasoning: no necessity, analogy to mahrams, but with greater prohibition due to stronger desire in slave women.
Contrast with mahrams: mahrams have lesser desire, so looking is less dangerous.
3
State the Opposing View and Its Proof
Muhammad ibn Muqatil holds it is permissible except below navel to knee. He cites Ibn Abbas's statement about looking during purchase, and analogizes to free women.
Ibn Abbas's statement: 'Whoever intends to buy a slave woman may look at places other than the waistband.'
4
Analyze the Hanafi Response to the Opposing View
The majority response argues that Ibn Abbas's statement is specific to the context of purchase (need), not general. The general rule is prohibition because no universal need exists. Moreover, the analogy to mahrams is stronger because mahrams have less desire, so if looking at mahrams is prohibited without need, then looking at slave women (with greater desire) is even more prohibited.
Note the logic: if X (mahram) is prohibited due to lack of need, then X+ (slave woman) is even more prohibited due to stronger desire.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf and Mufta Bihi
The practical difference: under the mufta bihi, a man cannot look at belly/back of another's slave woman at all; under the dissenting view, he may look except the area between navel and knee. The majority position is the mufta bihi.
The source also clarifies that the ruling applies to all categories of slave women (mudabbara, makataba, umm walad, mustas'ah).

And it is not permissible to look at her belly and her back, contrary to what Muhammad ibn Muqatil says that it is permissible except for the area below the navel to the knee, because there is no necessity, just as with mahrams; rather it is even more so because of the lack of desire in them (mahrams) and because of the intensity of desire in slave women. And the word 'mamluka' includes mudabbara, makataba, and umm walad due to the verification of need, and a mustas'ah is like a makataba according to Abu Hanifa as per the details that have been recognized. Translation: It is not permissible to look at the belly and back of a slave woman, contrary to what Muhammad ibn Muqatil says that it is permissible except for the area below the navel to the knee, because there is no necessity, just as with mahrams; rather it is even more so because of the lack of desire in mahrams and the intensity of desire in slave women. And the word 'mamluka' includes mudabbara, makataba, and umm walad due to the unified need, and a mustas'ah is like a makataba according to Abu Hanifa according to the details that have been recognized. Commentary: It is not permissible to look at another's slave woman's belly and back. Muhammad ibn Muqatil says it is permissible, i.e., she is like a free woman: looking from below the navel to the knee is impermissible, and the rest is permissible. They argued with the statement of Ibn Abbas: 'Whoever intends to buy a slave woman may look at places other than the waistband.' But we said that looking at her belly and back is not permissible because there is no need, just as there is no need in mahrams; rather, looking at slave women is more emphatically impermissible because mahrams have lesser desire while slave women have greater desire. Then this ruling applies generally to all slave women, and similarly to makataba, mudabbara, and umm walad, because the word 'mamluka' includes them all, and they have the same need in understanding. It has passed in Kitab al-Itaq that when a master frees a part of a slave woman, that part is freed, and she will earn the remaining portion of her price and give it to her master; this is called mustas'ah. So her ruling is the same as that of a makataba, and this detail is according to Imam Abu Hanifa's school, while the Sahibayn hold that freeing a part frees the whole. See Hidayah 436 vol. 2.
Source pages p. 345

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute within the Hanafi school regarding looking at the belly and back of another person's slave woman. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that it is not permissible, because there is no necessity (darurah) for looking at those parts, just as with mahram relatives. Muhammad ibn Muqatil holds that it is permissible except for the area between the navel and knee, arguing that a slave woman is like a free woman in terms of awrah. He cites a statement of Ibn Abbas allowing looking at a slave woman intended for purchase except the waist area. However, the Hanafi response (of the majority) emphasizes that the need in slave women is greater (due to work) but looking at belly/back has no need, and since desire is stronger in slave women, the prohibition is more emphatic. The passage also clarifies that the term 'mamluka' includes all types of slave women (mudabbara, makataba, umm walad), and even a mustas'ah (a slave woman who earns to free herself) follows the same ruling as a makataba according to Abu Hanifa. A note is added about the difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on partial manumission.

Key Terms
محمد بن مقاتل (Muhammad ibn Muqatil): A Hanafi scholar known for some differing views within the school.
مملوکہ (mamluka): A female slave; the term includes mudabbara (promised freedom upon master's death), makataba (contracting for freedom), umm walad (slave mother of master's child), and mustas'ah (earning to buy freedom).

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because there is no need, and desire in slave women is greater, making prohibition more emphatic
C) Because it is always haram to look at a slave woman
D) Because the slave woman herself prohibits it

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi ruling prohibits looking at another's slave woman's belly and back due to lack of necessity and heightened desire, distinguishing from the dissenting opinion of Muhammad ibn Muqatil.

The Ikhtilaf on Seclusion and Travel with Another's Slave Woman
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on seclusion and travel with another's slave woman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi opinions on seclusion and travel with another's slave woman and explain the basis of each opinion (qiyas to mahram vs. lack of necessity).

Core Idea
Seclusion and travel with another's slave woman: permissible by analogy to mahram, or prohibited due to lack of necessity.

This passage from Kitab al-Karahiyah addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether it is permissible to seclude oneself or travel with a slave woman belonging to someone else. Two opinions are cited: one permits it by analogy to mahram relatives, the other prohibits it due to the absence of necessity. Understanding the basis of each view is essential for grasping Hanafi reasoning in social interactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Legal Acts
Recall the two acts under discussion: khilwah (seclusion) and musafarah (traveling) with a slave woman owned by another person. These are specific interactions with a non-mahram female.
The source specifies 'with her' – the slave woman referred to in the previous context.
2
Recognize the Two Opinions
Note that the text presents two qawls (opinions). The first declares it permissible (yubah) like with mahram; the second declares it impermissible (la yubah) due to lack of darurah (necessity).
Both opinions exist within the Hanafi school; no single position is designated as the mufta bihi in this passage.
3
Analyze the Qiyas of the First Opinion
The first opinion analogizes (qiyas) the slave woman to a mahram relative. The illa (effective cause) is the absence of fitnah or the permissibility of such interactions due to the lack of legal prohibition.
The asl (original case) is mahram; the far' is the slave woman. The ruling follows if the illa is shared.
4
Analyze the Second Opinion's Ground
The second opinion rejects the analogy because of the absence of necessity. Unlike a mahram, interaction with a non-mahram slave woman is not inherently needed; thus, the default prohibition applies.
This argument rests on the principle that permissibility of interaction with non-mahram requires a valid excuse.
5
Note the Later Authorities' Inclinations
The commentary adds that Shams al-Aimmah al-Sarakhsi inclined to the first (permissive) opinion, while Hakim Shahid inclined to the second (restrictive). This shows that the issue remained unsettled among later Hanafi scholars.
The absence of a clear tarjih indicates that the mufti can choose based on circumstances.

Source Text

واما الخلوة بها والمسافرة معها فقد قيل يباح كما فى المحارم وقد قيل لا يباح لعدم الضرورة وفي الاركاب والا نزال اعتبر محمد في الاصل الضرورة فيهن وفى دوات المحارم مجرد الحاجة. ترجمہ اور بہر حال باندیوں کے ساتھ خلوت اور ان کیساتھ سفر کرنا پس کہا گیا ہے کہ مباح ہے جیسے محارم میں اور کہا گیا ہے کہ مباح نہیں ہے ضرورت نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے اور سوار کرنے میں اور اتارنے میں محمد نے مبسوط میں سخت ضرورت کا اعتبار کیا ہے باندیوں کے سلسلہ میں اور محارم میں محض حاجت کا۔ تشریح دوسروں کی باندیوں کے ساتھ خلوت اور مسافرت کو بعض نے جائز کہا ہے اور بعض نے ناجائز کہا ہے اول فریق نے محارم پر قیاس کیا ہے اور فریق ثانی نے عدم ضرورت کا لحاظ کیا ہے۔ اب رہا ان باندیوں کے چڑھانے اور اتارنے کا تو امام محمد نے مبسوط میں ضرورت کا لحاظ کیا ہے یعنی اگر ضرورت ہے کہ وہ خود چڑھ نہیں سکتی یا چڑھ سکتی ہیں مگر بمشقت اور ان کو اس کی وجہ سے ضر ر لاحق ہو سکتا ہے تو اب ضرورت ہے تو چڑھا سکتا ہے تو ضرورت سے مراد کہ جس کے بغیر چارہ کار نہ ہو۔ اور حاجت کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ سوار ہونے کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے پھر بھی جانا چاہتی ہے مثلاً اپنا کھیت دیکھنے کے لئے محارم میں امام محمد نے حاجت کا اعتبار کیا ہے اور اس میں اتارنے اور چڑھانے کو جائز قرار دیا ہے مگر باندی اگر بلاضرورت سوار ہونا چاہے تو ضرورت نہیں ہے لہذا ارکاب و انزال جائز نہ ہوگا۔ تنبیہ شمس الائمہ سرخسی کا میلان پہلے قول کی طرف ہے اور حاکم شہید کا میا ان دوسرے قول کی طرف ہے۔
As for seclusion with her and traveling with her: it has been said that it is permissible as with mahram relatives, and it has been said that it is not permissible due to lack of necessity. Regarding mounting and dismounting, Muhammad in al-Asl considered necessity for them (slave women), and for mahram relatives mere need. Translation: And in any case, seclusion with slave women and traveling with them: it has been said that it is permissible like with mahram, and it has been said that it is not permissible due to lack of necessity. Regarding mounting and dismounting, Muhammad in al-Mabsut considered severe necessity for slave women, and for mahram merely need. Elaboration: Some have declared seclusion and travel with others' slave women permissible, some have declared it impermissible. The first group analogized to mahram, the second considered the lack of necessity. As for mounting and dismounting these slave women, Imam Muhammad in al-Mabsut considered necessity, i.e., if she cannot mount herself or can only with difficulty and harm might befall her, then there is necessity and he may mount her. Necessity means that without which there is no alternative. Need means that there is no necessity for riding, yet she wishes to go, e.g., to see her field. For mahram, Imam Muhammad considered need and allowed mounting and dismounting. But if a slave woman wishes to ride without necessity, then there is no necessity, so mounting and dismounting will not be permissible. Note: Shams al-Aimmah al-Sarakhsi inclines towards the first opinion, and Hakim Shahid towards the second.
Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Karahiyah addresses a dispute regarding seclusion (khilwah) and traveling (musafarah) with a slave woman belonging to someone else. There are two opinions: one considers it permissible by analogy to mahram relatives, the other prohibits it due to the lack of necessity. The author then specifies the ruling for assisting such slave women to mount and dismount (al-irkab wal-inzal). Imam Muhammad distinguishes between slave women and mahram: for slave women, actual necessity (darurah) is required, while for mahram, mere need (hajah) suffices. The passage ends with a note that Shams al-Aimmah al-Sarakhsi leans towards the first (permissive) opinion, while Hakim Shahid leans towards the second (restrictive) opinion.

Key Terms
خلوت (khalwah): Seclusion with a non-mahram person in private
مسافرة (musafarah): Traveling together, i.e., accompanying a non-mahram on a journey
اركاب وانزال (irkab wa inzal): Helping a woman mount and dismount a riding animal

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is the basis for the opinion that khilwah with another's slave woman is permissible?
A) Analogy to mahram relatives
B) Necessity
C) Ijma
D) Hadith

Key Takeaway
Seclusion and travel with another's slave woman is a matter of ikhtilaf in the Hanafi school, with permissibility based on qiyas and impermissibility on lack of necessity.

The Distinction Between Darurah and Hajah in Assisting Slave Women Mount and Dismount
Imam Muhammad's ruling on assisting slave women mount/dismount

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain Imam Muhammad's distinction between necessity (darurah) for slave women and mere need (hajah) for mahram in the ruling on assisting mount and dismount.

Core Idea
For slave women: necessity; for mahram: need — the degree of proximity to prohibition dictates the threshold.

This part of the passage specifies the ruling for helping a slave woman mount and dismount a riding animal. Imam Muhammad in al-Asl distinguished between slave women and mahram relatives: for slave women, actual necessity (darurah) is required, while for mahram, mere need (hajah) suffices. This distinction reflects the different levels of prohibition in interaction with non-mahram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Specific Act
The act under discussion is al-irkab wal-inzal (helping mount and dismount) a slave woman belonging to another. This is a specific and limited physical interaction.
The passage contrasts this with mahram relatives.
2
Note Imam Muhammad's Position
Imam Muhammad, in his book al-Asl (or al-Mabsut), considered that for slave women, darurah (necessity) is required for this act to be permissible. For mahram, hajah (need) is sufficient.
This position is from the Zahir al-Riwayah and thus a strong authority.
3
Define Darurah and Hajah
Darurah means a situation without which there is no alternative (la budda minhu). Hajah means a desire or convenience, not an absolute necessity. The commentary explains: necessity includes inability to mount without assistance or risk of harm.
The passage provides examples: if she cannot mount alone or can only with difficulty and potential harm, then darurah exists.
4
Apply the Distinction
If a slave woman can mount herself without harm, then there is no darurah, and assisting her would not be permissible. For a mahram, even if she simply wants to go see her field (hajah), it is permissible.
This shows that the ruling is more restrictive for slave women than for mahram.
5
Understand the Underlying Principle
The stricter requirement for slave women reflects the stronger prohibition of physical contact with non-mahram. Necessity overrides the prohibition, but mere desire does not.
This is consistent with the general Hanafi principle that necessity permits the prohibited.

Touching a Slave Woman During Purchase: With or Without Desire
Ruling on touching a slave woman during purchase intention with or without desire

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on touching a slave woman during purchase and distinguish the ruling based on the presence or absence of desire.

Core Idea
Touching a slave woman during purchase is mubah without desire, but prohibited with desire due to analogy to intercourse.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on physically touching a slave woman when one intends to purchase her. The early Hanafi masters gave absolute permission, but later mashayikh refined the ruling by conditioning it on the absence of desire. Understanding this distinction is crucial for applying the school's reliance on necessity (darurah) and its caution against acts resembling prohibited sexual enjoyment (istimta').

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what specific act is being ruled upon (touching a slave woman) and in what context (during purchase). Identify the baseline hukm: mubah (permissible) according to the early texts, but later qualified.
The act is 'mass' (touching), not 'nazar' (looking).
2
Locate the dalil
Find the evidence used to restrict the permissibility. The mashayikh use qiyas: touching with desire resembles intercourse (jima'), which is forbidden with a non-owned slave.
The source does not quote a Quran or hadith; the proof is analogical reasoning.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the analogy works. The effective cause ('illa) is the presence of desire that transforms mere touch into istimta', which is legally akin to sexual intercourse. Since intercourse with a slave one does not own is forbidden, touching with desire is also forbidden.
The link is that both are forms of sexual enjoyment.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify the disagreement: Imam Muhammad and al-Quduri permitted touching even with desire; the later mashayikh prohibited it. This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
The earlier position is from zahir al-riwayah; the later position is from fatawa mutakhkhirin.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Determine the mufta bihi (operative ruling). According to the text, the mashayikh's restrictive view is relied upon (al-mu'tamad), especially in times of fitnah.
The author of al-Ikhtiyar explicitly adopts this view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ولا باس بان يمس ذلك اذا اراد الشراء وان خاف ان يشتهي كذا ذكر فى المختصر واطلق ايضا في الجامع الصغير ولم يفصل قال مشائخنا رحمهم الله يباح النظر في هذه الحالة وان اشتهى للضرورة ولا يباح المس اذا اشتهى او کان اکبر رائه ذلك لانه نوع استمتاع وفى غير حالة الشراء يباح النظر والمس بشرط عدم الشهوة. ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور کوئی حرج نہیں اس کو ( ان جگہوں کو جن کا دیکھنا جائز ہے ) چھونے میں جب کہ وہ خریدنے کا ارادہ کرے اگر چہ وہ شہورت کا خوف کرے ایسے ہی مختصر میں مذکور ہے اور نیز محمد نے جامع صغیر میں مطلق فرمایا ہے اور تفصیل نہیں کی ہمارے مشائخ نے فرمایا کہ اس حالت میں (بوقت شراء ) دیکھنا جائز ہے اگر چہ شہوت ہو حاجت کی وجہ سے اور چھونا جائز نہیں جب کہ شہوت ہو یا اس کو اس کا غالب گمان ہو اس لئے کہ یہ استمتاع ( فائدہ اٹھانا) کی ایک قسم ہے اور خرید کی حالت کے غیر میں دیکھنا اور چھونا مباح ہے عدم شہوت کی شرط کے ساتھ ۔ تشریح اور امام محمد نے جامع صغیر میں مطلقا یہ فرمایا ہے کہ خریدتے وقت باندی کو چھونا جائز ہے اور شہوت ہونے اور نہ ہونے کی کوئی تفصیل بیان نہیں کی ، اور قدوری نے فرمایا ہے کہ شہوت کے باوجود بھی چھونا جائز ہے۔ مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ ہمارے مشائخ نے یہ فرمایا ہے کہ اگر شہوت ہو یا شہوت کا غالب گمان ہوتو پھر چھونا مباح نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ مس بالشہوۃ معنی جماع ہے جس کی اجازت نہیں ہے البتہ شہوت سے دیکھنا جماع نہیں ہے لہذا اول کی اجازت نہیں اور ثانی کی اجازت ہے اور اگر خریدنے کا ارادہ نہ ہو تو چھوٹا اور دیکھنا جبھی جائز ہوگا کہ شہوت نہ ہو۔ تنبیہ بر بناء ضرورت چھونا جائز ہے تا کہ اس کے بدن کی نرمی معلوم ہو سکے اور یہ غرض صحیح ہے بعض حضرات نے کہا ہے کہ اگر شہوت ہو تو ہمارے زمانہ میں چھونے کو جائز نہیں کہا جائے گا اور اختیار شرح مختار میں اس پر جزم ظاہر کیا ہے۔
He (al-Quduri) said: There is no harm in touching that (the areas that are permissible to see) when he intends to purchase, even if he fears he will desire. Thus it is mentioned in al-Mukhtasar, and it is also absolute in al-Jami' al-Saghir without detail. Our mashayikh (may Allah have mercy on them) said: Looking is permissible in this situation even if he desires, due to necessity. But touching is not permissible if he desires or if his predominant opinion is that he will desire, because it is a type of enjoyment. Outside the purchase situation, looking and touching are permissible on condition of absence of desire. Translation: Al-Quduri said: There is no harm in touching them when he intends to purchase, even if he fears desire. Similarly mentioned in al-Mukhtasar, and Muhammad stated absolutely in al-Jami' al-Saghir without detail. Our mashayikh said: In this state (at time of purchase), looking is permissible even if there is desire, due to need. But touching is not permissible when there is desire or if he has a predominant assumption of desire, because it is a type of enjoyment. Outside the purchase situation, looking and touching are permissible with the condition of absence of desire. Elaboration: Imam Muhammad stated absolutely in al-Jami' al-Saghir that touching a slave woman at the time of purchase is permissible, without detailing desire or its absence. Al-Quduri said it is permissible even with desire. The author says our mashayikh ruled: if desire is present or predominant, then touching is not permissible because touching with desire is like intercourse, which is not permitted. However, looking with desire is not like intercourse, so the former is not permitted while the latter is. If there is no intention to purchase, then touching and looking are only permissible if there is no desire. Note: Touching is permissible based on necessity to ascertain the softness of her body, and this purpose is valid. Some have said that in our time, if desire is present, touching will not be called permissible, and al-Ikhtiyar Sharh al-Mukhtar explicitly states this.
Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This passage presents the rulings on looking at and touching a slave woman when one intends to purchase her. Imam Muhammad in al-Jami' al-Saghir gave an absolute permission for touching during purchase, without conditioning absence of desire. Al-Quduri similarly permitted it even with desire. However, the later mashayikh (our scholars) refined the ruling: looking is permissible even with desire because of necessity (the need to assess the slave), but touching is not permissible if desire is present or strongly anticipated, because touching with desire constitutes a form of sexual enjoyment (istimta'). Outside the purchase scenario, both looking and touching are permissible only if there is no desire. The note adds that some later authorities restrict touching even with necessity in times when fitnah is prevalent.

Key Terms
مس (mass): Physical touching, specifically of a slave woman during purchase assessment
استمتاع (istimta'): Sexual enjoyment; any act done for sexual gratification
ضرورت (darurah): Necessity that justifies normally prohibited acts; here, the need to assess the slave for purchase

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the later mashayikh, what is the ruling on touching a slave woman during purchase if the buyer desires her?
A) Touching is permissible because of necessity
B) Touching is not permissible because it is a type of enjoyment
C) Touching is permissible only if he does not have desire
D) Both B and C

Key Takeaway
Touching a slave woman during purchase is mubah without desire, but haram with desire according to the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Displaying a Mature Slave Woman: The One-Izar Rule
Ruling against presenting a balighah slave woman in only one izar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on displaying a balighah slave woman in a single izar and explain the rationale based on 'awrah.

Core Idea
A mature slave woman's back and belly are 'awrah so an izar alone is insufficient.

This lesson presents a key ruling from Imam Muhammad’s al-Jami‘ al-Saghir: a slave woman who has reached puberty (or is desirable) may not be presented for sale wearing only a lower garment (izar). The reason is that her back and belly are considered ‘awrah and must be covered. The ruling protects dignity and prevents fitna in the marketplace.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is displaying a slave woman for sale in a single izar. The ruling is prohibition: لا تعرض (she should not be displayed). Determine the legal category (haram/makruh).
In Hanafi, a prohibition without evidence of permissiveness indicates haram.
2
Pinpoint the triggering condition
The condition is either (a) she has menstruated (i.e., reached puberty) or (b) she is desirable and can be copulated with, even before puberty. Both trigger the same ruling.
The second condition is taken from a narration of Muhammad.
3
Understand the rationale: ‘awrah
The basis is that a slave woman’s back and belly are ‘awrah when she is mature or desirable. An izar covers only from navel to knee, leaving back and belly exposed.
This is a specific ruling for slave women; free women have a different ‘awrah standard.
4
Apply the ruling to a practical scenario
If a seller brings a balighah slave woman to market wearing only an izar, he must add a qamis (upper garment) to cover her back and belly, or else the display is impermissible.
The same applies if she is pre-pubescent but already desirable.
5
Recall the sources and authority
The ruling is from al-Jami‘ al-Saghir (Imam Muhammad) and is part of Zahir al-Riwayah. The commentary in al-Hidayah and al-Shami confirms it.
This is the mufta bihi position of the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال واذا حاضت الامة لم تعرض فى ازار واحد ومعناه بلغت وهذا لما بينا ان الظهر والبطن منها عورة وعن محمد انها اذا كانت تشتهى و تجامع مثلها فهى كالبالغة لاتعرض فى ازار واحد لوجود الاشتهاء. ترجمہ محمد نے ( جامع صغیر میں ) فرمایا ہے اور جب باندی بالغہ ہو جائے تو ایک ازار میں پیش نہ کی جائے اور اس کے معنی بلغت کے ہیں اور یہ اس دلیل کی وجہت ہے جو کہ ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں کہ اس کی پیٹھ اور پیٹ عورت ہے اور محمد سے منقول ہے کہ باندی جب کہ قابل شہوت ہو اور اس کے مثل سے جماع کیا جا سکتا ہے تو وہ بالغہ کے مثل ہے اشتہاء کے پائے جانے کی وجہ سے وہ ایک ازار میں پیش نہیں کی جائے گی۔ تشریح باندی کا پیٹ اور پیٹھ عورت ہے لہذا جب وہ بالغ ہو جائے تو اس کو منڈی میں جب فروخت کرنے کے لئے جائے تو ایک ازار میں نہ لے جائے بلکہ اس کے اوپر قمیص ڈالے تا کہ اس کا پیٹ اور پیٹھ چھپ جائے ، یعنی فقط اس ایک کپڑے میں نہ لے جائے جس سے صرف مادون السرة الى الركبة چھپے ہوئے ہوں اور باقی بدن کھلا ہوا اور جب وہ جماع کے قابل ہوگئی تو وہ بالغہ کے حکم میں ہے۔ تفصیل کے لئے ملاحظہ ہو شامی ص ۲۳۶ ج ۵ -
He (Muhammad) said: When the slave woman menstruates, she should not be displayed in a single izar. Its meaning is that she has reached puberty. This is because, as we have explained, her back and belly are 'awrah. And from Muhammad: if she is desirable and can be copulated with like her, then she is like an adult; she should not be displayed in a single izar because desire exists. Translation: Muhammad said in al-Jami' al-Saghir: When a slave woman reaches puberty, she should not be presented in a single izar. The meaning is that she has become balighah. This is due to the reason we have stated: her back and belly are 'awrah. And from Muhammad: if she is desirable and can be copulated with like her, then she is like an adult; she should not be displayed in a single izar because desire exists. Elaboration: The slave woman's belly and back are 'awrah. Therefore, when she reaches puberty, when going to the market for sale, she should not be taken in a single izar, but a qamis should be placed over it to cover her belly and back. That is, not be taken in just one garment that only covers from navel to knee while the rest of the body is uncovered. When she becomes capable of intercourse, she is in the ruling of an adult. For details, see Shami vol. 5 p. 236.
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling from al-Jami' al-Saghir that a sexually mature slave woman (balighah) should not be presented for sale wearing only an izar (lower garment). The reason is that her back and belly are considered 'awrah. If she is still young but has reached an age where she is desirable and can be copulated with, she is treated like an adult. The practical ruling: when bringing her to market, she must be covered with an additional garment such as a qamis to conceal the 'awrah of her back and belly.

Key Terms
ازار (izar): A lower garment worn from waist to ankles, leaving the upper body exposed
عورة ('awrah): Parts of the body that must be covered; for a slave woman, back and belly are 'awrah in addition to the usual parts

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, when is a slave woman prohibited from being displayed in a single izar?
A) Only when she has menstruated and reached puberty
B) Only when she is desirable and can be copulated with
C) Both A and B
D) Only if she is over 18 years old

Key Takeaway
A mature or desirable slave woman's back and belly are 'awrah, so she must be covered with at least an izar and a qamis when displayed for sale.

Eunuch's Gaze: Still Haram Like Any Man
Hukm on eunuch's (khasii) gaze: still like a fertile male due to residual sexual capacity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a eunuch looking at non-mahram women and explain the evidence from hadith and analogy.

Core Idea
Castration does not make lawful what was already forbidden; a eunuch remains a male with full legal responsibility for gaze.

This passage addresses a specific case: a castrated male (khasii). Does his altered physical state change the Islamic ruling on looking at non-mahram women? The author clarifies that the prohibition remains because castration is mere mutilation (muthlah) and does not erase his male legal identity or inherent sexual capacity. We will unpack the evidence from the hadith of Aisha and the analogical reasoning that extends the rule to other similar cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Subject
State clearly that the eunuch (khasii) is declared to be like a fertile male (fahl) regarding the prohibition of looking at non-mahram women. The ruling is haram.
The text begins with 'He said: The eunuch ... is like a fertile male.'
2
Locate the Primary Dalil
The hadith of Aisha radiAllahu anha: 'al-khisa' muthlah' (castration is mutilation). Explain that this hadith shows that an alteration of the body does not change legal rulings that were in place before the alteration.
The hadith is quoted in part; its full context is that the Prophet (ﷺ) forbade mutilation and said castration is a form of it.
3
Analyze the Wajh al-Dalalah
How does the hadith prove the ruling? Since looking was already forbidden before castration, and castration does not remove the prohibition, the eunuch remains under the same prohibition. Additionally, the eunuch retains the capacity for intercourse (yujami‘), which is the illa (effective cause) for the prohibition.
4
Trace the Expansion to Related Cases
The author extends the ruling to the majbub (one whose penis is amputated) because he can still achieve ejaculation through rubbing, and to the mukhannath (effeminate) who engages in worst actions, as he remains a sinful male. Then note the exemption of the young child (saghir) by explicit textual exception.
The expansion (expansion_probe) shows the principle applied consistently: any male with residual sexual capacity is treated as a full male for this ruling.
5
Conclude the General Principle
The ultimate ruling is derived from the clear text of the Quran (the general prohibition of looking) and the hadith. The young child is excluded by nass (textual evidence).
'Al-hasil' (the conclusion) ties it back to the primary sources.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال والخصى فى النظر الى الاجنبية كالفحل لقول عائشة رضى الله عنها الخصاء مثلة فلا يبيح ما كان حراما قبله ولانه فحل يجامع وكذا المجبوب لانه يسحق وينزل وكذا المخنث في الردى من الافعال لانه فحل فاسق والحاصل انه يوخذ فيه بمحكم كتاب الله المنزل فيه والطفل الصغير مستثنى بالنص
He (the author) said: The eunuch (khasii) regarding looking at a non-mahram woman is like a fertile male (fahl). Because of the saying of Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her): 'Castration is mutilation', so it does not permit what was forbidden before it. And because he is a male who can have intercourse (yujami'). Similarly, the one whose penis is cut off (majbub) because he can rub and ejaculate. And similarly the effeminate (mukhannath) in the worst of actions, because he is a sinful male. The conclusion is that the ruling is taken from the clear text of the revealed Book of Allah, and the young child is excluded by the text.
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling for a eunuch (khasii) looking at non-mahram women. The eunuch is treated like a normal fertile male (fahl) because he retains the capacity for intercourse and ejaculation. The hadith of Aisha radiAllahu anha states that castration is mutilation and does not render lawful what was previously unlawful. Similarly, a man whose penis has been amputated (majbub) can still experience ejaculation through rubbing, so he is likewise prohibited. An effeminate man (mukhannath) who engages in immoral acts is also a sinful male and cannot look. The general rule is that the rulings of the Quran regarding the prohibition of looking at non-mahram apply to all males except young children who are explicitly exempted by divine text (nass).

Key Terms
خصى (khasii): A castrated male (eunuch)
فحل (fahl): A sexually mature and potent male
مثلة (muthlah): Mutilation or disfigurement of the body

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the passage treat a eunuch (khasii) like a fertile male (fahl) regarding looking at non-mahram women?
A) Because a eunuch can still have intercourse
B) Because castration is mutilation and does not make lawful what was forbidden
C) Both A and B
D) Neither A nor B

Key Takeaway
A eunuch is legally treated as a fully capable male for the prohibition of looking at non-mahram women; castration does not lift the obligation to lower the gaze.

Ruling on Looking at and Touching a Slave Woman When Buying
States the permissibility of looking and the restriction on touching when purchasing a slave woman, with intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on looking at and touching a slave woman during purchase, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Muhammad and the later mashaykh.

Core Idea
Touching a slave woman with desire during purchase is prohibited because it resembles intercourse; looking is allowed even with desire due to need.

In classical Hanafi fiqh, the purchase of a slave woman involves specific rules regarding physical examination. This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah clarifies the distinction between looking and touching, and highlights an internal Hanafi difference between the earlier textual rulings and later fatwa practice. Understanding this dispute reveals how later scholars refined rulings based on analogy and caution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
Determine what act is being discussed (looking/touching) and in what situation (purchasing a slave woman).
The context of need (hajah) is key for permissibility of looking.
2
State the general Hanafi rule
State the ruling for looking and touching as given by the author: looking is permissible even with desire; touching is not permissible when desire is present or strongly presumed.
The reason given is that touching is a form of istimta' (sexual enjoyment).
3
Identify the intra-madhhab disagreement
Note that Imam Muhammad and al-Quduri allowed touching even with desire, while the later mashaykh prohibited it.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school.
4
Analyze the basis of the dispute
Understand the reasoning (talil) behind each position: the mashaykh analogized touching with desire to intercourse (qiyas), while earlier scholars considered the text of al-Jami' al-Saghir as absolute.
This is a classic example of textual authority vs. analogical reasoning.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Identify which position is relied upon for fatwa: the position of the mashaykh (touching with desire is prohibited) is the operative ruling.
The author of Ashraf al-Hidayah accepts the mashaykh view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نے فرمایا کہ اس حالت میں (بوقت شراء) دیکھنا جائز ہے اگر چہ شہوت ہو حاجت کی وجہ سے اور چھونا جائز نہیں جب کہ شہوت ہو یا اس کو اس کا غالب گمان ہو اس لئے کہ یہ استمتاع (فائدہ اٹھانا) کی ایک قسم ہے اور خرید کی حالت کے غیر میں دیکھنا اور چھونا مباح ہے عدم شہوت کی شرط کے ساتھ۔ تشریح اور امام محمد نے جامع صغیر میں مطلقا یہ فرمایا ہے کہ خریدتے وقت باندی کو چھونا جائز ہے اور شہوت ہونے اور نہ ہونے کی کوئی تفصیل بیان نہیں کی، اور قدوری نے فرمایا ہے کہ شہوت کے باوجود بھی چھونا جائز ہے۔ مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ ہمارے مشائخ نے یہ فرمایا ہے کہ اگر شہوت ہو یا شہوت کا غالب گمان ہو تو پھر چھونا مباح نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ مس بالشہوۃ معنی جماع ہے جس کی اجازت نہیں ہے البتہ شہوت سے دیکھنا جماع نہیں ہے لہذا اول کی اجازت نہیں اور ثانی کی اجازت ہے اور اگر خریدنے کا ارادہ نہ ہو تو چھونا اور دیکھنا جبھی جائز ہوگا کہ شہوت نہ ہو۔ تنبیہ بر بناء ضرورت چھونا جائز ہے تا کہ اس کے بدن کی نرمی معلوم ہو سکے اور یہ غرض صحیح ہے بعض حضرات نے کہا ہے کہ اگر شہوت ہو تو ہمارے زمانہ میں چھونے کو جائز نہیں کہا جائے گا اور اختیار شرح مختار میں اس پر جزم ظاہر کیا ہے۔
Author said: In this case (at the time of purchase) looking is permissible, even if there is desire, due to need. And touching is not permissible when there is desire or when one has a strong presumption of it, because it is a form of enjoyment (istimta'). And outside the context of purchase, looking and touching are permissible with the condition of no desire. Explanation: Imam Muhammad said in al-Jami' al-Saghir absolutely that touching a slave-girl at the time of purchase is permissible, and he did not specify any detail regarding the presence or absence of desire. And al-Quduri said: Touching is permissible even with desire. The author says: Our mashaykh said: If there is desire or a strong presumption of desire, then touching is not permissible, because touching with desire carries the meaning of intercourse, which is not permitted. However, looking with desire is not intercourse, so the first is not permitted and the second is permitted. And if there is no intention to purchase, touching and looking are only permissible when there is no desire. Caution: Touching is permissible due to necessity so that one may know the softness of her body, and this is a valid purpose. Some scholars have said that if there is desire, in our time touching will not be considered permissible, and al-Ikhtiyar Sharh al-Mukhtar affirms this.
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya discusses the rulings on looking at and touching a slave woman when one intends to buy her. The author first states the general rule: looking is allowed even with desire due to the need of purchase; touching is disallowed if desire is present because it constitutes sexual enjoyment. Outside purchase, both are only allowed without desire. The author then presents intra-Hanafi differences: Imam Muhammad and al-Quduri allowed touching even with desire, but the later mashaykh prohibited it because it resembles intercourse. The tanbih (cautionary note) adds that touching is allowed for necessity, like checking softness, but some later scholars restricted it even with desire. This illustrates the ijtihad within the Hanafi school on a practical fiqh issue.

Key Terms
شہوت (shahwah): sexual desire
استمتاع (istimta'): sexual enjoyment
مس بالشہوۃ (mass bil-shahwah): touching with desire

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mashaykh, why is touching a slave woman during purchase prohibited when desire is present?
A) Because it invalidates the purchase
B) Because it is analogous to intercourse
C) Because it causes distraction
D) Because it is not necessary

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, touching a slave woman with desire during purchase is prohibited because it is equivalent to intercourse; looking even with desire is permitted due to need.
