The Male Slave's Gaze Upon His Female Owner: Hanafi vs. Maliki/Shafi'i
Hanafi ruling with inter-madhhab dispute on slave's view of female owner

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on a male slave's view of his female owner, explain the opposing proof from need and the verse 'wa ma malakat aymanuhum', and articulate the Hanafi response that restricts the verse to female slaves and deems the need limited.

Core Idea
A male slave is not a mahram; he may see only the face and hands of his female owner – same as any non-mahram.

Classical Hanafi texts discuss the limits of a male slave's gaze upon his female owner. The Hanafi school maintains that a male slave is not a mahram and that his need to enter is limited, so he can see only the face and hands. This lesson examines the Hanafi position, the opposing view of Imam Malik and one view of Imam al-Shafi'i, and the textual and rational proofs on both sides.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi ruling: a male slave may see of his female owner only what any non-mahram man may see – the face and hands. He is not a mahram and has the capacity for marriage if freed, so desire exists.
2
Identify the opposing school and its proofs
Imam Malik and one view of Imam al-Shafi'i consider the male slave akin to a mahram, allowing greater visibility. Their proofs: (1) the slave frequently needs to enter without permission, and (2) the verse 'wa ma malakat aymanuhum' (Surah al-Nur, 24:31) which generally includes male slaves.
The slave is often admitted for domestic needs.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to each proof
Hanafi response to need: the need is qasirah (limited) because the slave works outside the home, so he does not need to see the owner's body. Response to the verse: early scholars (Sa'id b. Jubayr, Hasan al-Basri) interpreted 'ma malakat aymanuhum' in this verse as referring exclusively to female slaves, not male (i.e., 'your slave-girls'). Thus the verse does not grant male slaves permission to see beyond face and hands.
The Hanafi interpretation restricts the general (amm) to a specific (khass) based on context and early authority.
4
Determine the practical difference
The thamarah al-khilaf: under the Hanafi view, the male slave must cover his awrah from his female owner; she must also cover her awrah except face and hands before him. Under the opposing view, the slave is like a mahram, so the owner's awrah is less restrictive (like before a brother).
This affects daily interaction: e.g., the slave cannot travel with her alone.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الكراهية
کی وجہ سے اور اس لئے کہ حاجت متحقق ہے غلام کے داخل ہونے کی وجہ سے مالکہ پر بغیر اجازت کے۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ غلام ایسانہ ہے جو غیر محرم ہے اور نہ شوہر ہے اور شہوت متحقق ہے فی الجملہ نکاح کے جائز ہونے کی وجہ سے اور حاجت قاصر ہے اس لئے کہ غلام گھر سے باہر کام کرتا ہے اور مراد نص سے باندیاں ہیں فرمایا سعید اور حسن اور ان دونوں کے علاوہ نے کہ تم کو سورہ اور دھو کہ میں نہ ڈال دے اس لئے کہ وہ عورتوں کے سلسلہ میں ہے نہ کہ مردوں کے۔
تشریح غلام اپنی مالکہ کا صرف اتنا ہی بدن دیکھ سکتا ہے جتنا کہ دوسرا اجنبی مردو دیکھ سکتا ہے کیوں کہ رشتہ محرمیت نہیں بلکہ فی الجملہ غلام اس سے نکاح کی صلاحیت رکھتا ہے کہ وہ آزاد کر دے تو نکاح جائز ہو جائے گا اور شہوت بھی پوری ہے اور غلام ایسا نہ ہے جو نہ محرم ہے اور نہ شوہر اور یہاں ضرورت بھی نہیں کیونکہ غلام تو گھر سے باہر کے کام کاج کرتا ہے تو پھر دخول کی ضرورت نہیں ہے امام مالک فرماتے ہیں اور یہی امام شافعی کے دو قولوں میں سے ایک قول ہے کہ غلام محرم کے مثل ہے۔ جس پر انہوں نے دو دلیلیں پیش کی ہیں ایک تو یہ کہ یہاں ضرورت ہے کہ غلام بغیر اجازت کے مالکہ کے پاس جائے اور دوسری دلیل فرمان باری تعالیٰ و ما ملکت ایما نهن" جس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ فلاں فلان کے لئے زینت کا اظہار جائز ہے اور اپنے غلاموں کے لئے لہذا اس سے جواز معلوم ہوا۔ مصنف نے پہلی دلیل کا جواب دیا کہ حاجت قاصرہ ۔ ہے کیوں کہ غلام گھر سے بار ہر کام کرتا ہے اور آیت کا جواب یہ دیا کہ عورتیں اپنی باندیوں کے سامنے اپنی زینت کا اظہار کر سکتی ہیں نہ کہ غلاموں کے سامنے یعنی اگر چہ وما ملکت ایما نھن میں ما عام ہے جو غلام اور باندی دونوں کو شامل ہے مگر یہاں اس سے صرف باندیاں مراد ہیں جیسا کہ سعید بن جبیر اور حسن بصری وغیرہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ تم لوگ سورۃ نور کی اس آیت سے دھو کہ مت کھانا یعنی اس کو عام مت سمجھنا بلکہ یہ تو صرف عورتوں کے حق میں ہے نہ کہ مردوں کے یعنی صرف باندیاں مراد ہیں نہ کہ غلام یہ ہے مصنف کا ماحصل ۔
تنبیہ غلام اپنی مالکہ کا صرف چر اور ہاتھ دیکھ سکتاہے البتہ بغیر اس کی اجازت کے اس کے پاس جاسکتا ہے اور اس کے ساتھ سفر نہیں کرسکتا، در مختار علی ہامش ردالمختار ص ۲۳۶ ج ۵
Book of Disliked Acts. ... because of [need] and because need is verified due to the slave entering upon the female owner without permission. Our proof is that the slave is neither a non-mahram nor a husband, and desire is verified in general due to the permissibility of marriage, and the need is limited because the slave works outside the home. And the intent of the text is slave-girls – said Sa'id and Hasan and others: 'Do not be deceived by Surah [al-Nur] because it pertains to women, not men.' Clarification: The slave can only see of his female owner as much as any other strange man can see, because there is no mahram relationship; rather, the slave has the capacity for marriage if she frees him, and desire is complete. The slave is neither a mahram nor a husband, and there is no need because the slave works outside the home, so there is no need for entry. Imam Malik says (and this is one of two views of Imam al-Shafi'i) that the slave is like a mahram. They gave two proofs: (1) there is need for the slave to enter upon the owner without permission; (2) the verse 'and their slave-girls' indicates display of adornment is permissible before their slaves. The author answered the first proof: the need is limited because the slave works outside. And the answer to the verse: women may display their adornment before their slave-girls, not male slaves. Although 'ma' is general, here only slave-girls are meant, as Sa'id b. Jubayr and Hasan al-Basri said: do not be deceived by this verse of Surah al-Nur; it applies only to women, not men. Note: The slave may only see the face and hands of his female owner; he may enter upon her without permission but may not travel with her. (Durr al-Mukhtar with Radd al-Muhtar vol.5 p.236).
Source pages p. 349

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Karahiyah discusses the limits of a male slave's gaze upon his female owner. The Hanafi position is that a male slave is not a mahram and does not have the unrestricted access of a husband, so he can see only the face and hands, which is the same as any non-mahram man. The author presents the opposing view of Imam Malik and one view of Imam al-Shafi'i, who consider the slave like a mahram due to need and the verse 'wa ma malakat aymanuhum'. The Hanafi response argues that the need is limited since the slave works outside, and the verse is understood to refer specifically to female slaves, not male slaves, as interpreted by early authorities like Sa'id b. Jubayr and Hasan al-Basri. The note (tanbih) adds practical details: the slave may see only face and hands, may enter without permission, but cannot travel with her.

Key Terms
غلام (ghulam): Male slave owned by a woman.
مالکہ (malikah): Female owner of a male slave.
محرم (mahram): A person with whom marriage is permanently forbidden due to blood, marriage, or foster relationship.
شہوت (shahwah): Sexual desire; presence of desire is a factor in determining awrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, which parts of the female owner's body may a male slave see?
A) The entire body except the private parts.
B) Only the face and hands.
C) The same as a husband would see.
D) Nothing; he must always lower his gaze.

Key Takeaway
A male slave is not a mahram to his female owner; he may see only her face and hands, like any non-mahram.

Istibra' for a Purchased Slave-Girl: Ruling and Proof
Introduction to istibra' ruling with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on istibra' for a purchased slave-girl and explain its basis in the hadith of the captives of Awtas.

Core Idea
Istibra' (one menstrual wait) is wajib before intercourse with a purchased slave-girl to avoid lineage confusion.

Istibra' is a waiting period required for a purchased slave-girl to ensure she is not pregnant from her previous owner. This ruling protects lineage from mixing. In this lesson, we examine the ruling itself and its proof from the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Define Istibra'
Understand the term istibra' linguistically and legally: it means to seek purification, and in fiqh it refers to waiting for one menstrual period before intercourse with a purchased slave-girl.
The purpose is to verify that the womb is empty of the previous owner's child.
2
Identify the Hukm
Determine the ruling: istibra' is wajib (obligatory) upon the buyer, and mustahabb (recommended) upon the seller. The buyer must not have intercourse until one menses passes.
The prohibition extends to touching, kissing, and looking with desire.
3
Examine the Dalil
Locate the proof: the hadith of the captives of Awtas, where the Prophet (peace be upon him) prohibited intercourse with pregnant captives until delivery and with non-pregnant until one menses (istibra').
This is a sahih hadith, though ahad, it is accepted as evidence for obligation in Hanafi school.
4
Understand the Wisdom
Appreciate the legal cause: the prohibition prevents mixing of lineages (ikhtilat al-nasab) and avoids uncertain parentage.
This is a preventive measure (sadd al-dhara'i).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل فى الاستبراء وغيره
ترجمہ یہ فصل ہے استبراء اور اس کے غیر کے بیان میں
تشریح استبراء کے معنی صفائی طلب کرنا اور نبرات طلب کرنا اور مراد یہ ہے کہ ایک حیض سے صفائی کرے یعنی خریدی ہوئی باندی سے وطی نہ کرے جب تک کہ اس کو حیض نہ آجائے کیونکہ ہو سکتا ہے کہ اس کے رحم میں پہلے آقا کا نطفہ ہو جس سے پانیوں کا اختلاط لازم آئے گا اور انساب کا اختلاط لازم آئے گا اور حاملہ میں حقیقہ اختلاط ہوگا اور اور غیر حاملہ میں اختلاط کا تو ہم ہے۔ پھر استبرا کا حکم بائع کا بطریق استحباب ہے اور مشتری کو بطریق وجوب ہے جس کی وجوہات اور تفصیل آرہی ہے۔
وغیرہ سے مراد مصافحہ اور معانقہ اور بوسہ لینے کا احکام ہیں ۔
خریدی ہوئی باندی کا رحم جب تک صاف نہ ہو جائے وطی اور داعی وطی ممنوع ہیں
قال ومن اشترى جارية فانه لا يقربها ولا يلمسها ولا يقبلها ولا ينظر الى فرجها بشهوة حتى يستبرئها والاصل فيه قوله عليه السلام فى سبايا اوطاس الا لا تؤطا الحبالى حتى يضعن حملهن ولا الحيالى حتى يستبرئن بحيضة
ترجمہ فرمایا( محمد نے جامع صغیر میں ) اور جس نے کوئی باندی خریدی تو وہ اس سے وطی نہیں کرے گا اور نہ اس کو چھوئے گا اور نہ اس کا
Chapter on Istibra' and other matters. Translation: This chapter is about istibra' and other matters. Clarification: Istibra' means to seek purification, and the intent is to purify from one menstrual period; i.e., do not have intercourse with a purchased slave-girl until she has a menses, because it is possible that in her womb is the sperm of the previous owner, leading to mixing of fluids and confusion of lineage. For a pregnant one, actual mixing would occur; for a non-pregnant, mixing is feared. Then the ruling: istibra' is recommended for the seller and obligatory for the buyer; the reasons and details will follow. 'Other matters' refer to rulings on handshake, embrace, and kissing. The womb of a purchased slave-girl, until it is clean, intercourse and the call to intercourse are prohibited. He said: Whoever purchases a slave-girl, he shall not approach her, nor touch her, nor kiss her, nor look at her private part with desire until he makes istibra' of her. The basis for this is the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him) regarding the captives of Awtas: 'Beware! Do not have intercourse with pregnant women until they deliver, nor with non-pregnant until they have made istibra' with one menses.' Translation: Muhammad said (in al-Jami' al-Saghir): And whoever purchases a slave-girl, he shall not have intercourse with her, nor touch her, nor...
Source pages p. 350

Commentary
This passage introduces the chapter on istibra' (waiting period for a purchased slave-girl to confirm she is not pregnant). The ruling is that the buyer must wait for one menstrual period before having intercourse, touching, kissing, or looking with desire at the private part. This is based on a hadith from the captives of Awtas. The purpose is to avoid mixing lineages. The author notes that istibra' is recommended (mustahabb) for the seller but obligatory (wajib) for the buyer. The text also mentions that this section covers other topics like handshake, embrace, and kissing which will be discussed later. The ruling differentiates between a purchased slave-girl (must wait) and a free wife (no such waiting period).

Key Terms
استبراء (istibra'): Waiting for one menstrual period to ensure a purchased slave-girl is not pregnant from the previous owner.
جارية (jariyah): Female slave; slave-girl.
وطی (wati'): Sexual intercourse.
حیض (hayd): Menstruation; one full menstrual period is the standard for istibra'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One full lunar month.
B) One menstrual period.
C) Three menstrual periods.
D) Until she gives birth if pregnant.

Key Takeaway
One menstrual period of istibra' is obligatory for the buyer of a slave-girl to avoid mixing lineages.

Istibra' on the Buyer: Ruling and Proof from Hadith
Establishes istibra' obligation on buyer with hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on istibra' for the buyer, cite the hadith of 'Awtas, and identify the sabab (cause) of the obligation.

Core Idea
Istibra' is wajib on the buyer because the hadith forbids intercourse until one menses passes, and the cause is acquisition of ownership.

In this lesson, we examine the foundation of istibra' in the Hanafi school. Imam Muhammad states in al-Jami' al-Saghir that istibra' is obligatory on the buyer, not the seller. The proof is the Prophet's command at Ghazwa Hunain: do not have intercourse with captives until they have had one menses. From this, the school derives that the cause (sabab) of istibra' is the acquisition of ownership and possession (istihdath al-milk wa al-yad). Understanding the sabab is key to applying the ruling to all modes of acquisition, which we will explore in the next lesson.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
What is the ruling stated? Who is it obligatory upon and why not the seller?
Imam Muhammad's text directly says 'al-mushtari' (the buyer).
2
Locate the hadith proof
Find the hadith cited from Ghazwa Hunain. Note the exact wording: prohibition of intercourse until one menses for non-pregnant captives.
The hadith is from the battle of Hunain (Autas).
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith indicate obligation? The prohibition (la tuta') until a condition is fulfilled makes that condition necessary (wajib).
In Hanafi usul, al-amr yufidu al-wujub; here the prohibition implies the opposite, but the condition makes it obligatory.
4
Extract the sabab
What did the author identify as the cause (sabab) from the hadith? It is the acquisition of ownership and possession (istihdath al-milk wa al-yad).
The sabab is explicit in the text: the ruling is attached to the fact of ownership, not the hidden intention.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الكراهية
استبراء مشتری پر واجب ہے نہ کہ بائع پر
تشریح: یہ جامع صغیر میں امام محمد کا فرمان ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ جب تک خریدی ہوئی باندی کو ایک حیض نہ آئے جب تک اس سے وطی کرنے اور دوائی وطی سے احتراز کرے گا اور دلیل اس کی وہ حدیث ہے جو آنحضرت صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے غزوہ حنین میں ارشاد فرمائی ہے کہ جو عورتیں گرفتار کی گئی ہیں ان میں سے جو حاملہ ہیں ان سے وطی نہ کی جائے جب تک کہ بچہ نہ ہو جائے اور جو بے حمل ہیں ان سے وطی نہ کی جائے جب تک کہ ایک حیض نہ آجائے۔

افاد وجوب الاستبراء على المولى ودل على السبب في المسبية وهو استحداث الملك واليد لأنه هو الموجود في مورد النص وهذا لأن الحكمة فيه التعرف عن براءة الرحم صيانة المياه المحترمة عن الاختلاط والانساب عن الاشتباه وذلك عند حقيقة الشغل او توهم الشغل بماء محترم وهو ان يكون الولد ثابت النسب

تشریح: مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ اس حدیث سے دو باتیں معلوم ہوئیں۔
1- آقاء پر استبراء واجب ہے۔ ۲- گرفتار شدہ باندی میں وجوب استبراء کا سبب استحداث ملک ہے۔ لہذا یہ سبب جہاں ہوگا یہ حکم بھی وہاں ہوگا اور وجوب استبراء کی حکمت یہ ہے کہ رحم کا پانیوں کا اختلاط نہ ہو سکے اور انساب میں اشتباہ نہ ہو سکے اور محترم پانی سے مراد یہ ہے کہ وہ زنا کا پانی نہ بالفاظ دیگر جب بچہ ثابت النسب ہو گا اس وقت پانی کو محترم شمار کیا جائے گا۔
حمل کی صورت میں حقیقہ رحم کا دو پانیوں کے ساتھ اشتغال ہو گا اور حمل نہ ہونے کی صورت میں اشتغال کا تو ہم ہوگا۔
استبراء مشتری پر ہے نہ کہ بائع پر
ويجب على المشترى لاعلى البائع لان العلة الحقيقية ارادة الوطى والمشترى هو الذي يريده دون البائع فيجب عليه غيران الارادة امر مبطن فيدار الحكم على دليلها وهو التمكن من الوطى والتمكن انما يثبت بالملک والید فانتصب سببًا وادير الحكم عليه تيسيراً فكان السبب استحداث ملك الرقبة المؤكد باليد

تشریح: استبراء مشتری پر واجب ہے بائع پر نہیں اسلئے کہ وجوب استبراء کی علت وطی کا ارادہ ہے اور ولی کا ارادہ مشتری کا ہے نہ کہ بائع کا لہذا وجوب استبراء مشتری پر ہوا نہ کہ بائع پر لیکن ولی کا ارادہ ایک مخفی اور پوشیدہ چیز ہے تو حکم کا مدار ارادہ کی دلیل پر رہے گا اور ارادہ کی دلیل ولی پر قدرت ہے اور ملک اور قبضہ کے حاصل ہونے سے ولی پر قدرت ثابت ہوگی۔ لہذا ولی پر قدرت کو سبب قرار دے کر اسی پر مدار حکم رکھا جائے گا۔ جہاں جہاں استحداث ملک دید ہوگا وہاں وجوب استبراء کا حکم لاگو ہوگا
وتعدى الحكم الى سائر اسباب الملک کالشراء والهبة والوصية والميراث والخلع والكتابة وغير ذالك وكذا يجب على المشترى من مال الصبى ومن المرأة ومن المملوك وممن لا يحل له وطيها وكذا اذا كانت المشتراة بكرا لم تؤطا لتحقق السبب وادارة الاحكام على الاسباب دون الحكم لبطونها فيعتبر تحقق السبب عند توهم الشغل
ترجمہ: اور حکم متعدی ہوگا تمام اسباب ملک کی جانب جیسے شراء اور ہبہ اور وصیت اور میراث اور ضلع اور کتابت اور اس کے علاوہ اور ایسے ہی استبراء واجب ہے اس شخص پر جو خریدنے والا ہے بچہ کے مال سے، اور عورت سے اور مملوک سے اور اس شخص سے کہ اس کیلئے اس سے ولی کرنا حلال نہیں ہے اور ایسے جبکہ خریدی ہوئی باندی باکرہ ہو وطی نہیں کی جائے گی۔ سبب کے متحقق ہونے کی وجہ سے اور احکام کو گھمانا اسباب پر ہے نہ کہ حکمتوں پر حکمتوں کے پوشیدہ ہونے کی وجہ سے تو اعتبار کیا جائے گا سبب کے متحقق ہونے کا شغل کے توہم کے وقت۔
تشریح: جب ماقبل میں موردنص کے اندر سبب وجوب استبراء استحداث ملک وید ثابت ہو چکا ہے تو یہ سبب جہاں جہاں بھی پایا جائے گا وہاں پر وجوب استبراء کا حکم ہوگا۔ لہذا خرید اور ہبہ اور وصیت اور میراث اور ضلع اور کتابت اور صدقہ سب میں یہی حکم ہوگا۔ خلع کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ عورت نے شوہر کو ضلع میں اپنی باندی دی تو شوہر پر استبراء واجب ہے۔ کتابت کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ مولیٰ نے اپنے غلام سے کہہ دیا ہو کہ ایک باندی خرید کر مجھے دے دو تو میں تجھے آزاد کر دوں گا تو مولیٰ پر استبراء واجب ہے۔
Book of Disliked Acts. Istibra' is obligatory on the buyer, not on the seller. Explanation: This is the statement of Imam Muhammad in al-Jami' al-Saghir. Its summary is that as long as the purchased slave-girl does not have one menses, one should refrain from intercourse and from what leads to intercourse. The proof for it is the hadith that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said in the Ghazwa of Hunain: 'Do not have intercourse with the captured women who are pregnant until they give birth, and with those who are not pregnant until they have one menses.' Note: Jamali is the plural of jaliya meaning pregnant; hiyali is the plural of ha'il, the women who are not pregnant. Autas is a place three stages from Mecca where the famous battle known as Ghazwa Hunain took place. Istibra' is obligatory on the master, and the cause of obligation of istibra' for the captive slave-girl is the acquisition of ownership. The hadith indicates the obligation of istibra' on the master and indicates the cause in the captive (slave-girl) which is the acquisition of ownership and possession, because that is what is present in the text. This is because the wisdom in it is to know the purity of the womb, to protect the respected fluids from mixing and lineages from confusion, at the time of actual occupation or suspicion of occupation by a respected fluid, which is that the child is of confirmed lineage. Translation: This hadith gave the benefit of the obligation of istibra' on the master and guided to the cause which is in the captive (slave-girl) - that cause is the acquisition of ownership and possession. Because this (acquisition) is present in the text of the hadith, and this (obligation of istibra') is because the wisdom in it is to recognize the purity of the womb, for the purpose of protecting the fluids from mixing and protecting lineages from confusion. And this protection is when there is actual occupation or suspicion of occupation with a respected fluid, and that (respected fluid) is that the child is of confirmed lineage. Explanation: The author says that two things are known from this hadith: 1) Istibra' is obligatory on the master. 2) The cause of obligation of istibra' in the captive slave-girl is the acquisition of ownership. Therefore, wherever this cause exists, this ruling will also be there. And the wisdom of the obligation of istibra' is that the fluids in the womb should not mix and lineages should not be confused. And by 'respected fluid' is meant that it is not the fluid of adultery; in other words, when the child is of confirmed lineage, then the fluid is considered respected. In the case of pregnancy, there is actual occupation of the womb with two fluids, and in the case of no pregnancy, there is suspicion of occupation. Istibra' is for the buyer, not for the seller. And it is obligatory on the buyer, not on the seller, because the real cause is the intention to have intercourse, and the buyer is the one who intends it, not the seller. So it is obligatory on him. However, intention is a hidden matter, so the ruling is attached to its evidence, which is the ability to have intercourse. And ability is established by ownership and possession. So this was set up as a cause and the ruling was attached to it for ease. So the cause is the acquisition of ownership of the slave-girl confirmed by possession. Translation: Istibra' is obligatory on the buyer, not on the seller, because the real cause is the intention to have intercourse, and the buyer is the one who intends intercourse, not the seller. So it is obligatory on the buyer. Apart from this, intention is a hidden matter, so the ruling depends on the evidence of intention, and that is power over intercourse. And power is established by ownership and possession. So this became established as a cause, and for convenience, the ruling is attached to this ability. So the cause is the acquisition of ownership of the slave-girl confirmed by possession. Explanation: Istibra' is obligatory on the buyer, not on the seller, because the cause of obligation of istibra' is the intention to have intercourse, and the intention of the buyer is that of the buyer, not of the seller. Therefore, the obligation is on the buyer, not on the seller. But the intention is a hidden and concealed thing, so the ruling depends on the evidence of intention, and the evidence of intention is power over intercourse. And power over intercourse is proven by obtaining ownership and possession. Therefore, power over intercourse is made the cause, and the ruling is based on it. Wherever acquisition of ownership appears, there the ruling of obligation of istibra' will be applied. The ruling extends to all other causes of ownership such as purchase, gift, bequest, inheritance, khul', kitaba, and others. Similarly, istibra' is obligatory on the buyer from the property of a child, from a woman, from a slave, and from someone with whom it is not permissible for him to have intercourse. Similarly, if the purchased slave-girl is a virgin who has not been intercourse with, due to the realization of the cause. And the ruling revolves around causes, not wisdoms, because wisdoms are hidden. So consideration is given to the realization of the cause at the time of suspicion of occupation. Explanation: When in the preceding text, the cause of obligation of istibra' was established as acquisition of ownership and possession in the text of the hadith, then wherever this cause is found, the ruling of obligation of istibra' will be there. Therefore, in purchase, gift, bequest, inheritance, khul', kitaba, and sadaqa, the same ruling applies. The meaning of khul' is that a woman gave her slave-girl to her husband in khul', so istibra' is obligatory on the husband. The meaning of kitaba is that the master told his slave: 'Buy a slave-girl and give her to me, and I will free you', so istibra' is obligatory on the master.
Source pages p. 351

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah is a commentary on the Hidayah, dealing with the ruling of istibra' (waiting period for a newly acquired female slave to ensure her womb is empty). The passage type is a 'ruling with proof' followed by extension (qiyas). The author begins by stating the ruling: Istibra' is obligatory on the buyer, not on the seller. He then provides the proof from the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) regarding the captives of Hunain, where he forbade intercourse with pregnant captives until delivery and with non-pregnant ones until one menses. This hadith establishes the obligation of istibra' on the master (owner) and indicates that the cause (sabab) for this obligation is the acquisition of ownership and possession (istihdath al-milk wa al-yad). The wisdom (hikmah) behind istibra' is to avoid mixing of fluids (waters) in the womb and confusion of lineages. The respected fluid (ma' muharam) refers to semen that could result in a child of confirmed lineage; the fluid of adultery is not respected. The passage explains that the ruling is attached to the cause (ownership) rather than the hidden intention of intercourse, because ownership is tangible. Therefore, istibra' is required in all modes of acquiring ownership of a slave-girl: purchase, gift, bequest, inheritance, khul' (wife giving slave to husband as compensation), kitaba (master contracting with slave to buy a slave-girl), and even when the seller is legally unable to have intercourse (e.g., a minor, a woman, a relative within prohibited degrees). The ruling also applies even if the slave-girl is a virgin who has never been intercourse with, because the cause (ownership) is present. The passage emphasizes that the ruling revolves around the cause (sabab) and not the hidden wisdoms (hikam), for ease in application.

Key Terms
استبراء (istibra'): The waiting period observed for a newly acquired female slave to ensure her womb is empty of pregnancy before intercourse.
استحداث الملک (istihdath al-milk): The acquisition of ownership of a slave-girl for the first time, which is the cause (sabab) for the obligation of istibra'.
سبب (sabab): The effective cause (legal cause) that triggers a ruling. Here, istihdath al-milk is the sabab for istibra'.
حکمت (hikmah): The wisdom or underlying reason behind the ruling, which is to avoid mixing of lineages and fluids.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the sabab (cause) of istibra' according to the hadith interpretation in this passage?
A) The intention to have intercourse
B) The acquisition of ownership and possession (istihdath al-milk wa al-yad)
C) The pregnancy of the slave-girl
D) The act of purchase itself

Key Takeaway
Istibra' is wajib on the buyer because the hadith makes it a condition for permissible intercourse, and the cause is the acquisition of ownership.

The Extension of Istibra' to All Acquisitions
Extension of istibra' to all acquisitions via qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qiyas to extend istibra' to all modes of acquiring a slave-girl and explain why the ruling is on the buyer, not the seller.

Core Idea
Istibra' extends to any acquisition of ownership (istihdath al-milk), not just purchase, because the cause is the ability to have intercourse.

Having established the sabab as istihdath al-milk wa al-yad, the author now extends the ruling to all forms of acquisition: purchase, gift, inheritance, khul', and even kitaba. The passage also clarifies why the seller is exempt: the seller no longer has the intention or ability to have intercourse. This lesson focuses on the qiyas (analogical reasoning) that generalizes the ruling, showing how the Hanafi school systematically applies a cause-based approach.

Guided Path
1
Identify the asl (original case)
What is the original case for which the ruling was revealed? It is the captive slave-girl in war, where the Prophet forbade intercourse until istibra'.
The asl is the captive (mashriyyah).
2
Extract the illa (effective cause)
What is the common cause that justifies extending the ruling? The illa is istihdath al-milk wa al-yad (acquisition of ownership and possession).
This is explicitly stated as the sabab.
3
Identify the far' (new cases)
List the new cases to which the ruling is extended: purchase, gift, bequest, inheritance, khul', kitaba, and even when the seller cannot have intercourse (e.g., woman, minor).
The passage enumerates these.
4
Apply the ruling to the far'
For each new case, the ruling is the same: istibra' is wajib before intercourse.
The ruling is attached to the cause, not the specific scenario.

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah is a commentary on the Hidayah, dealing with the ruling of istibra' (waiting period for a newly acquired female slave to ensure her womb is empty). The passage type is a 'ruling with proof' followed by extension (qiyas). The author begins by stating the ruling: Istibra' is obligatory on the buyer, not on the seller. He then provides the proof from the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) regarding the captives of Hunain, where he forbade intercourse with pregnant captives until delivery and with non-pregnant ones until one menses. This hadith establishes the obligation of istibra' on the master (owner) and indicates that the cause (sabab) for this obligation is the acquisition of ownership and possession (istihdath al-milk wa al-yad). The wisdom (hikmah) behind istibra' is to avoid mixing of fluids (waters) in the womb and confusion of lineages. The respected fluid (ma' muharam) refers to semen that could result in a child of confirmed lineage; the fluid of adultery is not respected. The passage explains that the ruling is attached to the cause (ownership) rather than the hidden intention of intercourse, because ownership is tangible. Therefore, istibra' is required in all modes of acquiring ownership of a slave-girl: purchase, gift, bequest, inheritance, khul' (wife giving slave to husband as compensation), kitaba (master contracting with slave to buy a slave-girl), and even when the seller is legally unable to have intercourse (e.g., a minor, a woman, a relative within prohibited degrees). The ruling also applies even if the slave-girl is a virgin who has never been intercourse with, because the cause (ownership) is present. The passage emphasizes that the ruling revolves around the cause (sabab) and not the hidden wisdoms (hikam), for ease in application.

Key Terms
استبراء (istibra'): The waiting period observed for a newly acquired female slave to ensure her womb is empty of pregnancy before intercourse.
علت (illa): The effective cause in qiyas. Here, the illa is istihdath al-milk wa al-yad.
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning extending a ruling from an original case (asl) to a new case (far') based on a shared cause (illa).
سبب (sabab): The legal cause that triggers a ruling. Here, istihdath al-milk is the sabab for istibra'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
To which of the following does the ruling of istibra' NOT apply according to this passage?
A) Purchase (shira')
B) Gift (hiba)
C) Bequest (wasiyya)
D) The seller after the sale

Key Takeaway
The ruling of istibra' applies to any acquisition of ownership (istihdath al-milk), not just purchase, and it is always on the new owner, not the previous one.

The Prohibition of Dawa'i al-Wat' Before Istibra'
Explains prohibition of actions leading to intercourse for buyer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on dawa'i al-wat' for a buyer before istibra' and explain why the ruling differs for a menstruating woman.

Core Idea
Dawa'i al-wat' are haram for the buyer before istibra' due to sadd al-dhara'i' and property risk; not so for menstruation.

This lesson examines a nuanced ruling in Hanafi fiqh: although istibra' makes intercourse haram, actions leading to it (dawa'i) are also haram for the buyer, but not for a menstruating woman. The distinction reveals the interplay of principle and context.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what 'dawa'i al-wat'' refers to and what the hukm is for the buyer before istibra'. Note that the ruling is haram.
Dawa'i include kissing, touching with desire, etc.
2
Analyze the proof (istihsan)
The reasoning is based on istihsan: actions that lead to haram are themselves haram (sadd al-dhara'i'), and there is a specific risk of pregnancy belonging to the seller, which could invalidate the sale.
The textual proof is not a direct text but a derived principle.
3
Understand the exception
Contrast with a menstruating woman: although intercourse is haram, dawa'i are not haram because there is no property risk (same owner) and aversion naturally prevents intercourse.
The exception shows that the ruling is not purely based on the prohibition of intercourse.
4
Apply the contrast
Use the contrast to reinforce the rationale: the prohibition for the buyer is due to both the general principle and the specific property concern, which are absent in menstruation.
This highlights the importance of contextual factors in Hanafi rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الكراهية
على اعتبار ظهور الحبل ودعوة البائع
ترجمہ اور جبکہ استبراء کا وجوب ثابت ہو گیا اور وطی حرام ہو گئی تو دوائی وطی حرام ہوں گے دوائی کے پہنچانے کی وجہ سے وطی کی جانب یا دوائی کے وقوع کے احتمال کی وجہ سے غیر ملک میں ظہور حمل کے اعتبار پر اور بائع کے دعوی کے اعتبار پر۔
تشریح صور مذکورہ میں مولی پر استبراء واجب ہے اور ولی حرام ہے لہذا دوائی ولی بھی حرام ہوں گے اسلئے دواعی وطی مفضی الی الولی ہیں۔ نیز احتمال ہے کہ دوائی وطی کا وقوع غیر کی ملک میں ہو جائے اس طریقہ پر کہ باندی کو حمل ظاہر ہو جائے اور بائع اس کے حمل کے بارے میں دعوی کر دے کہ میرا ہے تو یہ باندی بائع کی ام ولد ہوگی جس کی بیع جائز نہیں تو بیع نسخ ہو جائے گی تو معلوم ہوا کہ جو دوائی وطی معرض ظہور میں آئے تھے وہ غیر کی ملک میں واقع ہوئے تھے اس وجہ سے یہاں ولی کے ساتھ ساتھ دوائی ولی سے بھی منع کیا جائے گا۔ حائضہ سے دوائی ولی حرام نہیں
بخلاف الحائض حيث لاتحرم الدواعى فيها لانه لا تحتمل الوقوع فى غير الملک ولانه زمان نفرة الاطلاق في الدواعي لا يفضى الى الوطى والرغبة فى المشتراة قبل الدخول اصدق الرغبات فتفضى اليه ترجمہ بخلاف حائضہ کے اس حیثیت سے کہ حیض میں دوائی ولی حرام نہیں ہیں اسلئے کہ غیر کی ملک میں وقوع کا احتمال نہیں ہے اور اسلئے کہ یہ نفرت کا زمانہ ہے تو دوائی کی اباحت مفضی الی الولی نہیں ہے اور خریدی ہوئی باندی میں دخول سے پہلے کچی رغبت ہے تو دوائی لی کی جانب مفضی ہوں گے۔
تشریح یہاں ایک سوال پیدا ہوتا تھا کہ جب ولی کے حرام ہونے کی وجہ سے دوائی وطی حرام ہیں تو حالت حیض میں بیوی سے وطی کرنا تو حرام ہے لیکن دوائی ولی حرام نہیں ہیں تو اس کا جواب دیا کہ یہاں دوائی میں یہ احتمال نہیں ہے کہ وہ غیر کی ملک میں واقع ہو جائیں بخلاف اول کے (کمامر ) نیز حالت حیض نفرت کا زمانہ ہے تو یہاں دوعی کی اباحت مفضی الی الوطی نہیں ہے۔ بخلاف مشتراة کے کہ اس میں دخول سے پہلے رغبت صادقہ ہے تو اس میں دواعی کی اباحت مفضی الی الوہی ہوگی۔
Book of Karahiya. Based on the appearance of pregnancy and the seller's claim. Translation: When istibra' becomes obligatory and intercourse becomes haram, then the inducements to intercourse (dawa'i al-wat') are also haram, because they lead to intercourse or because of the possibility of their occurrence in the property of another, based on the appearance of pregnancy and the seller's claim. Explanation: In the mentioned situation, istibra' is wajib upon the master and intercourse is haram, therefore the dawa'i are also haram because they lead to intercourse. Also there is a possibility that intercourse could occur in the property of another, such that if pregnancy appears in the slave-girl and the seller claims it is his, then she becomes his umm walad, whose sale is not permissible, so the sale would be rescinded. Thus, the dawa'i that appeared were in the context of occurring in another's property, so here along with intercourse, the dawa'i are also prohibited. As for a menstruating woman, the dawa'i are not haram. Contrary to the menstruating woman: the dawa'i are not prohibited in her case because there is no possibility of occurrence in the property of another, and because it is a time of aversion, so the permissibility of dawa'i does not lead to intercourse; and the desire for a purchased slave-girl before entry is a strong desire, so it leads to intercourse. Translation: Contrary to the menstruating woman, in the sense that during menstruation the dawa'i are not haram because there is no possibility of occurrence in the property of another, and because it is a time of aversion, so the permissibility of dawa'i does not lead to intercourse, and in the purchased slave-girl before entry there is a strong desire, so the dawa'i lead to it. Explanation: A question arises: Since intercourse is haram due to being haram, why are dawa'i not haram during menstruation? The answer is that here there is no possibility that they will occur in another's property, contrary to the first case. Also, menstruation is a time of aversion, so permissibility of dawa'i does not lead to intercourse. Contrary to the purchased slave-girl, where before entry there is genuine desire, so permissibility of dawa'i leads to intercourse.
Source pages p. 356

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof explaining why actions that lead to intercourse (dawa'i al-wat') are haram for the buyer of a slave-girl before completing istibra'. The Hanafi position is that since istibra' is wajib and intercourse is haram during this period, any action that typically leads to intercourse (like kissing, touching with desire) is also haram. This is based on the principle that what leads to haram is itself haram (sadd al-dhara'i'). Additionally, there is the specific concern that if pregnancy occurs and the seller claims it, the slave-girl becomes an umm walad and the sale is invalidated. Thus, even the possibility of pregnancy being in another's ownership makes dawa'i haram. The exception is a menstruating woman (wife or slave): although intercourse is haram during menstruation, dawa'i are not haram because there is no risk of pregnancy belonging to another owner (since she is owned by the husband or the same master), and the time of menstruation is one of natural aversion, so permissibility does not inevitably lead to intercourse. This contrast highlights that the prohibition for the purchased slave-girl is due both to the general principle of sadd al-dhara'i' and the specific property concern.

Key Terms
دواعي الوطء (dawa'i al-wat'): Actions that typically lead to sexual intercourse, such as kissing, touching, and foreplay.
استبراء (istibra'): A period of waiting (one menstrual cycle or one month) to confirm that a slave-girl is not pregnant from a previous owner before her new master can have intercourse with her.
أم ولد (umm walad): A slave-girl who bears a child to her master, thereby becoming free upon her master's death and cannot be sold.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why are dawa'i al-wat' haram for the buyer of a slave-girl before istibra', but not haram for a menstruating wife?
A) Because intercourse is haram in both cases, so the rule must be the same.
B) Because in the slave-girl case there is a risk of pregnancy belonging to the seller, and desire is strong; in menstruation there is no such risk and aversion is present.
C) Because the buyer is a stranger to the slave-girl, while the husband has a permanent relationship.
D) Because istibra' is a form of fasting that prohibits all physical contact.

Key Takeaway
The prohibition of dawa'i al-wat' before istibra' is not merely because intercourse is haram, but due to the risk of property confusion and the strength of desire.
